- **Datasets:** GigaEdit-S (250h editing data from GigaSpeech-S) for SFT; 625h LibriTTS/LibriTTS-R + YODAS2 for BigVGAN; 3,000 GigaSpeech-XL utterances for GRPO. Eval: Ming-Freeform-Audio-Edit (editing), CV3-EVAL (multilingual zero-shot TTS).
- **Code:** https://cjy1018.github.io/CosyEdit2 (demo page; no code repo found)
- **Recipe:** Stage 1 SFT: LLM 8 epochs lr 1e-6 grad-accum 8; flow 9 epochs lr 3e-5; BigVGAN on 625h mix. Stage 2 GRPO: build editing prompts from 3,000 GigaSpeech-XL utterances via nlpaug rule-based perturbations (no target audio); 380 steps, G=4 rollouts/prompt, lr 3e-6, batch 64. Rewards: r_wer=exp(-k_w*w^alpha) with k_w=12, alpha=1.5; r_sim = speaker-embedding cosine (>=0); r_mcd=exp(-k_m*max(m-delta,0)) with k_m=0.2, delta=2 on unedited regions; combine r = lambda_c*r_wer-mcd + lambda_s*r_sim with dynamic schedule 0.9/0.1 -> 0.8/0.2.
- **Key results:** Editing WER (Ming-Freeform-Audio-Edit, EN): substitution 1.43 (SSR-Speech 1.90, VoiceCraft-X 7.29), insertion 1.90, deletion 5.52. Zero-shot TTS (CV3-EVAL) beats CosyVoice2: ZH 3.52% vs 3.77% CER, EN 4.87% vs 5.45% WER, JA 6.16% vs 7.76% CER, KO 5.14% vs 6.89% WER.
- **Notes:** Central claim: editing-oriented GRPO improves both editing and general zero-shot TTS, revealing a link between editing and synthesis. No code repo; demo only.

### 6. Emo-LiPO: Listwise Preference Optimization for Fine-Grained Emotion Intensity Control in LLM-based Text-to-Speech

_Lin et al. (Chinese University of Hong Kong, Shenzhen; National University of Singapore) · 2026 · arXiv preprint (June 2026)_

- **Categories:** C3, C4, C6, C7, C2
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.13006) · arXiv:2606.13006 · [code](https://github.com/hlt-cuhksz/Emo-LiPO)
- **Synthetic-data role:** ESD-plus is a fully synthetic emotional-intensity dataset: 45,500 samples (~36.89 h) generated by gpt-4o-mini-tts using 10 official voices (4 male, 6 female) over 350 parallel ESD sentences, spanning 4 non-neutral emotions x 3 intensity levels plus neutral (13 fine-grained labels). 91.23% of dev/test passed human verification for monotonic intensity ordering. Preference lists are synthetically constructed per prompt: K+2 candidates = target, K-1 same-emotion different-intensity samples, one neutral, one cross-emotion negative, ranked by intensity distance with index-based preference scores psi(i)=1-(i-1)/(K+2).
- **Method:** Casts fine-grained emotion-intensity control in LLM-based TTS as a learning-to-rank problem and applies listwise preference optimization (LiPO) to align prompt-conditioned speech generation with relative emotion intensity expressed in text, explicitly modeling global intensity ordering within each emotion under fixed transcripts to bridge the semantic-acoustic gap.
- **Architecture:** Backbone: CosyVoice-300M-Instruct (LLM-based TTS). Training: supervised fine-tuning followed by LiPO optimization. Listwise ranking loss with distance-aware weighting lambda_ij derived from gain and discount functions (learning-to-rank style).
- **Base models:** CosyVoice-300M-Instruct; gpt-4o-mini-tts used as the data-generation engine for ESD-plus.
- **Datasets:** Real: ESD (Emotional Speech Database) English subset (350 parallel sentences). Synthetic: ESD-plus (45,500 samples, ~37 h; train/dev/test split 300/20/30 utterances).
- **Code:** https://github.com/hlt-cuhksz/Emo-LiPO ; dataset: https://huggingface.co/datasets/hlt-cuhksz/ESD-plus
- **Recipe:** 1) Build ESD-plus: generate emotional speech with gpt-4o-mini-tts across 10 voices and 350 ESD sentences, 4 non-neutral emotions x 3 intensities + neutral (13 labels), human-verify monotonic intensity ordering. 2) Supervised fine-tune CosyVoice-300M-Instruct. 3) Construct listwise preference lists per prompt (K+2 candidates: target, K-1 same-emotion varying-intensity, 1 neutral, 1 cross-emotion negative) ranked by intensity distance with preference scores psi(i)=1-(i-1)/(K+2). 4) Optimize with listwise ranking loss using distance-aware weights lambda_ij from gain/discount functions.
- **Key results:** On ESD-plus, Recall-ft 39.54 and WER 4.26 for Emo-LiPO vs CosyVoice (Recall-ft 29.90, WER 4.47) and Emo-DPO (I) (Recall-ft 37.21, WER 6.79). Quality metrics: NISQA, DNSMOS, UTMOS; emotion metrics: EmoSIM, Recall, Recall-ft. Human Arena win rates 86-94% across speech quality, emotion expression, and intensity control. Beats supervised and DPO-based LLM-TTS baselines.
- **Notes:** ESD-plus is fully LLM-TTS-generated speech (corpus generated synthetically) and supports multi-speaker/multi-voice emotion intensity (category 6). Code and dataset publicly released. Preference data is auto-constructed for listwise RL-style alignment (category 3).

### 7. Fish Audio S2 Technical Report

_Fish Audio team · 2026 · arXiv preprint (Fish Audio)_

- **Categories:** C3, C4, C5, C6, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.08823) · arXiv:2603.08823 · [code](https://github.com/fishaudio/fish-speech)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Heavy use of machine-generated annotations and pseudo-labels. A rich-transcription ASR model jointly transcribes content and auto-annotates speaker turns and vocal events as natural-language instruction tags ([laugh],[whisper],[angry], etc.); video sources are pseudo-labeled (video captioning + speech captioning + voice-quality assessment) then human-verified. RL post-training (GRPO variant) optimizes on the model's own generated speech scored by multi-dimensional reward models (ASR confidence for semantics, a speech-quality model for acoustics, voiceprint similarity for timbre). Optional LLM instruction-rewriting at inference further boosts Turing-test scores.
- **Method:** Open multi-speaker, multi-turn, instruction-following TTS. Keeps S1's decoder-only Transformer + RVQ codec but adds a Dual-Autoregressive (Slow AR over time / Fast AR over residual codebooks) design, a staged data pipeline built on rich-transcription pseudo-labeling and voice-quality assessment, and RL-based reward post-training, plus a production SGLang streaming engine.
- **Architecture:** Dual-AR: Slow AR = Qwen3-4B backbone over semantic/time-axis tokens; Fast AR = 4 Transformer layers (~400M) generating the remaining 9 residual acoustic codebooks per timestep. Audio codec: 446M-param DAC-based RVQ tokenizer with causal convolutions, sliding-window Transformers, 2048x downsampling, EVA-GAN decoder at 44.1kHz. Decoder-only Transformer backbone inherited from S1.
- **Base models:** Built on Fish Audio S1 (decoder-only Transformer + RVQ codec). Slow AR backbone initialized from/uses Qwen3-4B. Reward models use external ASR, a speech-quality model, and voiceprint/speaker-verification features.
- **Datasets:** Pre-training on 10,000,000+ hours of raw audio across ~80 languages, pseudo-labeled (incl. video sources) then human-verified. Audio codec trained 1M steps. Context 8192 (stage1) -> 16384 (stage2). Eval on Seed-TTS-Eval, Minimax Multilingual Testset, an Audio Turing Test, EmergentTTS-Eval.
- **Code:** https://github.com/fishaudio/fish-speech ; HF: https://huggingface.co/fishaudio/s2-pro ; demo https://fish.audio
- **Recipe:** 1) Train 446M DAC-style RVQ codec with GAN losses (~1M steps, 44.1kHz, EVA-GAN decoder). 2) Pre-train Dual-AR on 10M+ hr pseudo-labeled multilingual data with rich-transcription instruction tags; context 8192. 3) Continue/extend context to 16384. 4) SFT on curated high-quality data. 5) RL post-training with a GRPO variant using multi-dim rewards (ASR-confidence semantic reward + speech-quality acoustic reward + voiceprint timbre reward). 6) Optional LLM instruction-rewriting at inference. Slow AR 4B + Fast AR 400M; SGLang streaming engine (RTF 0.195, TTFA<100ms on one H200).
- **Key results:** Seed-TTS-Eval WER 0.54% (zh), 0.99% (en). Leads speaker similarity on 17/24 languages (Minimax Multilingual Testset). Audio Turing Test posterior mean 0.483 (0.515 with instruction rewriting). EmergentTTS-Eval 81.88% win rate. Inference RTF 0.195, TTFA<100ms on a single H200.
- **Notes:** Open weights + fine-tuning code + production SGLang engine released. GRPO-style RL with three reward heads makes it a strong category-3 example. Pseudo-labeled video/speech corpus and instruction-tag annotation make it category 4/5/7. 44.1kHz high-fidelity codec.

### 8. FlexiVoice: Enabling Flexible Style Control in Zero-Shot TTS with Natural Language Instructions

_FlexiVoice authors (arXiv:2601.04656; OpenReview F7GmbfyVg9) · 2026 · arXiv preprint (under review, OpenReview)_

- **Categories:** C2, C3, C4, C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2601.04656) · arXiv:2601.04656 · [code](https://flexi-voice.github.io/)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Two synthetic-data uses. (1) Natural-language style instructions are LLM-generated: Deepseek-V3 produces style descriptions from speech metadata (video titles, tags, character names) for ~4,316 h, forming the FlexiVoice-Instruct dataset. (2) Preference data for DPO/GRPO is built from the model's own sampled generations scored by reward models (Emotion2vec, CAM++, Kimi-Audio), i.e., on-policy synthetic preference pairs; the preference tasks themselves come from existing emotion datasets (ESD, MEAD, CSEMOTIONS) rather than being synthesized.
- **Method:** A zero-shot TTS system where speaking style is set by a natural-language instruction and timbre by a reference clip; a Progressive Post-Training (PPT) scheme (DPO then multi-objective GRPO) progressively unlocks accurate, decoupled control over style instruction, reference timbre, and text content, resolving the style-timbre-content conflict.
- **Architecture:** LLM-core codec language model: an LLM takes text plus optional natural-language style instruction and optional reference speech, predicting speech codec tokens. Three frozen modules around the LLM: speech tokenizer, flow-matching decoder, and Vocos vocoder. Only the LLM core is trained during pre-training and post-training.
- **Base models:** LLM-core codec-LM (pre-trained on speech+instruction data); Vocos vocoder + flow-matching decoder (frozen). Reward models: Emotion2vec-Large (SER), CAM++ (speaker verification), Kimi-Audio-7B-Instruct (instruction-adherence judge).
- **Datasets:** Pre-training: Emilia (multilingual in-the-wild speech), FlexiVoice-Instruct (~4,316 h with Deepseek-V3 LLM-generated style annotations), ParaSpeechCaps, NVSpeech, plus emotion/debate corpora (EN+ZH). Post-training preference data: ESD, MEAD, CSEMOTIONS. Evaluation: InstructTTSEval and emotion instruction-following tasks.
- **Code:** https://flexi-voice.github.io/ (project/demo page; samples and reproducibility materials)
- **Recipe:** 1) Pre-train: tokenize ground-truth speech; train the LLM core on (text + style instruction + reference) -> speech-token pairs over Emilia + FlexiVoice-Instruct + caption/emotion corpora; generate instructions via Deepseek-V3 from metadata. 2) PPT Stage S1 (Multi-modality DPO): DPO on emotion templates with neutral references so the model follows instruction and reference simultaneously. 3) Stage S2 (Decoupling GRPO): multi-objective GRPO with deliberately conflicting scenarios (e.g., happy instruction vs sad reference); rewards = Emotion2vec-Large SER probability + CAM++ binary speaker verification. 4) Stage S3 (Instruction GRPO): GRPO on open-ended complex instructions with Kimi-Audio-7B-Instruct giving a binary yes/no instruction-adherence reward; mix in S2 data to avoid catastrophic forgetting. Build GRPO preference groups from on-policy samples; keep tokenizer/decoder/vocoder frozen throughout.
- **Key results:** 97.4% instruction-following accuracy on English emotion tasks (vs 72.4% for the pre-trained base model); 89.4% on complex multi-modality (style+timbre conflict) tasks. On InstructTTSEval: 79.3% average (English), 70.8% (Chinese), competitive with Gemini-pro and exceeding all open-source baselines; human evaluations confirm naturalness, controllability, robustness.
- **Notes:** 2026 preprint under OpenReview. Combines LLM-generated text/instructions (cat 4), preference RL (cat 3, DPO+GRPO), and instruction/style+timbre control (cat 6). Reward models are off-the-shelf; only the LLM core is trainable.

### 9. GSRM: Generative Speech Reward Model for Speech RLHF

_Includes N. Kanda et al. (full author list not confirmed from abstract page) · 2026 · arXiv preprint_

- **Categories:** C3, C4, C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2602.13891) · arXiv:2602.13891
- **Synthetic-data role:** Two roles. (1) The reward model's training corpus is built largely on synthesized speech: the ConvTTS training set (4,579 conversational TTS audio samples) plus an out-of-domain benchmark of real-world user-assistant speech interactions, annotated with 31k expert naturalness ratings. (2) GPT-4o is used as a teacher to synthesize the chain-of-thought reasoning traces (pseudo-labels) that ground the model's feature-based judgments during SFT. The trained GSRM then acts as a verifier providing reward signals for online RLHF of speech LLMs, so it indirectly shapes generation of synthetic speech downstream.
- **Method:** A reasoning-centric generative reward model for speech naturalness. Instead of regressing audio to a scalar, GSRM decomposes evaluation into interpretable acoustic feature extraction (vowel-level prosody: pitch, intensity, duration via forced phoneme alignment) followed by feature-grounded chain-of-thought reasoning that yields an explainable rating. Serves as a verifier for online RLHF to improve speech LLM naturalness.
- **Architecture:** Multimodal LLM backbone Qwen2.5-Omni-7B (7B params). Pipeline: (1) acoustic feature extraction stage (forced alignment + vowel-level prosody, discretized to ordinal categories), (2) evidence-log CoT reasoning, (3) interpretable rating prediction. Trained with the SWIFT framework.
- **Base models:** Qwen2.5-Omni-7B as the backbone; GPT-4o as teacher for synthesizing reasoning traces during data preparation.
- **Datasets:** Curated human-feedback dataset of 31k expert ratings; ConvTTS training set of 4,579 conversational TTS audio samples; out-of-domain benchmark of real-world user-assistant speech interactions.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Preprocess audio with forced phoneme alignment; extract vowel-level prosody (pitch, intensity, duration) and discretize to ordinal categories. 2) Use GPT-4o to synthesize feature-grounded CoT reasoning traces. 3) SFT Qwen2.5-Omni-7B with SWIFT: LR 2e-5, cosine scheduler, batch size 32, max seq len 4096, up to 10 epochs. 4) Inference: 16 random sampling passes per sample (temperature 1.0, top-p 0.6), average scores. 5) Deploy as verifier for online RLHF of speech LLMs. Note: authors observe RL alone underperforms without SFT knowledge injection first.
- **Key results:** In-domain naturalness Pearson correlation 0.889 (approaching human inter-rater consistency); out-of-domain Pearson 0.465. Sub-metrics intonation and pacing correlate most strongly with human-likeness. Substantially outperforms existing scalar speech naturalness predictors; improves naturalness of speech LLM generations when used as an online RLHF verifier.
- **Notes:** arXiv ID format 2602.xxxxx corresponds to Feb 2026 submission. Code release status unspecified. Full author list not fully confirmed from the abstract page (search surfaced Kanda N. among authors).

### 10. Improving Code-Switching Speech Recognition with TTS Data Augmentation

_Yue Heng Yeo et al. (6 authors) · 2026 · arXiv preprint_

- **Categories:** C2, C5, C6, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2601.00935) · arXiv:2601.00935
- **Synthetic-data role:** Synthetic Chinese-English code-switching speech is generated by a CosyVoice2 TTS model fine-tuned on the SEAME corpus. Each SEAME transcript is re-synthesized multiple times with different x-vector speaker embeddings (random speakers) to produce 100h to 500h of synthetic conversational code-switching audio, which augments (or partly replaces) real labeled speech for training a code-switching ASR system. Optimal volume found at 200-300h (~2-3x real data).
- **Method:** Fine-tune a multilingual zero-shot TTS model (CosyVoice2) on a small code-switching corpus, then synthesize large amounts of code-switching speech with diverse speaker embeddings to augment ASR training data and reduce mixed error rate.
- **Architecture:** TTS: CosyVoice2 = QwenLM (0.5B) autoregressive speech-token LM + supervised speech tokenizer + flow-matching decoder + vocoder (only the 0.5B QwenLM is updated; tokenizer/flow/vocoder frozen). ASR: Whisper-small (~240M) for ablations, Whisper-Large-v3 for main results, trained in ESPnet.
- **Base models:** CosyVoice2 (pretrained on ~200k h Chinese-English for tokenizer, 167k h across four languages); Whisper-small and Whisper-Large-v3 for ASR.
- **Datasets:** Real: SEAME (~192h, 156 speakers, Mandarin-English code-switching; ~100h used for TTS fine-tuning, tests 10h-100h), test sets DevMan and DevSGE; ASCEND (9h, 38 speakers, HK Chinese-English) for cross-domain. Synthetic: 100h-500h CosyVoice2-generated code-switching speech.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Fine-tune CosyVoice2 QwenLM (0.5B) on SEAME text->speech-token pairs: Adam, lr 1e-4, linear warmup 10k updates then constant, 200 epochs; only QwenLM updated, rest frozen. 2) Re-synthesize each SEAME transcript several times using different x-vector speaker embeddings to build 200-300h synthetic code-switching speech (UTMOS ~3.2 vs GT 3.6). 3) Train ASR (Whisper-small/Large-v3 in ESPnet) on GT + synthetic: 80-bin log-Mel @24kHz (20ms win, 12ms hop), SpecAugment (2 freq masks <=40 bins, 5 time masks <=12%, 5-frame time-warp); AdamW (b=0.9/0.99, eps 1e-6, wd 0.01), linear warmup 0->1e-5 over 1500 updates, inverse-sqrt decay, ~12M-element minibatches with 4-step grad accumulation, auto language ID. No explicit synthetic-data filtering described.
- **Key results:** Whisper-Large-v3 MER: GT-only 12.1% (DevMan)/17.8% (DevSGE) -> GT + 100h TTS (random speakers) 10.1%/16.0%. TTS outperforms speed perturbation (GT+300h TTS 12.6%/18.7% vs GT+speed-perturb 13.4%/19.2%, Whisper-small). Cross-domain ASCEND (Whisper-small): GT 17.8%, SEAME-fine-tuned CosyVoice 19.1%, zero-shot CosyVoice 25.2%.
- **Notes:** Random-speaker synthesis beats original-speaker synthesis. Returns diminish beyond ~300h synthetic. No code released; relies on public ESPnet/Whisper/CosyVoice2.

### 11. IndexTTS 2.5 Technical Report

_IndexTTS team (Bilibili) · 2026 · arXiv preprint (Bilibili IndexTTS team)_

- **Categories:** C2, C5, C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2601.03888) · arXiv:2601.03888 · [code](https://github.com/index-tts/index-tts)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Moderate. The multilingual data pipeline uses speech enhancement (Demucs) and acoustic preprocessing plus pseudo-labeling/synthetic-data augmentation to extend language coverage and balance the corpus; emotion supervision comes from Emotion2Vec-derived embeddings. Synthetic role is mainly data augmentation / pseudo-labeling for multilingual extension rather than training on fully synthetic speech or RL on generated audio.
- **Method:** An efficiency-and-coverage upgrade of IndexTTS 2: compress the semantic codec from 50Hz to 25Hz (halve sequence length), replace the U-DiT S2M backbone with a lighter Zipformer architecture, and extend multilingual coverage, yielding much faster inference at comparable quality with cross-lingual emotion transfer in the zero-shot setting.
- **Architecture:** Three-stage zero-shot TTS: Transformer Text-to-Semantic (T2S) module + non-autoregressive Semantic-to-Mel/Acoustic (S2M/S2A) module + acoustic codec decoder. v2.5 changes: semantic codec 50Hz->25Hz; S2M backbone changed from U-DiT to Zipformer encoder (fewer params, faster mel generation). Emotion2Vec embeddings condition expressive/emotional synthesis; duration prediction and CTC/attention objectives.
- **Base models:** Builds on IndexTTS 2 (T2S transformer + non-autoregressive S2M). Uses Emotion2Vec for emotion embeddings; inherits codec from IndexTTS 2 lineage.
- **Datasets:** Multilingual mix: CommonVoice, LibriSpeech, EMILIA, plus proprietary corpora (large hour count, exact total not stated). Speech enhanced via Demucs. Evaluated on multilingual zero-shot WER, speaker similarity, RTF, MOS.
- **Code:** https://github.com/index-tts/index-tts ; project page https://index-tts.github.io/index-tts2-5.github.io/ ; HF papers https://huggingface.co/papers/2601.03888
- **Recipe:** Start from IndexTTS 2. Retrain/compress semantic codec to 25Hz (half sequence length). Swap S2M U-DiT for Zipformer encoder to cut params and speed mel generation. Build multilingual pipeline: Demucs enhancement + acoustic preprocessing + pseudo-labeling/synthetic augmentation for under-resourced languages; condition on Emotion2Vec emotion embeddings. Train T2S (text->semantic) and S2M (semantic->mel) with CTC/attention + duration objectives; decode mel with acoustic codec/vocoder. Target 2.28x RTF speedup at matched WER/SIM.
- **Key results:** 2.28x RTF improvement over IndexTTS 2 with comparable WER and speaker similarity; broader language coverage; replicates emotional prosody in unseen languages under zero-shot. Exact WER/SIM/MOS numbers in paper tables (reported competitive with IndexTTS 2 baseline).
- **Notes:** Primarily an efficiency/coverage iteration (category 2 fine-tuning/upgrade + 5 augmentation + 6 multilingual). No RL/preference optimization reported. PDF rendering limited exact numeric tables; metrics described qualitatively as on-par-or-better vs IndexTTS 2 at much higher speed.

### 12. Investigating Group Relative Policy Optimization for Diffusion Transformer based Text-to-Audio Generation

_Yi Gu, Yanqing Liu, Chen Yang, Sheng Zhao · 2026 · arXiv preprint (eess.AS, Mar 2026)_

- **Categories:** C3, C4
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.01565) · arXiv:2603.01565
- **Synthetic-data role:** Synthetic data is textual, not audio: a large language model generates high-fidelity, richly detailed audio captions from the original (often ambiguous or underspecified) text prompts. These LLM-rewritten captions improve text-audio semantic alignment and are used as conditioning during GRPO fine-tuning. The audio itself is generated by the policy (the T2A DiT) during RL rollouts and scored by reward models, so generations are self-produced rollouts rather than a fixed synthetic corpus.
- **Method:** Apply Group Relative Policy Optimization (GRPO) to fine-tune a diffusion-transformer text-to-audio model, combined with an LLM caption-enrichment front end. The work systematically studies which reward functions (CLAP, KL, FAD, and combinations) drive effective RL for audio synthesis, analyzing how reward design affects audio quality and prompt adherence.
- **Architecture:** Diffusion Transformer (DiT)-based text-to-audio generation model fine-tuned with GRPO. An LLM front end rewrites/enriches captions. Reward signals include CLAP (audio-text contrastive alignment), KL divergence (regularization to reference policy), and FAD (Frechet Audio Distance) for fidelity. Specific codec/vocoder, model sizes, and latent-diffusion details are not reported in the available abstract/HTML.
- **Base models:** A pretrained DiT-based T2A model (likely Tango/Tango2-style or an internal Microsoft DiT T2A model given the authorship) serves as the policy initialized for GRPO; an unspecified LLM generates enriched captions; CLAP used as a reward/encoder. Exact base checkpoints not reported.
- **Datasets:** Not reported in the available abstract/HTML; T2A GRPO work of this type typically uses AudioCaps/Clotho-style caption-audio benchmarks, but specific training/eval sets and hours are not confirmed from the fetched source.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Take original T2A text prompts and use an LLM to rewrite them into detailed, high-fidelity audio captions to improve semantic alignment. 2) Initialize the policy from a pretrained DiT-based T2A model. 3) Run GRPO: for each prompt sample a group of audio generations, score each with reward functions (CLAP for text-audio alignment, FAD for fidelity, KL as regularizer), compute group-relative advantages, and update the DiT. 4) Ablate reward combinations (CLAP only, +KL, +FAD, combined) to identify drivers of synthesis quality. Specific learning rates, group sizes, diffusion sampling steps, and dataset scales are NOT reported in the fetched source; consult the PDF for full hyperparameters.
- **Key results:** GRPO-based fine-tuning yields substantial gains in synthesis fidelity and prompt adherence over the base T2A model; reward-design ablations identify CLAP/FAD/KL combinations as key drivers. Exact numerical CLAP/FAD/KL scores and baseline comparisons are not reported in the fetched abstract/HTML.
- **Notes:** Verified on arXiv (2603.01565, Mar 2026) with consistent abstract across arxiv.org, papers.cool, and arxiv HTML. Authors appear affiliated with Microsoft (Yanqing Liu, Sheng Zhao are known Microsoft TTS researchers). Quantitative metrics and dataset specifics require the full PDF. Related concurrent work: Tango 2 (DPO for T2A) and Resonate (online feedback RL).

### 13. Language-Invariant Multilingual Speaker Verification via Zero-Shot TTS (TidyVoice 2026 Challenge)

_ZXHY-82 et al. (LI-MSV-TidyVoice2026 team) · 2026 · Interspeech 2026 / TidyVoice 2026 Challenge system description_

- **Categories:** C5, C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.08092) · arXiv:2603.08092 · [code](https://github.com/ZXHY-82/LI-MSV-TidyVoice2026)
- **Synthetic-data role:** A multilingual zero-shot TTS (Qwen3-TTS-12Hz-1.7B-Base) is used for cross-lingual voice-cloning data augmentation. ~3,495 reference utterances (10+ per speaker, >=3s each) from TidyVoiceX are each re-synthesized into all 10 target languages, producing 349,500 synthetic utterances. Reference transcripts come from Whisper-large-v3; synthesis text is LibriTTS English sentences translated by M2M100 into each language. The synthetic speech adds language diversity per speaker so the SV model learns language-invariant speaker embeddings. Authors note synthetic augmentation helps mainly in low-resource conditions and gives limited gains when real data is already sufficient.
- **Method:** Fine-tune a large multilingual SSL backbone for speaker verification, add layer adapters and multi-scale feature aggregation to exploit all Conformer layers, and apply gradient-reversal language-adversarial training plus zero-shot-TTS cross-lingual augmentation to obtain language-invariant speaker embeddings.
- **Architecture:** Backbone: w2v-BERT 2.0 (24-layer Conformer, pretrained on 4.5M hours over 143 languages). Per-layer Layer Adapters for dimensionality reduction; Multi-scale Feature Aggregation (MFA) concatenating adapted layer features with attentive statistics pooling. SphereFace2-C / SimAM-ResNet34 heads compared. Language-adversarial branch: two-linear-layer language classifier behind a Gradient Reversal Layer.
- **Base models:** w2v-BERT 2.0 (SSL Conformer) as SV backbone; Qwen3-TTS-12Hz-1.7B-Base for synthesis; Whisper-large-v3 for ASR transcripts; M2M100 for text translation; SimAM-ResNet34 baseline.
- **Datasets:** Real: VoxCeleb2, VoxBlink2, 3D-Speaker, KeSpeech, CN-Celeb1&2, TidyVoiceX (challenge train). Synthetic: 349,500 Qwen3-TTS utterances across 10 languages (zh, en, ja, ko, de, fr, ru, pt, es, it). Eval: tv26_dev, tv26_eval-A, tv26_eval-U.
- **Code:** https://github.com/ZXHY-82/LI-MSV-TidyVoice2026
- **Recipe:** 1) Select ~3,495 reference utterances (>=10 per speaker, >=3s) from TidyVoiceX. 2) Transcribe references with Whisper-large-v3; take LibriTTS English sentences, translate via M2M100 into the 10 languages. 3) Use Qwen3-TTS-12Hz-1.7B-Base zero-shot voice cloning to synthesize each speaker in all 10 languages -> 349,500 utterances. 4) Fine-tune w2v-BERT 2.0 backbone; attach Layer Adapters per Conformer layer + MFA with attentive statistics pooling; SphereFace2-C margin head. 5) Add language-adversarial training: language classifier behind GRL with lambda_GRL=0.1 and lambda_lang=0.1, reversing gradients to suppress language information. 6) Optionally add synthetic data and apply QMF score calibration at test time.
- **Key results:** EER on tv26_dev / eval-A / eval-U: SimAM-ResNet34 baseline 3.07% / 9.058% / 11.59%; w2v-BERT 2.0 + SphereFace2-C 0.950% / 3.061% / 4.338%; + GRL adversarial 0.937% / 2.964% / 5.020%; + QMF calibration 0.893% / 2.458% / 4.451%. Synthetic-only training gave 1.022% dev EER. Large SSL fine-tuning gives the dominant gain; adversarial training adds robustness; synthetic augmentation helps mostly in low-resource settings.
- **Notes:** Title in the survey list is paraphrased; the actual arXiv title is 'Language-Invariant Multilingual Speaker Verification for the TidyVoice 2026 Challenge.' Task is speaker verification (downstream of TTS) rather than TTS itself, but TTS-generated multilingual speech is the core augmentation.

### 14. LEAF: Growing Trees Without Branching for Speech-Aware Large Language Model Post-Training

_Not reported (references Elmakies et al., 2026 as a baseline) · 2026 · arXiv preprint_

- **Categories:** C3
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2606.07610) · arXiv:2606.07610
- **Synthetic-data role:** No external synthetic data is used. The 'synthetic' element is the model's own on-policy rollouts: K complete responses are sampled per prompt and reused. LEAF's contribution is retrospectively organizing these i.i.d. rollouts into a tree (grouping by shared prefixes at high-surprisal boundaries) to derive span-level advantages, rather than generating new branched samples. All training datasets are established real benchmarks.
- **Method:** LEAF (Low-rank Exploration with Adaptive Forking) is a retrospective tree-based RL method for speech-aware LLM post-training. Standard GRPO broadcasts one terminal-reward advantage to every token, ignoring shared-prefix structure in rollouts. LEAF instead samples K complete responses recording token surprisals, selects B high-surprisal boundaries (with separation constraint Delta), groups responses by exact token-prefix equality into tree nodes, and assigns piecewise-constant span-level advantages combining global (vs root) and local (vs parent) value differences with multiplicity correction. This gives process-aware credit assignment with no online branching or extra decoding.
- **Architecture:** Speech-aware LLM backbones fine-tuned with LoRA under an RL objective. Three backbones evaluated: Granite Speech 3.3 (2B and 8B), Granite-4.0-1B-Speech, and Qwen2-Audio-7B. Standard audio tokenization; no special codec reported.
- **Base models:** Granite Speech 3.3 (2B/8B), Granite-4.0-1B-Speech, Qwen2-Audio-7B as policy initializations; LoRA adapters added on top.
- **Datasets:** All real benchmarks: LibriSQA (short-form spoken QA, 85,045 train), DailyTalk (long-form dialogue, 21,891 train), LongAudio (extended audio transcription, 13,374 train), CoVoST2 English-to-German speech translation (288,069 train). No synthetic data.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Initialize a speech-aware LLM (e.g. Granite Speech 3.3-2B) and add LoRA (rank 64, alpha 128, dropout 0.05). 2) For each prompt sample K=8 complete responses, recording per-token surprisals. 3) Greedily select B=2 high-surprisal boundaries subject to a minimum separation constraint Delta. 4) Group the K responses by exact token-prefix equality at those boundaries to form retained tree nodes. 5) Compute span-level piecewise-constant advantages = combination of global advantage (node value vs root) and local advantage (vs parent), with multiplicity correction. 6) Optimize with Adam, lr 5e-6, KL coefficient 0.02, reward = sentence BLEU, 1-6 epochs depending on dataset/model. Hardware: three A40 GPUs, single seed per setting. Full hyperparameters in Appendix B.1.
- **Key results:** LEAF beats LoRA-GRPO under identical rollout/LoRA budgets: LibriSQA (Granite 3.3-2B) +5.09 BLEU (Likert 3.34 vs 3.20; DA-100 86.64 vs 84.89); CoVoST2 (8B) +1.92 BLEU (DA-100 75.01 vs 73.05); DailyTalk +5.05 BLEU (DA-100 68.99 vs 62.62); LongAudio +8.68 BLEU (Likert 2.93 vs 2.43). Against published full-parameter GRPO (Elmakies et al., 2026), LEAF reaches 45.82 vs 44.90 BLEU on LibriSQA with 22.5x fewer trainable params (133.7M vs 3.01B). CVaR tail-risk metrics show reduced catastrophic failures.
- **Notes:** Verified on arXiv (2606.07610). Baselines: untrained base models, LoRA-GRPO, and full-parameter GRPO (Elmakies et al. 2026). Single training seed and 3x A40 GPU constraint are stated caveats. No public code found. Category 3 (RL/preference optimization for speech LLMs); note this is speech-understanding/translation post-training, not speech synthesis per se.

### 15. LLM-to-Speech: A Synthetic Data Pipeline for Training Dialectal Text-to-Speech Models

_Ahmed Khaled Khamis, Hesham Ali · 2026 · AbjadNLP / ACL Anthology 2026 (2026.abjadnlp-1.6)_

- **Categories:** C2, C4, C6, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2602.15675) · arXiv:2602.15675
- **Synthetic-data role:** The entire dialectal training corpus (NileTTS, 38 hours) is synthetically generated. An LLM generates Egyptian Arabic text across medical, sales, and general-conversation domains; that text is converted to speech with audio-synthesis tools; the resulting audio is then auto-transcribed (ASR) and speaker-diarized into two speakers, with manual quality verification. The fully synthetic corpus is used to fine-tune a multilingual TTS model for an under-resourced dialect.
- **Method:** A synthetic-data pipeline (LLM text generation -> speech synthesis -> ASR transcription -> diarization -> manual QA) that builds NileTTS, a 38-hour Egyptian-Arabic dialectal speech corpus, then fine-tunes XTTS v2 on it to produce a dialectal TTS model where no native transcribed data existed.
- **Architecture:** XTTS v2: autoregressive codec/token language model (GPT-style decoder predicting VQ-VAE / discrete audio tokens) plus HiFi-GAN-style decoder/vocoder, multilingual, with speaker conditioning for zero-shot voice cloning. Sizes not reported in abstract.
- **Base models:** Base TTS fine-tuned: Coqui XTTS v2 (multilingual). Synthetic-data pipeline relies on an unspecified LLM for Egyptian Arabic text generation and unspecified audio-synthesis tools plus an ASR system and a diarization model.
- **Datasets:** NileTTS: 38 hours of transcribed speech, 2 speakers, domains = medical, sales, general conversation; fully synthetically generated. Baseline comparison uses XTTS v2 trained/available on other Arabic dialects.
- **Code:** Authors state all resources and an open-source fine-tuned model are released; specific repository URL not found in abstract (none found).
- **Recipe:** 1) Prompt an LLM to generate Egyptian Arabic text spanning medical, sales, and general domains. 2) Synthesize speech from that text with audio-synthesis tools. 3) Run ASR to transcribe the synthesized audio and apply speaker diarization to attribute to two speakers. 4) Manually verify/clean transcripts and audio to form NileTTS (38 h). 5) Fine-tune XTTS v2 on NileTTS. 6) Evaluate against the baseline XTTS v2 (other Arabic dialects). Hyperparameters and training steps not reported in available text.
- **Key results:** Reports that the NileTTS-fine-tuned XTTS v2 is evaluated against a baseline trained on other Arabic dialects; specific numeric metrics (MOS/WER/CER) not stated in the available abstract/page.
- **Notes:** Addresses scarcity of neural TTS resources for Arabic dialects. Published in the AbjadNLP workshop (ACL Anthology 2026). Quantitative results require the full PDF; abstract emphasizes open release of model and resources.

### 16. MOSS-TTSD: Text to Spoken Dialogue Generation

_SII-OpenMOSS Team (OpenMOSS / MOSI.AI) · 2026 · arXiv preprint_

- **Categories:** C2, C4, C5, C6, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.19739) · arXiv:2603.19739 · [code](https://github.com/OpenMOSS/MOSS-TTSD)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Two roles. (1) Pseudo-labeling/data pipeline: an internal speaker-diarization model segments and speaker-attributes massive in-the-wild audio; a Chinese-finetuned Whisper-d model gives fine-grained speaker-attributed transcription; DNSMOS>=2.8 quality filtering; dialogue segments are constructed by concatenating speaker-separated audio. (2) Explicit synthetic speech: ~40,000 hours per language of SYNTHETIC dialogue data are generated specifically to improve speaker-switching/turn-taking accuracy. Codec additionally uses 500k h untranscribed audio.
- **Method:** Fully-discrete long-context spoken-dialogue model that turns a dialogue script with speaker tags into multi-speaker conversational speech (up to ~60 min single pass, up to 5 speakers, zero-shot cloning from a short reference). Built on an LLM backbone + audio tokenizer with a multi-head delay pattern; also introduces TTSD-eval, a forced-alignment-based evaluation of speaker-attribution accuracy and speaker similarity that avoids diarization tools.
- **Architecture:** Decoder-only LLM backbone (Qwen3-8B-base per the paper/GitHub; 8B 'MossTTSDelay' model) + MOSS-Audio-Tokenizer (Cat / Causal Audio Tokenizer with Transformer, ~1.6B params, CNN-free, ~1kbps); models only the first 16 RVQ layers with a multi-head delay pattern for robust long-context generation. (An earlier v0 variant used Qwen3-1.7B + XY-Tokenizer 8-layer RVQ.)
- **Base models:** Qwen3-8B-base LLM backbone; MOSS-Audio-Tokenizer (trained from scratch on ~3M h speech/SFX/music); initialized/continued from the MOSS-TTS single-speaker model.
- **Datasets:** TTS pretraining ~1.1M h ZH+EN speech (Seed-tts-eval reported); TTSD post-training ~100k h ZH + ~270k h EN conversational (~400k h dialogue total); +~40k h/language synthetic speaker-switching data; codec 100k h transcribed + 500k h untranscribed. Supports 20 languages.
- **Code:** https://github.com/OpenMOSS/MOSS-TTSD ; HF OpenMOSS-Team/MOSS-TTS(-D), ModelScope; project page https://www.open-moss.com/en/moss-ttsd/
- **Recipe:** 1) Data pipeline: diarize -> Whisper-d speaker-attributed transcription -> DNSMOS>=2.8 filter -> build dialogue segments. 2) Train MOSS-Audio-Tokenizer (16 RVQ used downstream) from scratch on ~3M h. 3) Three-stage curriculum starting from MOSS-TTS single-speaker checkpoint: TTS pretrain on ~1.1M h monologue (incl. voice-cloning data, DNSMOS>=2.8) -> TTSD post-train on ~400k h dialogue + ~40k h/lang synthetic switching data with WSD scheduler -> long-context/multi-speaker refinement; checkpoint selection by manual evaluation. Multi-head delay-pattern AR decoding on first 16 RVQ layers.
- **Key results:** TTS pretrain WER 1.54 (normalized) on Seed-tts-eval, competitive with strong baselines. Objective+subjective evals show MOSS-TTSD surpasses strong open-source and proprietary dialogue baselines; introduces TTSD-eval (speaker-attribution accuracy + speaker similarity). Exact dialogue WER/SIM numbers not fully quantified in fetched abstract.
- **Notes:** Apache-2.0. Backbone reported as Qwen3-8B-base (8B model) in the arXiv paper/GitHub; one secondary source described a 1.7B/XY-Tokenizer predecessor (v0). Up to 60 min single-pass, 5 speakers, 20 languages, zero-shot cloning.

### 17. OV-InstructTTS: Towards Open-Vocabulary Instruct Text-to-Speech

_Yong Ren, Jiangyan Yi, Jianhua Tao, et al. (Institute of Automation CAS, Tsinghua University, and others) · 2026 · arXiv preprint (Jan 2026)_

- **Categories:** C2, C4, C5, C6, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2601.01459) · arXiv:2601.01459 · [code](https://y-ren16.github.io/OV-InstructTTS)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Heavily synthetic-annotation-driven. The OV-Speech dataset is built on real ContextSpeech audiobook audio (476.8h), but all supervision around it is LLM-generated: Qwen3-32B generates 2-5 open-vocabulary instructions per utterance from 1000-word narrative-context windows; DeepSeek-R1 predicts emotional/acoustic attributes and Qwen3-32B judges instruction-attribute consistency for filtering; Qwen3-32B then writes step-by-step reasoning chains (Instruction Deconstruction + Attribute Inference) linking each instruction to acoustic attributes; a fine-tuned Qwen2-Audio-7B inserts 18 paralinguistic tags via a two-stage PC-PTI method. These LLM-generated reasoning chains and enriched transcripts are the actual training targets (SFT supervision). Speech is real; instructions, reasoning, and paralinguistic/emotion annotations are synthetic.
- **Method:** Introduces open-vocabulary InstructTTS: handling flexible, high-level descriptive instructions rather than rephrased acoustic labels. Provides (1) OV-Speech, a dataset pairing speech with open-vocabulary instructions each augmented with an explicit reasoning process, and (2) OV-InstructTTS-TEP, a reasoning-driven framework that first 'thinks' (maps instruction to emotion/acoustic/paralinguistic info) then generates interleaved text-audio tokens with enriched transcripts of form '[emotion label] Transcript <|paralinguistic tags|>'.
- **Architecture:** Audio LLM that emits interleaved text+audio tokens. Two stages: a Thinking stage producing textual reasoning, and a Generation stage producing enriched transcript + discrete audio tokens. Audio tokens are converted to waveform by a flow-matching model + HiFiGAN vocoder inherited from the base. Built on Step-Audio-2-mini-Base.
- **Base models:** Step-Audio-2-mini-Base (pretrained large audio language model) fine-tuned via SFT. Annotation pipeline relies on Qwen3-32B, DeepSeek-R1, and a fine-tuned Qwen2-Audio-7B. Flow-matching + HiFiGAN vocoder inherited from Step-Audio-2-mini-Base.
- **Datasets:** OV-Speech: 316,807 training utterances (3 instructions each) + 1,500 test samples, derived from ContextSpeech (476.8h Mandarin audiobooks, 83 novels, ~100-200 narrators). Test set drawn from unseen novels/speakers.
- **Code:** https://y-ren16.github.io/OV-InstructTTS (project page with dataset/demos); depends on https://github.com/stepfun-ai/Step-Audio2
- **Recipe:** Data: 1) Take ContextSpeech utterances with surrounding 1000-word context. 2) Qwen3-32B generates 2-5 open-vocab instructions per utterance from context. 3) DeepSeek-R1 predicts emotional/acoustic attributes; Qwen3-32B judges instruction-attribute consistency, discarding low-scoring pairs. 4) Qwen3-32B writes reasoning chains (Instruction Deconstruction -> Attribute Inference). 5) Fine-tuned Qwen2-Audio-7B inserts 18 paralinguistic tags via PC-PTI two-stage classify-then-insert (0.35% S-CER). Training: SFT of Step-Audio-2-mini-Base on (instruction -> reasoning -> '[emotion] transcript <|tags|>' + audio tokens). LR 1e-5, global batch size 32, 8x A100 80GB. Inference uses inherited flow-matching + HiFiGAN to render audio tokens.
- **Key results:** OV-InstructTTS-TEP: Gemini Score 70.42 (GT 75.43; best baseline GPT-4o 68.31); MOS 4.28 (beats GT 4.10 and best baseline 3.84); ICMOS 3.91; CER 3.61% (GT 3.10%); speaker similarity 0.722 (vs 0.707). Ablations: full +T,+E,+P gives best Gemini Score 71.57; reasoning alone +T = 68.71 vs 67.70 baseline; enriched transcripts without reasoning marginal/negative.
- **Notes:** Mandarin audiobook domain. Reasoning chains as explicit supervision are the key novelty; demonstrates LLM-generated reasoning + paralinguistic annotation as training signal on real speech.

### 18. Qwen3-TTS Technical Report

_Qwen Team, Alibaba Cloud · 2026 · arXiv preprint (Qwen Team, Alibaba Cloud)_

- **Categories:** C3, C4, C6, C2
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2601.15621) · arXiv:2601.15621 · [code](https://github.com/QwenLM/Qwen3-TTS)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Synthetic/derived data is used in two ways. (1) Preference data: preference pairs for multilingual samples are constructed (machine-scored, human-feedback-grounded) to drive DPO and GSPO rule-based-reward RL post-training, i.e. the model is optimized on judged outputs. (2) Data-quality pipeline assigns stratified quality levels (machine-labeled) and uses long-speech upsampling/augmentation for the long-context stage. The report stresses real high-quality data over fully synthetic speech; synthetic role is concentrated in preference/reward construction and quality annotation rather than synthetic training audio.
- **Method:** A multilingual, controllable, streaming TTS family using a dual-track LM (text and acoustic tokens concatenated along the channel axis; predict acoustic tokens right after each text token) with a jointly trained learnable speaker encoder, two interchangeable speech tokenizers, three-stage pretraining, and three-stage post-training (DPO, GSPO rule-based RL, speaker SFT). Supports 3s voice cloning and description/instruction-based voice design.
- **Architecture:** Dual-track autoregressive LM over concatenated text+acoustic tokens; learnable speaker encoder trained jointly. Two tokenizers: (a) Qwen-TTS-Tokenizer-25Hz, single-codebook, built on Qwen2-Audio, two-stage (ASR pretrain + mel reconstruction), block-wise DiT streaming reconstruction; (b) Qwen-TTS-Tokenizer-12Hz, 12.5Hz multi-codebook with 16 quantizers, Mimi-style semantic-acoustic disentanglement, GAN training, causal ConvNet decoder. Model sizes 0.6B and 1.7B; variants Base/VoiceDesign/CustomVoice/VoiceEditing.
- **Base models:** Backbone from the Qwen3 LM family; 25Hz tokenizer leverages Qwen2-Audio encoder. Speaker encoder trained jointly. Specialized variants fine-tuned from the Base model.
- **Datasets:** Over 5,000,000 hours of speech across 10 languages (zh, en, de, it, pt, es, ja, ko, fr, ru). Quality-stratified internal data pipeline. Eval on Seed-TTS-Eval, multilingual TTS test set, InstructTTSEval, and a long-speech test set. Preference pairs constructed for multilingual samples.
- **Code:** https://github.com/QwenLM/Qwen3-TTS ; HF: https://huggingface.co/Qwen/Qwen3-TTS-12Hz-0.6B-Base (Apache-2.0)
- **Recipe:** Pretrain S1 (general, 5M+ hr, monotonic text->speech mapping), S2 (high-quality continual pretrain on quality-stratified data to cut hallucinations), S3 (long-context, expand 8192->32768 tokens with long-speech upsampling). Post-train: (1) DPO on human-preference multilingual pairs; (2) rule-based rewards optimized with GSPO; (3) lightweight speaker fine-tuning of Base. Tokenizers trained separately (25Hz: ASR pretrain then mel recon + block-wise DiT; 12Hz: 16-codebook RVQ, GAN, causal conv). Sizes 0.6B/1.7B. Apache-2.0 release of tokenizers+models.
- **Key results:** Seed-TTS zero-shot clone (12Hz-1.7B): WER 0.77 (zh), 1.24 (en), beating CosyVoice 3 and MiniMax-Speech. Lowest WER in 6/10 languages; highest speaker similarity all 10 languages (cos 0.73-0.82). Cross-lingual zh->ko 4.82 vs CosyVoice 3 14.4 (~66% error reduction). InstructTTSEval voice design 85.2 APS / 81.1 DSD / 65.1 RP (zh); +28% over GPT-4o-mini-tts on speaker editing. Long-form 10+ min: 1.517 WER (zh), 1.225 (en). First-packet 97-101ms; RTF 0.288-0.434 at 6x concurrency.
- **Notes:** Apache-2.0. GSPO = Group Sequence/Supervised Policy Optimization (RL). Emphasizes real data quality over synthetic audio; synthetic contribution is in preference/reward data and quality labeling. Category 4 applies via LLM/description-conditioned voice-design data and instruction text.

### 19. SelfTTS: Cross-Speaker Style Transfer through Explicit Embedding Disentanglement and Self-Refinement using Self-Augmentation

_AI-Unicamp group (UNICAMP and CPQD, Brazil) · 2026 · arXiv preprint (cs.SD); from UNICAMP / CPQD, Brazil_

- **Categories:** C2, C5, C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.22252) · arXiv:2603.22252 · [code](https://github.com/AI-Unicamp/SelfTTS)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Synthetic speech is generated BY THE MODEL ITSELF via its learned voice-conversion capability (self-augmentation). After base training, source utterances are encoded to latent z, passed through normalizing flows conditioned on a randomly-permuted TARGET speaker reference while keeping the SOURCE emotion, producing synthetic samples that preserve the original emotion across different voices. A fixed proportion of each training batch is masked and replaced with these self-generated synthetic samples to refine naturalness and disentanglement. On-the-fly self-augmentation, not a fixed pre-built corpus; applied only after pre-training during a 50k-step refinement stage.
- **Method:** Cross-speaker emotional style transfer TTS that removes external pretrained speaker/emotion encoders. It explicitly disentangles speaker and emotion embeddings using Gradient Reversal Layers (GRL) + cosine-similarity loss, encourages clustered embeddings with Multi-Positive Contrastive Learning (MPCL), then self-refines via self-augmentation: uses its own voice-conversion path to synthesize emotion-preserving cross-speaker samples mixed into training to make a neutral target speaker expressive.
- **Architecture:** VITS-based end-to-end conditional VAE (posterior encoder, residual coupling/normalizing flow blocks, stochastic duration predictor, GAN waveform decoder used as vocoder). Adds dedicated speaker embedding g and emotion embedding e conditioning all sub-modules. Reference Encoder = 6-layer CNN over mel-spectrogram + GRU producing a fixed-length embedding. GRL + cosine-similarity for disentanglement; MPCL contrastive objective.
- **Base models:** Initialized from a VITS checkpoint pre-trained on VCTK (800k steps). No external speaker/emotion encoder is used (explicit design goal).
- **Datasets:** ESD emotional speech corpus (350 parallel utterances, 20 speakers - 10 English, 10 Mandarin; 5 emotions: neutral/happy/angry/sad/surprise; >29 h). Cross-corpus neutral data from LJSpeech and VCTK speakers p226, p231 (~350 neutral sentences each). Target neutral speakers: ESD speakers 11 (M) and 15 (F), only their neutral data used in training. Synthetic data = self-generated VC samples (on the fly).
- **Code:** https://github.com/AI-Unicamp/SelfTTS (samples: https://ai-unicamp.github.io/publications/tts/selftts/)
- **Recipe:** 1) Pre-train VITS backbone on VCTK for 800k steps. 2) Main training 200k steps with speaker/emotion conditioning, GRL+cosine disentanglement, and MPCL contrastive loss on speaker and emotion embeddings. 3) Self-augmentation refinement: 50k steps at reduced LR 2e-5; each batch has a fixed proportion masked and replaced by self-generated VC samples (encode source -> z -> flows conditioned on permuted target speaker + source emotion). Optimizer AdamW (beta1=0.8, beta2=0.99, weight decay 0.01); initial LR 2e-4 decayed 0.999^(1/8) per epoch; batch size 64; single NVIDIA L40S (48GB), ~2 days per run. Evaluation via Whisper WER, Resemblyzer SECS, emotion2vec+ EECS, UTMOS, and CKA/LK-CKA for disentanglement.
- **Key results:** vs E3-VITS and VECL baselines: eMOS 2.853 (best; E3-VITS 2.237, VECL 2.556); sMOS 3.112 (best); SECS 0.8163 (best); EECS 0.8423 (best). nMOS 2.746, UTMOS 3.6104 (below E3-VITS 3.9614). WER 0.2305 (higher than E3-VITS 0.2011 / VECL 0.1944). Ablation 'w/o Aug.' lowers nMOS from 2.746 to 2.228, showing self-augmentation mainly improves naturalness.
- **Notes:** arXiv ID 2603.22252 is consistent with a 2026 submission. Improves naturalness/emotional expressivity and speaker/emotion similarity at a small WER cost. No external encoders is the key claim.

### 20. ZeSTA: Zero-Shot TTS Augmentation with Domain-Conditioned Training for Data-Efficient Personalized Speech Synthesis

_Youngwon Choi, Jinwoo Oh, Hwayeon Kim, Hyeonyu Kim · 2026 · Interspeech 2026 (accepted; 6 pages)_

- **Categories:** C2, C5, C6, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.04219) · arXiv:2603.04219
- **Synthetic-data role:** Zero-shot TTS systems are used as a data-augmentation source: they generate large amounts of synthetic personalized speech (linguistically rich, phonetically diverse) for a target speaker to supplement a very small set of real target recordings during fine-tuning. The central finding is that naively mixing this synthetic speech with limited real data degrades speaker similarity, so synthetic data is explicitly tagged via a domain embedding and down-weighted relative to oversampled real data.
- **Method:** A domain-conditioned fine-tuning framework for low-resource personalized TTS: distinguish real vs synthetic (ZS-TTS-generated) speech with a lightweight domain embedding and oversample real data, so the model exploits synthetic augmentation for coverage while steering generation toward the real-speaker domain at inference.
- **Architecture:** Works on top of an existing TTS backbone without modifying its architecture; adds only a lightweight domain embedding (a learned real-vs-synthetic conditioning token/vector) injected into the base model. Two external ZS-TTS systems serve as the synthetic-speech generators.
- **Base models:** A base personalized TTS model fine-tuned per target speaker (architecture unchanged); two unspecified zero-shot TTS systems act as the augmentation/synthetic-data sources. Specific model names not reported.
- **Datasets:** LibriTTS and an in-house/proprietary dataset; synthetic augmentation produced by two ZS-TTS sources. Hours/scale not stated in abstract.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** (1) Take limited real recordings of a target speaker. (2) Generate synthetic personalized speech with zero-shot TTS systems (two sources) to expand phonetic/linguistic coverage. (3) Fine-tune the base TTS with a domain embedding that flags each utterance as real or synthetic, conditioning generation on domain. (4) Oversample real data to stabilize adaptation under extremely limited target data. (5) At inference, condition on the real-domain embedding to bias output toward the genuine speaker. No base-architecture changes required. Exact oversampling ratio, embedding dimension, and fine-tuning hyperparameters not reported in abstract.
- **Key results:** Improves speaker similarity over naive synthetic augmentation while preserving intelligibility and perceptual quality, on LibriTTS and the in-house set with two ZS-TTS sources. Exact SIM/MOS numbers in the paper.
- **Notes:** Practical, architecture-agnostic recipe; key insight is that synthetic ZS-TTS speech helps coverage but hurts speaker fidelity unless domain-separated and counterbalanced with real-data oversampling. arXiv ID 2603.04219 corresponds to a March 2026 listing; confirmed via arXiv abs/html/pdf and ResearchGate. Code/audio samples on a project page (URL not surfaced).

### 21. A Self-Refining Framework for Enhancing ASR Using TTS-Synthesized Data

_Cheng-Kang Chou, Chan-Jan Hsu, Ho-Lam Chung, Liang-Hsuan Tseng, Hsi-Chun Cheng, Yu-Kuan Fu, Kuan Po Huang, Hung-Yi Lee · 2025 · arXiv preprint_

- **Categories:** C4, C5, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.11130) · arXiv:2506.11130
- **Synthetic-data role:** Closed-loop bootstrapping with only unlabeled data: (1) an existing ASR pseudo-labels unlabeled speech; (2) those speech-pseudolabel pairs train a high-fidelity TTS; (3) the TTS synthesizes new speech-text pairs (using an external text corpus) fed back to fine-tune the ASR. Both pseudo-labels (synthetic text) and TTS-synthesized audio are the synthetic data driving improvement.
- **Method:** A self-refining cyclic framework improving ASR using only unlabeled speech and text. The ASR pseudo-labels unlabeled speech, those pairs train a TTS, and the TTS generates additional synthetic speech-text pairs reintegrated to fine-tune the ASR, forming a closed loop adapted to a low-resource/code-switching target domain (Taiwanese Mandarin).
- **Architecture:** Whisper-large-v2 as ASR backbone; a high-fidelity TTS trained on pseudo-labeled data. Iterative ASR <-> TTS data-exchange loop.
- **Base models:** ASR: Whisper-large-v2 (fine-tuned into the resulting model 'Twister'). TTS: trained from the pseudo-labeled corpus (specific backbone in full paper).
- **Datasets:** ~6,000 hours unlabeled speech plus a text corpus, targeting Taiwanese Mandarin with Mandarin-English code-switching evaluation. Synthetic data = ASR pseudo-labels + TTS-synthesized speech-text pairs.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Start from Whisper-large-v2. 2) Run it over ~6,000 h unlabeled speech to produce pseudo-labels. 3) Train a high-fidelity TTS on (speech, pseudo-label) pairs. 4) Use a text corpus to drive the TTS, synthesizing new (text, synthetic-speech) pairs. 5) Fine-tune Whisper on a mix incorporating these synthetic pairs, yielding 'Twister'. 6) Optionally iterate the loop. 7) Evaluate on Mandarin and Mandarin-English code-switching benchmarks. Needs no human transcriptions, only unlabeled audio and text.
- **Key results:** Resulting model 'Twister' achieves ~20% relative error-rate reduction on Mandarin and ~50% on Mandarin-English code-switching benchmarks vs Whisper baseline.
- **Notes:** License CC BY 4.0. Strong fit for self-training / pseudo-labeling and TTS-for-ASR augmentation. Code URL not found in available text.

### 22. Active Learning for Text-to-Speech Synthesis with Informative Sample Collection

_Kentaro Seki, Shinnosuke Takamichi, Takaaki Saeki, Hiroshi Saruwatari · 2025 · arXiv preprint; also IEEE (Xplore document 11249057), University of Tokyo / Keio University_

- **Categories:** C5, C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.08319) · arXiv:2507.08319
- **Synthetic-data role:** Synthetic speech is used as the INFORMATIVENESS PROBE rather than as training data: at each active-learning round, the current TTS model zero-shot synthesizes speech for candidate speakers/utterances; if synthetic quality already exceeds a high-quality threshold theta_hq the real sample is judged redundant and excluded, so only informative real samples are collected. Diffusion-based synthetic speaker embeddings are also generated to test speaker-generalization.
- **Method:** An active-learning corpus-construction loop for multi-speaker TTS that iteratively alternates data collection and model training, selecting only the samples the current model cannot yet synthesize well. This yields a data-efficient corpus that trains higher-quality TTS than equal-size passively-collected corpora, while collecting web-scale data on demand to avoid downloading everything.
- **Architecture:** Multi-speaker FastSpeech 2 acoustic model (non-autoregressive Transformer with predicted durations) conditioned on x-vector speaker embeddings (instead of one-hot IDs), with a HiFi-GAN vocoder. A diffusion model generates novel speaker embeddings for generalization testing. Pseudo-MOS predictor used as the quality oracle.
- **Base models:** FastSpeech 2 + HiFi-GAN as the TTS backbone; x-vector speaker encoder for conditioning; an automatic MOS-prediction model (pseudo-MOS) as the informativeness/quality estimator. not reported which specific pretrained checkpoints.
- **Datasets:** Candidate pool: web-scale YouTube speech, 2,719 speakers / ~66h, downloaded on-demand in segments. Evaluation: 100 phonetically balanced sentences from the JVS corpus; 324 test sentences from the ITA corpus (Japanese).
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Initialize a multi-speaker FastSpeech 2 (x-vector conditioned) + HiFi-GAN. 2) Iterate active-learning rounds: for each candidate speaker/utterance, zero-shot synthesize with the current model and score with a pseudo-MOS predictor; if predicted quality > theta_hq, mark redundant and skip (do not download/add), otherwise add the real sample to the training corpus. 3) Retrain/continue training the TTS on the updated corpus. 4) Download web data on demand by segments rather than the full dataset upfront. 5) Evaluate with pseudo-MOS, high-quality-speaker ratio, Wasserstein-1 distance of speaker distribution, and minimum-spanning-tree length for speaker diversity; diffusion-generated speaker embeddings test generalization.
- **Key results:** At equal corpus size the active-learning corpus produced 71.0% high-quality speakers vs 66.6% for the baseline (passive) corpus, and higher pseudo-MOS / better speaker-distribution coverage, demonstrating more data-efficient corpus construction.
- **Notes:** Japanese-language study. Synthetic speech here is a selection signal, not augmentation training data, so the synthetic-data role is methodological (active-learning informativeness gate). On-demand streaming download is a practical storage-cost contribution.

### 23. Adaptive Data Augmentation with NaturalSpeech3 for Far-field Speaker Verification

_Li Zhang, Jiyao Liu, Lei Xie (Northwestern Polytechnical University) · 2025 · ICASSP 2025 (IEEE Xplore 10822278)_

- **Categories:** C5, C6, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2501.08691) · arXiv:2501.08691
- **Synthetic-data role:** Synthetic = pseudo far-field speech generated by a TTS-codec voice-conversion procedure. The augmented utterances are produced by NaturalSpeech3's FACodec: it disentangles speech into content, prosody, speaker, and residual (acoustic-detail) embeddings, then reconstructs S_pseudo-far = C(F^f_p, F^f_c, F^n_s, F^f_r), combining far-field prosody/content/residual embeddings with near-field speaker embeddings. This injects near-field (clean, many-speaker) identities into the far-field acoustic environment, expanding speaker-annotated far-field data. Identity space scales to q x t (far-field x near-field speakers), e.g. 120 FFSVC2020 speakers crossed with 1,991 AISHELL-2 speakers.
- **Method:** Use NaturalSpeech3's FACodec as an attribute-disentangling neural codec to do controllable voice conversion, mixing near-field speaker identity into far-field acoustic conditions to synthesize labeled pseudo far-field training data, then train an ECAPA-TDNN speaker verification model on the augmented set. Augmentation is 'adaptive' in that it preserves the in-domain far-field channel/noise while swapping in out-domain near-field identities.
- **Architecture:** Disentanglement/voice-conversion: FACodec from NaturalSpeech3 (factorized neural audio codec; NaturalSpeech3 is ~1B params trained on 200k hours). Speaker verification backbone: ECAPA-TDNN (1024 channels) trained with AAM-Softmax (margin 0.2, scale 30); cosine-similarity scoring.
- **Base models:** NaturalSpeech3 / FACodec (pretrained foundation TTS-codec, ~1B params, 200k hours) used as the frozen disentanglement+reconstruction engine. ECAPA-TDNN as the SV model.
- **Datasets:** Far-field (in-domain): FFSVC2020 (120 training speakers, 35 dev speakers). Near-field (out-domain): AISHELL-2 (~1,000 hours clean read speech, 1,991 speakers). Synthetic: pseudo far-field utterances generated by crossing these speaker pools.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Take FACodec from NaturalSpeech3 to decompose far-field utterances into content/prosody/speaker/residual embeddings and near-field utterances likewise. 2) Generate pseudo far-field speech by FACodec reconstruction with far-field prosody+content+residual and near-field speaker embedding. 3) Build expanded training set from real far-field + pseudo far-field (and clean near-field). 4) Train ECAPA-TDNN (1024 ch): 80-dim log Mel-filterbank, 25 ms window / 10 ms shift; AAM-Softmax margin=0.2, scale=30; cosine scoring. Evaluate on FFSVC2020 Task1/2/3.
- **Key results:** On FFSVC2020 with the adaptive augmentation: Task1 EER 6.022% / minDCF 0.5366; Task2 EER 7.669% / 0.6892; Task3 EER 5.707% / 0.5820. Versus baseline Task1 10.00%/0.8399, Task2 14.06%/0.9575, Task3 8.711%/0.8203 - roughly 35-45% relative EER reduction.
- **Notes:** FACodec disentanglement is approximate so residual speaker leakage / channel artifacts are possible; the augmentation effectively performs identity transplant via codec resynthesis. Mandarin SV setting (AISHELL-2 + FFSVC2020). No code released.

### 24. Advancing Zero-shot Text-to-Speech Intelligibility across Diverse Domains via Preference Alignment

_Xueyao Zhang, Yuancheng Wang, Chaoren Wang, Ziniu Li, Zhuo Chen, Zhizheng Wu · 2025 · ACL 2025 (Main, Long)_

- **Categories:** C3, C7, C5, C4, C6, C2
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2505.04113) · arXiv:2505.04113 · [code](https://huggingface.co/datasets/amphion/INTP)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Introduces INTP, a large fully-synthetic preference dataset: ~250K preference pairs (>2,000 hours) of generated speech across regular, repeated-word, code-switching, and cross-lingual (out-of-pretraining-distribution) text. Pairs are built three ways: (a) Intra pairs via Best-of-N self-sampling from one model, (b) Inter pairs comparing outputs across different TTS models, and (c) Perturbed pairs where human-guided text perturbations (pronunciation/punctuation edits) create deliberately bad negatives. Chosen/rejected is decided by intelligibility (pointwise text-accuracy / WER-style annotation) plus pairwise naturalness preference. The synthetic speech is generated by three TTS systems (an AR system, F5-TTS, MaskGCT).
- **Method:** Improve zero-shot TTS intelligibility on hard domains by preference alignment: targetedly construct out-of-distribution preference data (INTP) and extend DPO so it works across heterogeneous TTS architecture families (autoregressive, flow-matching, masked-generative). Aligning on INTP improves intelligibility plus naturalness, similarity, and audio quality, and supports iterative alignment and weak-to-strong generalization.
- **Architecture:** Architecture-agnostic preference alignment applied to three TTS families: AR LM + codec (auto-regressive system, and CosyVoice 2-style), flow-matching models (F5-TTS), and masked generative models (MaskGCT). DPO loss is adapted to each family's training objective. Sizes per model not individually reported.
- **Base models:** Pretrained zero-shot TTS systems aligned/evaluated: CosyVoice 2 (AR), F5-TTS (flow matching), MaskGCT (masked generative), and an in-house 'Ints' system; the generators producing INTP samples are an AR system, F5-TTS, and MaskGCT.
- **Datasets:** INTP synthetic preference dataset: ~250K pairs / >2,000h over regular + repeated + code-switching + cross-lingual domains (HF: amphion/INTP, CC-BY-NC-4.0). Evaluation on Amphion-TTS-Eval with objective WER/CER and SIM plus subjective metrics across the hard domains.
- **Code:** https://huggingface.co/datasets/amphion/INTP (dataset); project/eval via Amphion (https://github.com/open-mmlab/Amphion); paper PDF https://aclanthology.org/2025.acl-long.598.pdf
- **Recipe:** Data pipeline: (1) Generate candidate speech with three TTS systems (AR, F5-TTS, MaskGCT) over diverse texts spanning regular, repeated-word, code-switching, and cross-lingual domains. (2) Build preference pairs three ways: Intra (Best-of-N self-sampling within one model), Inter (cross-model comparison to exploit complementary strengths), and Perturbed (human-guided text perturbations of pronunciation/punctuation to manufacture hard negatives). (3) Annotate preference by pointwise intelligibility (text-accuracy / WER) and pairwise naturalness, defining chosen vs rejected; yields ~250K pairs / >2,000h (INTP). Training: apply DPO, with the loss adapted to each architecture family (AR / FM / MGM), to the corresponding pretrained TTS model; supports iterative alignment (re-generate, re-rank, re-align) for further gains. Evaluate on Amphion-TTS-Eval reporting WER/CER and SIM.
- **Key results:** After INTP alignment, consistent improvements across CosyVoice 2, F5-TTS, and MaskGCT in intelligibility (lower WER/CER), plus gains in naturalness, speaker similarity (SIM), and audio quality across regular and hard domains (tongue-twisters, repeats, code-switch, cross-lingual). Demonstrates weak-to-strong generalization and additional gains from iterative alignment. Exact per-model WER/SIM numbers were not extractable from the available HTML/PDF render; full numeric tables are in the ACL anthology PDF.
- **Notes:** Verified via arXiv, HF dataset card, ACL anthology, OpenReview. Strong category-7/4 example: a large synthetic preference corpus from multiple TTS systems with multi-source pair construction (intra/inter/perturbed). Dataset license CC-BY-NC-4.0 (non-commercial). Cross-lingual/code-switch coverage also touches multilingual (cat 6). PDF binary did not parse cleanly via WebFetch, so precise per-model numbers were unavailable, but existence and method are well-corroborated.

### 25. Align2Speak: Improving TTS for Low Resource Languages via ASR-Guided Online Preference Optimization

_Shehzeen Hussain, Paarth Neekhara, Xuesong Yang, Edresson Casanova, Subhankar Ghosh, Roy Fejgin, Ryan Langman, Mikyas Desta, Leili Tavabi, Jason Li (NVIDIA) · 2025 · arXiv preprint_

- **Categories:** C2, C3, C5, C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2509.21718) · arXiv:2509.21718
- **Synthetic-data role:** The core data is unpaired/text-only: during the GRPO stage the model is driven with unpaired target-language text and arbitrary speaker prompts (no ground-truth speech). The policy TTS generates candidate speech online, which is pseudo-labeled by frozen reward models (pretrained ASR for intelligibility, speaker-verification for similarity, audio-quality estimator). The reward signal, derived entirely from synthesized samples scored by these models, replaces paired supervision, so synthetic generations plus model-derived pseudo-rewards are the entire training signal in the alignment phase. This sidesteps the lack of paired low-resource speech corpora.
- **Method:** Adapt an autoregressive multilingual TTS model to a new low-resource language using online preference optimization (GRPO) guided by an ASR-centric multi-objective reward, so that abundant text plus cheap ASR/SV/quality models substitute for scarce paired text-speech data.
- **Architecture:** Autoregressive, multilingual TTS LM operating on IPA (International Phonetic Alphabet) input tokens predicting discrete acoustic/codec tokens (Koel-TTS-style encoder-decoder transformer lineage from the same group); reward models are a pretrained ASR, a speaker-verification model, and an audio-quality estimator used as frozen scorers in GRPO.
- **Base models:** Pretrained multilingual IPA-based autoregressive TTS foundation model (same NVIDIA Koel-TTS lineage); frozen pretrained ASR, speaker-verification, and audio-quality models as reward functions. Initialized from a multilingual baseline then fine-tuned on limited paired target-language data before GRPO.
- **Datasets:** Multilingual baseline trained on multiple high/low-resource languages (IPA tokens); target low-resource languages adapted with limited paired text-speech then GRPO on unpaired text + speaker prompts. Specific language list, dataset names, and hours not reported in the abstract (full paper required).
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** Three stages: (1) Pretrain a multilingual autoregressive TTS on IPA tokens across languages. (2) Supervised fine-tune on the limited paired text-speech available for the target low-resource language. (3) GRPO online preference optimization: feed unpaired target-language text + speaker prompts, sample a group of candidate generations per prompt, score each with a multi-objective reward = combination of ASR intelligibility (e.g. negative WER/CER), speaker-verification similarity to the prompt, and audio-quality estimate; compute group-relative advantages and update the policy. No paired data needed in stage 3. Exact group size, reward weighting, KL/beta, and learning rates not reported in the abstract.
- **Key results:** Produces intelligible, speaker-consistent speech in low-resource languages and substantially outperforms fine-tuning alone; in high-resource settings surpasses offline alignment (DPO) on intelligibility, speaker similarity, and audio quality. Exact metric numbers not reported in the abstract.
- **Notes:** Same author group as Koel-TTS (NVIDIA), strongly suggesting Align2Speak builds on the Koel-TTS architecture. Key contribution is ONLINE (GRPO) vs offline (DPO) preference optimization and using ASR/SV/quality models as the reward to avoid paired low-resource data. Detailed datasets/hyperparameters require the full PDF.

### 26. ArVoice: A Multi-Speaker Dataset for Arabic Speech Synthesis

_Hawau Olamide Toyin, Rufael Marew, Humaid Alblooshi, Samar M. Magdy, Hanan Aldarmaki · 2025 · INTERSPEECH 2025 (accepted); MBZUAI_

- **Categories:** C4, C6, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2505.20506) · arXiv:2505.20506 · [code](https://huggingface.co/datasets/MBZUAI/ArVoice)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Part of the released corpus is itself synthetic: high-quality synthetic speech generated by TWO commercial TTS systems is included alongside human recordings, so the dataset is partially synthetically generated (a corpus partly built from synthetic speech). Synthetic voices expand speaker/voice count to 11 total. The diacritized text serves all voices.
- **Method:** Introduce a multi-speaker Modern Standard Arabic (MSA) corpus with fully diacritized transcriptions, combining professional human recordings, a cleaned subset of the existing Arabic Speech Corpus, and commercial-TTS synthetic speech, then demonstrate utility by training open-source TTS and voice-conversion systems.
- **Architecture:** Dataset paper (no single model). For demonstration they trained three open-source TTS systems and two voice-conversion systems on ArVoice (specific architectures used as baselines, e.g. standard neural TTS / VC pipelines).
- **Base models:** Existing Arabic Speech Corpus (modified subset) as a source; two unnamed commercial TTS systems generate the synthetic portion; three open-source TTS and two VC systems trained as demonstrations. not reported which exact open-source models.
- **Datasets:** ArVoice: 83.52 hours total across 11 voices; ~10 hours from 7 human speakers (6 professional voice talents + diverse demographics) plus a modified subset of the Arabic Speech Corpus; remainder is synthetic speech from two commercial TTS systems. All Modern Standard Arabic with diacritized transcriptions.
- **Code:** https://huggingface.co/datasets/MBZUAI/ArVoice
- **Recipe:** Corpus-construction recipe: 1) Record 6 professional voice talents reading diacritized MSA text (~10h with additional speakers). 2) Take and clean/modify a subset of the Arabic Speech Corpus. 3) Generate synthetic speech for the same diacritized text using two commercial TTS systems. 4) Combine to 83.52h / 11 voices with full diacritization. 5) Benchmark by training 3 open-source TTS and 2 VC systems on the corpus. To replicate downstream TTS, train a standard multi-speaker neural TTS on the diacritized text-audio pairs.
- **Key results:** Headline contribution is the dataset itself (83.52h, 11 voices, diacritized MSA). Demonstrations show ArVoice enables training of functional Arabic TTS and voice-conversion systems; specific MOS/WER numbers are reported in the paper's experiments but the primary result is corpus release and usability. (Exact baseline metrics not extracted here.)
- **Notes:** Modern Standard Arabic, fully diacritized. Synthetic component sourced from commercial systems may carry licensing/usage constraints; human-recording portion is the curated core. Hosted on Hugging Face under MBZUAI.

### 27. Bayesian Speech synthesizers Can Learn from Multiple Teachers

_Ziyang Zhang, Yifan Gao, Xuenan Xu, Baoxiang Li, Wen Wu, Chao Zhang · 2025 · arXiv preprint (also OpenReview ADRwyhQWzY)_

- **Categories:** C1, C4, C5, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2510.24372) · arXiv:2510.24372 · [code](https://github.com/OpenTSLab/BELLE)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Central. BELLE synthesizes diverse speech samples from MULTIPLE pre-trained TTS teacher models conditioned on the SAME text-audio prompts, then uses these synthetic samples as a statistical 'support set' to learn reliable output variance from single-reference (one-to-one) datasets. This converts a one-to-one dataset into a one-to-many distribution distilled into BELLE via Bayesian evidential learning, enabling robust aleatoric-uncertainty estimation without extra parameters or latency.
- **Method:** Reframes TTS from deterministic regression to principled Bayesian inference. BELLE (Bayesian Evidential Learning with Language modeling) models acoustic targets as a Normal-Inverse-Gamma distribution to capture data-dependent aleatoric uncertainty. A one-to-many training strategy distills variance information from multiple teacher TTS systems' synthetic outputs into a single LM-based synthesizer.
- **Architecture:** Language-model-style (autoregressive) TTS over acoustic/codec tokens, augmented with an evidential head that predicts Normal-Inverse-Gamma distribution parameters instead of point estimates. Adds no extra parameters or inference latency vs. the deterministic baseline; supports streaming generation. Exact model size not stated in abstract (trained on ~5k hours).
- **Base models:** Multiple pre-trained TTS models serve as teachers to generate synthetic support samples; the synthesizer is an LM-based TTS. Specific teacher identities and the codec/tokenizer not detailed in the abstract.
- **Datasets:** Real training data ~5,000 hours (vs. competitors' ~50,000 hours). Synthetic data: diverse samples generated by multiple pre-trained TTS teachers on the same text-audio prompts, used as a statistical support set. Specific dataset names not reported in abstract.
- **Code:** https://github.com/OpenTSLab/BELLE (demos: https://belletts.github.io/Belle/)
- **Recipe:** 1) Take a single-reference (one-to-one) text-audio dataset (~5k hours). 2) For each text-audio prompt, generate multiple diverse speech samples by running several pre-trained TTS teacher models on the same prompt, building a per-prompt synthetic support set. 3) Train an LM-style TTS where the prediction head outputs Normal-Inverse-Gamma (NIG) evidential parameters rather than point estimates. 4) Use a Bayesian evidential learning loss so the model learns aleatoric variance from the synthetic support-set distribution (one-to-many training), distilling multiple teachers into one student. 5) The evidential formulation adds no parameters and preserves streaming inference. Exact NIG loss weights, codec, and optimizer schedule are in the paper/repo (not in abstract).
- **Key results:** 25.8% relative WER reduction vs. leading open-source models trained on ~10x more data (~50k hours), while using only ~5k hours; supports high-quality streaming generation.
- **Notes:** Verified via arXiv, OpenReview (ADRwyhQWzY), and official GitHub (OpenTSLab/BELLE). Strong multi-teacher synthetic-distillation paper; check repo for exact teacher models, codec, and NIG hyperparameters.

### 28. CosyVoice 3: Towards In-the-wild Speech Generation via Scaling-up and Post-training

_Zhihao Du, Changfeng Gao, et al. (FunAudioLLM / Alibaba Tongyi SpeechTeam) · 2025 · arXiv preprint (FunAudioLLM / Alibaba Tongyi SpeechTeam)_

- **Categories:** C1, C2, C3, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2505.17589) · arXiv:2505.17589 · [code](https://github.com/FunAudioLLM/CosyVoice)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Two roles. (1) Massive in-the-wild data scaled from 10k to 1M hours is collected and pseudo-labeled by an internal ASR/recognition pipeline (the new multi-task speech tokenizer doubles as a recognizer producing transcripts, language ID, emotion, events, speaker tags), i.e. machine-labeled corpus at scale. (2) Post-training uses a differentiable reward model (DiffRO) whose reward signal is computed over the LM-generated speech tokens to optimize the autoregressive TTS LM; the model effectively trains on its own generated/sampled outputs scored by the reward model, which predicts quality dimensions (ASR-based content consistency, speaker, prosody) directly from speech tokens so gradients flow back to the generator.
