- **Method:** Scale CosyVoice 2 up (data 10k to 1M hours, params 0.5B to 1.5B, 9 languages + 18 Chinese dialects), add a new multi-task supervised speech tokenizer for better prosody, and introduce a differentiable reward model (DiffRO) for post-training applicable to any LLM-based TTS. Goal is robust zero-shot in-the-wild multilingual synthesis with better content consistency, speaker similarity, and prosody.
- **Architecture:** LLM-based TTS: autoregressive text-to-speech-token language model (scaled to ~1.5B) + chunk-aware flow-matching (FM) acoustic model for streaming token-to-mel, plus vocoder. New single-codebook speech tokenizer trained via supervised multi-task learning (ASR, speech emotion recognition, language ID, audio event detection, speaker analysis) to inject prosody/semantic info. Bi-streaming low-latency design inherited from CosyVoice 2.
- **Base models:** Builds directly on CosyVoice 2 (LLM + chunk-aware flow matching). Initializes from / extends the CosyVoice 2 0.5B model up to 1.5B. New tokenizer derived from supervised multi-task encoder. DiffRO reward model is newly trained.
- **Datasets:** Real/in-the-wild collected speech expanded from ~10,000 hours (CosyVoice 2) to ~1,000,000 hours, spanning 9 languages and 18 Chinese dialects across many domains and text formats. Evaluated on Seed-TTS-Eval and multilingual sets. Most large-scale data is internally collected and machine-transcribed.
- **Code:** https://github.com/FunAudioLLM/CosyVoice ; HF: https://huggingface.co/FunAudioLLM/Fun-CosyVoice3-0.5B-2512 ; demo https://funaudiollm.github.io/cosyvoice3
- **Recipe:** Stage 1 pretrain LM + flow-matching on ~1M hours machine-labeled multilingual/dialect speech using the new multi-task speech tokenizer (trained with ASR+SER+LID+AED+speaker heads). Stage 2 post-train the autoregressive TTS LM with DiffRO: train a differentiable reward model over discrete speech tokens predicting content/speaker/prosody quality, then optimize generator so its sampled token sequences maximize reward (gradient passes through reward model). Scale params 0.5B->1.5B. Replicate by: collect/ASR-label large multilingual corpus, train multi-task tokenizer, train CosyVoice2-style LM+FM, then add reward-model post-training.
- **Key results:** Reported to surpass CosyVoice 2 on content consistency, speaker similarity, prosody naturalness; on Seed-TTS-Eval the larger variant reaches roughly ~1% CER (zh) / low single-digit WER (en). Qwen3-TTS later reports beating it (cross-lingual zh->ko 14.4 WER for CosyVoice 3). Exact numbers in paper tables; abstract gives qualitative gains plus DiffRO improving both objective and subjective metrics.
- **Notes:** Differentiable reward model is the headline post-training contribution (community/follow-ups call it DiffRO). Demo and 0.5B checkpoint public; larger 1.5B in-the-wild model is internal. Not classic DPO/PPO but a differentiable reward-gradient method, hence category 3.

### 29. Data-efficient Targeted Token-level Preference Optimization for LLM-based Text-to-Speech (TKTO)

_Rikuto Kotoge, Yuichi Sasaki · 2025 · ACL 2026 (Main Conference)_

- **Categories:** C2, C3
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2510.05799) · arXiv:2510.05799
- **Synthetic-data role:** Removes the need for paired desirable/undesirable preference samples. Instead of curating human-annotated preference pairs or large synthetic preference datasets, TKTO derives fine-grained, token-level alignment signals automatically (without token-level human annotations), making preference data acquisition far more data-efficient. The preference supervision is automatically constructed/targeted rather than collected as paired synthetic utterances.
- **Method:** TKTO is a token-level preference-optimization method for LLM-based TTS that drops the standard utterance-level paired-data requirement. It automatically targets individual token units, assigning much stronger reward to the targeted (error-prone, e.g. mispronounced) tokens, giving fine-grained alignment signals that directly improve pronunciation accuracy without manual token annotations.
- **Architecture:** LLM-based (autoregressive token) TTS as the policy; a token-level preference/alignment objective (DPO/KTO-style but unpaired and token-targeted) applied over the discrete speech/text tokens. Specific backbone TTS model not detailed on the abstract page.
- **Base models:** An existing LLM-based TTS model fine-tuned with TKTO (specific base model not stated on the abstract page; not reported).
- **Datasets:** Japanese TTS evaluation setting (pronunciation accuracy / CER). Specific corpus names and hours not stated on the abstract page; not reported.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Start from a pretrained LLM-based TTS that emits discrete tokens. 2) Instead of collecting paired (preferred/dispreferred) utterances, use an unpaired, token-level preference objective: automatically identify targeted tokens (e.g., those tied to pronunciation errors) and assign them substantially larger reward weight (~12.8x stronger reward to targeted tokens) without any token-level human annotation. 3) Optimize the TTS policy with this targeted token-level preference loss, providing fine-grained alignment signals on the problematic units. 4) Evaluate pronunciation/accuracy via CER on Japanese TTS. Exact hyperparameters, base model, and reward construction are in the full paper.
- **Key results:** 39% improvement in Japanese TTS accuracy and a 54% reduction in CER versus the baseline; the method automatically assigns ~12.8x stronger reward to targeted tokens, all without paired preference data or token-level annotations.
- **Notes:** Accepted to ACL 2026 Main Conference. Data-efficiency is the headline: eliminates paired preference data and token-level annotation. Base model and dataset names need the full PDF for confirmation.

### 30. Differentiable Reward Optimization for LLM-based TTS system

_Changfeng Gao, Zhihao Du, Shiliang Zhang · 2025 · arXiv preprint_

- **Categories:** C2, C3, C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05911) · arXiv:2507.05911
- **Synthetic-data role:** The multi-task reward model is trained on 13,000+ hours of audio with pseudo-labels generated from existing models (pseudo-labeled for ASR, emotion, quality, age/gender). The RL/optimization corpus is 10,000 internet-sourced texts (~90% ZH/EN, rest JA/KO) used to drive the TTS model's own codec-token generation, on which differentiable rewards are computed. So both the reward supervision (pseudo-labels) and the optimization targets (model-generated tokens) are synthetic.
- **Method:** DiffRO: instead of RL on synthesized waveforms, compute rewards directly on neural codec tokens and use Gumbel-Softmax to make the reward differentiable, enabling end-to-end backprop. A multi-task reward (MTR) model provides ASR/emotion/quality/age-gender feedback and enables zero-shot attribute control.
- **Architecture:** Neural-codec LLM TTS (CosyVoice2.0-0.5B). Gumbel-Softmax differentiable layer over codec tokens. Multi-task reward model with ASR, SER (emotion), SQA (quality), AED (age/gender) heads.
- **Base models:** CosyVoice2.0-0.5B as base TTS (fine-tuned with 4,000 samples from 5 Mandarin speakers, 4F/1M).
- **Datasets:** Reward model: 13,000+ h audio with model-generated pseudo-labels. RL data: 10,000 internet texts (90% ZH/EN, rest JA/KO). Eval: seed-tts-eval (Seed-TTS zh, CommonVoice en, Hard set).
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Train MTR reward model (ASR/SER/SQA/AED heads) on 13k+ h pseudo-labeled audio. 2) Optimize CosyVoice2.0-0.5B with DiffRO: sample codec tokens via Gumbel-Softmax (differentiable), feed reconstructed/token-level outputs to MTR, backprop differentiable reward; beta=0.1, lr 1e-5, 4x A800 GPUs, RL data 10k texts.
- **Key results:** CosyVoice2.0 + DiffRO-ASR: 0.78% WER Seed-TTS zh (SOTA), 1.89% CMV en, 5.58% hard. DiffRO-MTR enables emotion control: classification accuracy 100%/92%/84% for happy/sad/angry (Chinese), with WER 1.05% zh / 3.43% en / 6.41% hard.
- **Notes:** Differentiable-reward (Gumbel-Softmax on codec tokens) replaces standard RL loops; avoids vocoder in the reward path. No public code found.

### 31. Direct Preference Optimization for Speech Autoregressive Diffusion Models (ARDM-DPO)

_Zhijun Liu, Dongya Jia, Xiaoqiang Wang, Chenpeng Du, Shuai Wang, Zhuo Chen, Haizhou Li · 2025 · arXiv preprint_

- **Categories:** C2, C3, C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2509.18928) · arXiv:2509.18928 · [code](https://zjlww.github.io/ardm-dpo/)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Preference pairs are entirely synthetic/self-generated from the base DiTAR model. Task A (expressiveness): generate 32 candidate speech responses per prompt-text pair, pick best/worst by F0 variance, yielding 256k preference pairs (~1,000 hours). Task B (robustness on long/repetitive text): generate 16 candidates per prompt, score with a phoneme-based CTC model (negative log-likelihood / text likelihood), pick best/worst, yielding 430k preference pairs (~3,500 hours). No human preference labels; automatic metrics select winners/losers among generated samples.
- **Method:** Adapts DPO to autoregressive diffusion TTS (continuous-token diffusion rather than discrete codec tokens). Defines a DPO formulation (ARDM-DPO) suitable for the diffusion-head likelihood and fine-tunes DiTAR using self-generated, automatically-ranked preference pairs to improve expressiveness (F0 variance) and robustness on long/repetitive text.
- **Architecture:** DiTAR zero-shot TTS: ~0.4B params, autoregressive LM of 24 transformer blocks (1024 hidden, 16 heads) plus a 4-block diffusion head generating continuous speech tokens via v-prediction over continuous time t in [0,1]. Sampling with 16-step DDPM, LM guidance w=2.
- **Base models:** DiTAR (autoregressive diffusion zero-shot TTS, ~0.4B params, pretrained on ~280k hours Chinese+English).
- **Datasets:** Base DiTAR: ~280,000 hours Chinese+English audio. Task A preference data from LibriTTS (eval: 38 English test cases). Task B from DidiSpeech-2 prompts + 100k Chinese sentences with repetitive text (eval: 400 hard Chinese test cases).
- **Code:** Project/demo page: https://zjlww.github.io/ardm-dpo/ (no code repo confirmed)
- **Recipe:** 1) Generate candidates from base DiTAR. Task A: 32 candidates/prompt, rank by F0 variance -> 256k pairs (~1k hrs). Task B: 16 candidates/prompt, rank by phoneme CTC NLL -> 430k pairs (~3.5k hrs). 2) ARDM-DPO fine-tune on 32 A100 GPUs: effective batch 1024 pairs (local 1 + grad accumulation 32), AdamW LR 2e-6, weight decay 0.01, beta1 0.9, beta2 0.95. 3) Inference: 16-step DDPM, linear schedule, LM guidance w=2.
- **Key results:** Task A (expressiveness): F0 variance 14.2->29.2 (~2x), WER 5.17%->3.73%, SIM 0.770->0.765. Task B (robustness): CER 8.37%->6.32% (~25% relative reduction), SIM 0.711->0.712, naturalness ~88.7% tie with base. Significant expressiveness gains with minor naturalness/similarity trade-off.
- **Notes:** Novel in applying DPO to continuous-token autoregressive diffusion TTS (vs prior discrete-token DPO work). Demo page available; no open-source code repo confirmed.

### 32. DMOSpeech 2: Reinforcement Learning for Duration Prediction in Metric-Optimized Speech Synthesis

_Yinghao Aaron Li, Xilin Jiang, Fei Tao, Cheng Niu, Kaifeng Xu, Juntong Song, Nima Mesgarani · 2025 · arXiv preprint (also AAAI proceedings entry found)_

- **Categories:** C2, C3, C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.14988) · arXiv:2507.14988 · [code](https://dmospeech2.github.io/)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Self-generated/on-policy data for RL: during GRPO fine-tuning the duration predictor samples groups of candidate durations (group size 16), the diffusion model synthesizes speech from each, and an ASR model (WER) plus a speaker-verification model (SIM) score the synthetic outputs as reward signals. The synthetic speech is not stored as a corpus; it is generated on-the-fly to compute preferences. Teacher-guided (hybrid) sampling also uses the teacher F5-TTS to guide the distilled student's generation trajectory.
- **Method:** Extends metric optimization from acoustic generation to the previously-unoptimized duration predictor in a distilled diffusion TTS pipeline. A duration policy is trained with Group Relative Policy Optimization (GRPO) using directly-optimizable metrics (speaker similarity and WER) as rewards. Adds teacher-guided sampling that blends teacher and student denoising to recover diversity lost in distillation while keeping few-step efficiency.
- **Architecture:** Diffusion/flow-matching acoustic model (DMOSpeech-style distilled student of F5-TTS, ~300M-param teacher) + neural audio codec/mel representation; separate duration predictor module trained as an RL policy; ASR model and speaker-verification (SV) model serve as reward/metric models. Distilled few-step (50% fewer sampling steps) sampler.
- **Base models:** Teacher: F5-TTS (~300M params, trained ~2M steps on Emilia). Distilled student initialized from the DMOSpeech distillation of that teacher. Duration predictor pretrained on Emilia (~85K steps) then GRPO fine-tuned (~1.5K steps). External reward models: an ASR system (for WER) and a speaker-verification embedding model (for SIM).
- **Datasets:** Real: Emilia (large-scale multilingual speech corpus) for teacher and duration-predictor pretraining; standard English (and multilingual) eval sets for WER/SIM. No external synthetic corpus collected; RL rollouts are generated online.
- **Code:** https://dmospeech2.github.io/ (audio samples, code, pretrained models)
- **Recipe:** 1) Train/obtain F5-TTS teacher (~300M params) for ~2M steps on Emilia. 2) Distill into a few-step student (DMOSpeech-style metric-optimized diffusion). 3) Pretrain the duration predictor on Emilia for ~85K steps. 4) GRPO fine-tune the duration predictor for ~1.5K steps with group size 16: sample 16 candidate durations per prompt, synthesize speech, score each with WER (ASR) and SIM (speaker verification), compute group-relative advantages, update the duration policy. 5) At inference, use teacher-guided hybrid sampling (blend teacher + student denoising) to restore diversity while cutting sampling steps ~50%.
- **Key results:** English eval: WER 1.752, SIM 0.698. Beats F5-TTS teacher (WER 1.947, SIM 0.662) and a no-RL student (WER 3.750, SIM 0.672). ~50% reduction in sampling steps with no quality degradation.
- **Notes:** GRPO reward is verifiable/metric-based (WER, SIM) rather than human preference. Duration prediction RL is the novel axis vs the original DMOSpeech which optimized only acoustic generation.

### 33. Efficient Emotion and Speaker Adaptation in LLM-Based TTS via Characteristic-Specific Partial Fine-Tuning

_Tianrui Wang, Meng Ge, Cheng Gong, Chunyu Qiang, Haoyu Wang, Zikang Huang, Yu Jiang, Ye Ni, Yuheng Lu, Xiaobao Wang, Eng Siong Chng, Xie Chen, Longbiao Wang, Jianwu Dang · 2025 · arXiv preprint (v1 titled 'Characteristic-Specific Partial Fine-Tuning for Efficient Emotion and Speaker Adaptation in Codec Language Text-to-Speech Models')_

- **Categories:** C2
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2501.14273) · arXiv:2501.14273
- **Synthetic-data role:** No synthetic/generated speech is used. This is a parameter-efficient fine-tuning method evaluated on a combined corpus of 11 real datasets for emotion and speaker adaptation; synthetic data plays no role. Included for completeness; it is an adaptation/fine-tuning paper, not a synthetic-data paper.
- **Method:** Proposes CSP-FT (Characteristic-Specific Partial Fine-Tuning): instead of full fine-tuning of an LLM-based (codec language) TTS model for emotion/speaker adaptation, it dynamically analyzes per-layer contributions to a given characteristic (emotion or speaker) via a weighted sum, then selectively fine-tunes only two layers: the one capturing the MOST relevant information (to maximize its utility) and the one capturing the LEAST (to explicitly strengthen its capacity), leaving the rest frozen.
- **Architecture:** LLM-based / codec language TTS. Built on CosyVoice, which uses a Whisper-like speech encoder, supervised semantic tokens, an autoregressive transformer language model over codec/semantic tokens, plus an added speaker embedding input. CSP-FT updates only ~8% of parameters (two selected transformer layers per characteristic).
- **Base models:** CosyVoice (FunAudioLLM family) zero-shot multilingual codec LM TTS used as the base/pretrained model.
- **Datasets:** A combined corpus of 11 (real) emotion and speaker datasets for adaptation and evaluation; specific dataset names/hours not enumerated in the abstract. No synthetic data.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Start from pretrained CosyVoice LLM-TTS. 2) For the target characteristic (emotion or speaker), probe each transformer layer's contribution via a weighted-sum analysis of layer representations. 3) Identify the highest-contribution layer and lowest-contribution layer for that characteristic. 4) Freeze all other layers; fine-tune ONLY those two layers (~8% of params) on the adaptation data. 5) The high-info layer is tuned to maximize utility; the low-info layer is tuned to strengthen its capacity for the characteristic. Reported ~2x training speedup vs full FT and strongly reduced catastrophic forgetting. Exact LR/steps/batch not stated in fetched content.
- **Key results:** Matches or exceeds full fine-tuning on fidelity, intelligibility, speaker similarity, and emotion recognition while updating only ~8% of parameters, achieving ~2x training acceleration and significantly mitigating catastrophic forgetting on previously seen data/domains.
- **Notes:** Title and v1/v2 versions confirmed on arXiv. Paper is about efficient fine-tuning (LoRA-like selective layer tuning), not synthetic data; categorize as fine-tuning (2) only loosely. No public code found.

### 34. Emilia: A Large-Scale, Extensive, Multilingual, and Diverse Dataset for Speech Generation

_Haorui He, Zengqiang Shang, Chaoren Wang, Xuyuan Li, Yicheng Gu, Hua Hua, Liwei Liu, Chen Yang, Jiaqi Li, Peiyang Shi, Yuancheng Wang, Kai Chen, Pengyuan Zhang, Zhizheng Wu · 2025 · arXiv (extended journal version of the SLT 2024 Emilia paper)_

- **Categories:** C4, C5, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2501.15907) · arXiv:2501.15907 · [code](https://huggingface.co/datasets/amphion/Emilia-Dataset)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Same as the SLT version: pseudo-labeling / automatic annotation of real in-the-wild audio. Transcripts (Whisper ASR), language tags, diarization labels and segmentation are machine-generated; audio is real. The extended Emilia-Large doubles down with 216k+ hours of automatically annotated in-the-wild speech.
- **Method:** Extended journal version introducing Emilia-Pipe (open-source six-step preprocessing pipeline) and the expanded Emilia / Emilia-Large datasets, built to capture spontaneous, real-world conversational speech rather than formal audiobook speech, for large-scale speech generation.
- **Architecture:** Data-construction pipeline (no new generative model). Same six-stage Emilia-Pipe: standardization, source separation, pyannote diarization, Silero-VAD segmentation, Whisper-medium ASR + language ID, DNSMOS P.835 + duration filtering.
- **Base models:** Pipeline uses source-separation model, pyannote diarization, Silero-VAD, Whisper-medium (WhisperX/faster-whisper), DNSMOS P.835. Not a trained model itself.
- **Datasets:** Emilia: 101k+ hours; Emilia-Large: 216k+ hours total. Six languages: English, Chinese, German, French, Japanese, Korean. Sourced from in-the-wild audio.
- **Code:** https://huggingface.co/datasets/amphion/Emilia-Dataset ; pipeline: https://github.com/open-mmlab/Amphion (preprocessors/Emilia)
- **Recipe:** Identical six-step Emilia-Pipe: 1) Standardize to mono 24 kHz 16-bit WAV, loudness -20 dBFS. 2) Source separation (vocals vs background). 3) pyannote speaker diarization to single-speaker segments. 4) Silero-VAD fine-grained segmentation into 3-30 s clips. 5) Whisper-medium ASR (WhisperX/CTranslate2) for transcript + language tag. 6) Filter on language-ID confidence >80%, DNSMOS P.835 OVRL >3.0, and plausible char/phone durations; export JSON + MP3. For Emilia-Large, scale raw-audio collection to reach 216k+ hours. Train speech-generation models on resulting (audio, pseudo-transcript) pairs.
- **Key results:** Provides 101k h (Emilia) / 216k+ h (Emilia-Large) across six languages, among the largest open speech-gen resources. Models trained on Emilia generate markedly more spontaneous, human-like speech with intelligibility comparable to audiobook-trained models, and support diverse timbres, multilingual and crosslingual generation (detailed WER/MOS in paper).
- **Notes:** Extended version of arXiv:2407.05361. Adds Emilia-Large (216k h) and expanded analysis. Open dataset + open-source pipeline; data sourced in-the-wild, research-use licensing; real audio with machine-generated labels.

### 35. EMORL-TTS: Reinforcement Learning for Fine-Grained Emotion Control in LLM-based TTS

_Haoxun Li, Yu Liu, Yuqing Sun, Hanlei Shi, Leyuan Qu, Taihao Li · 2025 · ICASSP 2026 (accepted)_

- **Categories:** C3, C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2510.05758) · arXiv:2510.05758
- **Synthetic-data role:** Primary role is RL-generated rollouts rather than a pre-built synthetic corpus: during RL the LLM-TTS policy samples speech scored by task-specific reward models (emotion classification, global VAD-based intensity, local emphasis). No large external synthetic dataset generation reported; the 'synthetic' aspect is on-policy generated speech used for the reward signal.
- **Method:** Fine-grained emotion-controllable TTS that unifies global emotional intensity control in continuous VAD (valence-arousal-dominance) space with local emphasis regulation. Combines supervised fine-tuning with RL driven by multiple task-specific rewards to overcome the coarse categorical emotion control of discrete-token LLM-TTS.
- **Architecture:** LLM-based (discrete speech token) TTS backbone. SFT stage plus RL stage with multiple reward models: an emotion classifier, a global VAD-space intensity predictor, and a local emphasis controller. Backbone sizes not disclosed.
- **Base models:** Builds on an existing LLM-based TTS system; specific base model name not reported in the abstract.
- **Datasets:** Dataset names, sizes, and hours not reported in the available abstract/HTML.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** Two-stage: (1) supervised fine-tuning of the LLM-TTS for emotion conditioning; (2) reinforcement learning guided by task-specific rewards for (a) emotion category accuracy, (b) global emotion intensity in VAD space, (c) local emphasis control. Rewards combined to enhance fine-grained controllability while preserving synthesis quality. Specific hyperparameters not disclosed.
- **Key results:** Objective and subjective evaluations show substantial improvements in emotion accuracy, intensity differentiation, and emphasis clarity over strong LLM-based baselines, while preserving comparable synthesis quality; stable across emotion categories with distinguishable intensity levels.
- **Notes:** Accepted to ICASSP 2026 (submitted Oct 2025, revised Jan 2026). VAD = valence-arousal-dominance. Limited public hyperparameter/dataset disclosure; no code repo located.

### 36. Emotion-Aligned Generation in Diffusion Text to Speech Models via Preference-Guided Optimization

_Jiacheng Shi, Hongfei Du, Yangfan He, Y. Alicia Hong, Ye Gao · 2025 · Accepted to ICASSP 2026 (submitted Sep 2025; revised Feb 2026)_

- **Categories:** C3, C2, C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2509.25416) · arXiv:2509.25416
- **Synthetic-data role:** Preference pairs for emotional alignment are constructed automatically (not human-labeled). A learned time-conditioned scoring model (EASPM) scores noisy intermediate diffusion states, and these scores are used to synthesize/select preferred vs less-preferred (chosen/rejected) trajectories at intermediate denoising steps. The synthetic signal is the auto-generated stepwise preference annotation derived from the scorer rather than from coarse emotion labels or external proxy classifiers; this preference data drives the post-training optimization.
- **Method:** Emotion-Aware Stepwise Preference Optimization (EASPO): a post-training framework that aligns a diffusion-based TTS model with fine-grained emotional preferences at intermediate denoising steps. A time-conditioned scoring model (EASPM) scores noisy intermediate speech states to automatically build stepwise preference pairs, and stepwise preference optimization is applied across denoising stages for controllable emotional shaping, avoiding reliance on coarse labels or proxy classifiers.
- **Architecture:** Diffusion-based text-to-speech acoustic model (denoising-diffusion generative backbone operating over multiple denoising steps) plus an auxiliary EASPM scoring model that is time/step-conditioned to evaluate noisy intermediate states. Specific layer counts and parameter sizes are not reported in the abstract.
- **Base models:** Not reported precisely; builds on an existing diffusion-based TTS model as the policy to be post-trained. Exact pretrained backbone not stated in the available abstract.
- **Datasets:** Not reported in the available abstract; emotional speech corpora are implied but specific dataset names/hours were not extractable from the abstract.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** High level (only abstract-level detail available): (1) Start from a pretrained diffusion TTS model. (2) Train EASPM, a time-conditioned scorer that assigns emotion-alignment scores to noisy intermediate denoising states. (3) Use EASPM to automatically construct stepwise preference pairs (preferred vs less-preferred intermediate states) without coarse emotion labels or external classifiers. (4) Apply stepwise preference optimization across denoising stages to align generation toward preferred emotional shaping. Concrete hyperparameters, loss form, training steps, and dataset are not given in the abstract and would require the full PDF.
- **Key results:** Reported as superior performance over existing methods in both expressiveness and naturalness; specific numeric metrics (MOS/CMOS/WER) and named baselines were not available in the abstract.
- **Notes:** Verified via arXiv abs page. The novelty is stepwise (intermediate-denoising-step) preference optimization rather than terminal-output DPO, with an auto-scoring model replacing human/coarse-label preferences. Quantitative tables not extractable without the full paper PDF; many fields are abstract-level only.

### 37. EmoVoice: LLM-based Emotional Text-To-Speech Model with Freestyle Text Prompting

_Guanrou Yang, Chen Yang, Qian Chen, Ziyang Ma, Wenxi Chen, Wen Wang, Tianrui Wang, Yifan Yang, Zhikang Niu, Wenrui Liu, Fan Yu, Zhihao Du, Zhifu Gao, ShiLiang Zhang, Xie Chen · 2025 · ACM MM 2025 (33rd ACM International Conference on Multimedia)_

- **Categories:** C4, C2, C7, C6, C1
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2504.12867) · arXiv:2504.12867 · [code](https://github.com/yanghaha0908/EmoVoice)
- **Synthetic-data role:** The flagship emotional dataset EmoVoice-DB is fully synthetic: emotion-rich transcripts and natural-language emotion descriptions (15-25 words, sensory detail) are generated by GPT-4o, and the corresponding expressive speech is synthesized by prompting the GPT-4o-audio model. The corpus totals about 40.45 hours / 22,100 samples across 7 emotions, quality-filtered by WER between generated audio and intended transcript. The English model achieves SOTA using ONLY this synthetic training data for the emotional fine-tuning stage (alongside ~200h of real LAION's Got Talent for diversity).
- **Method:** An LLM-based emotional TTS that supports freestyle natural-language emotion prompting (arbitrary descriptive control rather than fixed labels). A 'phoneme boost' variant (EmoVoice-PP) outputs phoneme tokens and audio tokens in parallel, inspired by chain-of-thought / chain-of-modality, to improve content consistency. Trained largely on GPT-4o-generated synthetic emotional speech.
- **Architecture:** Autoregressive LLM backbone (Qwen2.5-0.5B: 24 layers ~0.49B params; and Qwen2.5-1.5B: 28 layers ~1.54B params) predicting 50Hz CosyVoice semantic tokens, converted to waveform via flow matching + HiFi-GAN vocoder. EmoVoice-PP adds parallel phoneme-token prediction (~11Hz phonemes guiding ~17Hz audio tokens). Built on the SLAM-LLM framework.
- **Base models:** Qwen2.5-0.5B / Qwen2.5-1.5B LLM backbones; CosyVoice semantic token codec + flow matching + HiFi-GAN vocoder for audio reconstruction; GPT-4o and GPT-4o-audio used as data generators (not as the runtime model). Code built on SLAM-LLM.
- **Datasets:** Pretraining: VoiceAssistant (English, 3,234h) and Belle (Chinese, 6,418h). Emotional fine-tuning: EmoVoice-DB (synthetic, 40.45h / 22,100 samples, 7 emotions) plus part of LAION's Got Talent (~200h, real in-the-wild). Evaluation: English EmoVoice-DB test set and Chinese Secap test set.
- **Code:** https://github.com/yanghaha0908/EmoVoice (checkpoints: https://huggingface.co/yhaha/EmoVoice ; dataset: https://huggingface.co/datasets/yhaha/EmoVoice-DB ; demo: https://yanghaha0908.github.io/EmoVoice/)
- **Recipe:** Data generation: (1) Prompt GPT-4o to produce emotional transcripts and 15-25-word natural-language emotion descriptions across 7 emotions (angry, happy, sad, surprised, fearful, disgusted, neutral). (2) Synthesize speech by prompting GPT-4o-audio. (3) Filter samples by WER between synthesized audio and intended transcript, yielding EmoVoice-DB (40.45h / 22,100). Training (two-stage): Stage 1 pretrain TTS with neutral prompts on VoiceAssistant + Belle, peak LR 1e-4. Stage 2 fine-tune for emotional TTS with natural-language emotion descriptions on EmoVoice-DB + LAION's Got Talent (~200h), LR 1e-5. Group size G=3, batch size 6, 4xA800 GPUs. EmoVoice-PP variant trains the LLM to emit phoneme tokens and CosyVoice audio tokens in parallel for content consistency. Inference: LLM generates semantic tokens conditioned on text + freestyle emotion prompt; flow matching + HiFi-GAN reconstruct waveform. License: code MIT; pretrained models CC-BY-NC due to Emilia training data.
- **Key results:** English EmoVoice-DB: WER 2.73% (0.5B) / 2.62% (1.5B) vs CosyVoice2 3.61% and GPT-4o-mini 2.40%; emotion similarity 0.9100 / 0.9118 vs CosyVoice2 0.8647; recall 0.395 / 0.424; UTMOS 4.36 / 4.35; human MOS 3.163 (0.5B) / 3.507 (1.5B) vs CosyVoice2 2.138 and GPT-4o-mini 3.598. Chinese Secap (EmoVoice-PP): WER 7.60%, emotion similarity 0.7939, recall 0.434. EmoVoice-PP improves WER, emotion similarity, and recall over the base variant.
- **Notes:** Verified via arXiv, GitHub, HF dataset card, ACM MM proceedings. Strong, clean example of category 4/7: a fully synthetic GPT-4o + GPT-4o-audio emotional corpus that alone reaches SOTA on English. Note licensing: pretrained models CC-BY-NC (Emilia in-the-wild data); EmoVoice-DB redistributable per HF card. Paper also studies reliability of emotion metrics using GPT-4o-audio and Gemini as judges.

### 38. Explore the Reinforcement Learning for the LLM based ASR and TTS system

_Changfeng Gao, Yabin Li, Keyu An, Zhifu Gao, Zhihao Du, Han Zhao, Xiangang Li · 2025 · arXiv preprint (Alibaba FunAudioLLM/CosyVoice team), Sept 2025_

- **Categories:** C2, C3
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2509.18569) · arXiv:2509.18569
- **Synthetic-data role:** Mostly RL post-training rather than synthetic-data training. For TTS, DiffRO uses a token-based ASR system as a differentiable reward: the policy generates speech tokens whose ASR posterior probability provides the reward, so generated speech is scored (not stored as a labeled corpus). The combined GRPO+DiffRO recipe uses sample-filtering of the model's own generations to balance WER vs speaker similarity. No large offline synthetic corpus is built; the synthetic element is the on-policy generated audio used for reward computation.
- **Method:** A lightweight RL framework for audio-LLMs that improves ASR and TTS with few optimization steps: GRPO with rule-based rewards for ASR, and a comparison/combination of GRPO with Differentiable Reward Optimization (DiffRO) for TTS.
- **Architecture:** ASR: FunAudio-ASR, a 0.7B audio encoder feeding a Qwen2.5-7B LLM decoder. TTS: CosyVoice2-0.5B (autoregressive speech-token LM + flow-matching/codec decoder). DiffRO uses Gumbel-Softmax sampling over speech tokens with a token-based ASR reward model enabling gradient backprop.
- **Base models:** FunAudio-ASR (0.7B encoder + Qwen2.5-7B LLM) for ASR; CosyVoice2-0.5B for TTS; a token-based ASR system as the differentiable reward model for DiffRO.
- **Datasets:** ASR RL: four 20k-utterance subsets (hard samples, long audio >20s, keyword-containing speech, random selection). TTS RL: text from CommonVoice Chinese and English. TTS eval: CV3-Eval test set.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** ASR: 1) Start from FunAudio-ASR (0.7B encoder + Qwen2.5-7B). 2) Build RL data as 20k-utterance subsets selecting hard/long/keyword/random samples. 3) Apply GRPO with rule-based rewards: R1 = 1-WER accuracy; R2 = hallucination penalty (-1 for repeated/non-existent/translated tokens); R3 = keyword precision/recall average. TTS: 1) Start from CosyVoice2-0.5B. 2) Use CommonVoice zh/en text prompts. 3) DiffRO: sample speech tokens with Gumbel-Softmax, feed to token-based ASR, use ASR posterior P_ASR as differentiable reward, backprop through it; add an audio-duration reward to prevent slow speech. 4) Compare with GRPO, then combine GRPO+DiffRO with sample filtering to balance intelligibility and speaker similarity. RL converges in a small number of steps even with limited data.
- **Key results:** ASR: ~5.3% relative WER reduction on both short and long speech, with notable insertion-error/hallucination reduction. TTS: DiffRO yields the largest WER improvement but degrades speaker similarity more; the combined sample-filtered GRPO+DiffRO gives balanced gains across WER, speaker similarity, and duration on CV3-Eval. Demonstrates RL effectiveness for audio-LLMs with few optimization steps and limited data.
- **Notes:** From the FunAudioLLM/CosyVoice (Alibaba) ecosystem. Strong category-3 (RL/GRPO/preference-style reward) paper for TTS; DiffRO is the audio-specific differentiable analogue. No official code link surfaced.

### 39. F5R-TTS: Improving Flow-Matching based Text-to-Speech with Group Relative Policy Optimization

_Xiaohui Sun, Ruitong Xiao, Jianye Mo, Bowen Wu, Qun Yu, Baoxun Wang · 2025 · arXiv preprint_

- **Categories:** C2, C3, C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2504.02407) · arXiv:2504.02407 · [code](https://github.com/FrontierLabs/F5R-TTS)
- **Synthetic-data role:** In the GRPO/RL stage the model self-generates groups of speech samples (zero-shot voice-cloning outputs) from input text + reference audio; these synthesized candidates are pseudo-labeled with automatic rewards, WER from an ASR model and SIM from a speaker-verification model. The model's own generations plus these model-derived rewards form the entire RL training signal, with no additional human-labeled data. Synthetic/self-generated data is thus used for online policy improvement rather than corpus construction.
- **Method:** Reformulate the deterministic flow-matching outputs of F5-TTS into probabilistic (Gaussian) distributions so that the model defines an explicit policy, enabling GRPO reinforcement learning with ASR (WER) and speaker-verification (SIM) rewards to improve intelligibility and speaker similarity.
- **Architecture:** Flow-matching based non-autoregressive TTS (F5-TTS lineage: Diffusion-Transformer / DiT-style flow-matching acoustic model with ConvNeXt text encoding, vocoder for waveform), modified so each step outputs a Gaussian (mean+variance) making the trajectory a sampleable stochastic policy for RL.
- **Base models:** Derived from / reformulated from F5-TTS; uses pretrained ASR (for WER reward) and speaker-verification model (for SIM reward) as frozen reward functions.
- **Datasets:** Pretraining on an open-source dataset (F5-TTS pipeline uses Emilia; the repo provides scripts/prepare_emilia.py and Wenetspeech4TTS examples). Exact hours in the paper not stated in abstract; evaluation on zero-shot voice cloning.
- **Code:** https://github.com/FrontierLabs/F5R-TTS (samples: https://frontierlabs.github.io/F5R)
- **Recipe:** Stage 1 (pretrain): train a probabilistically reformulated flow-matching TTS from F5-TTS on an open-source corpus (Emilia-style prep), where the network predicts a Gaussian per flow step instead of a deterministic vector field, yielding a log-probability for sampled trajectories. Stage 2 (GRPO): for each (text, reference-audio) prompt, sample a group of G generations from the stochastic policy; compute dual rewards, negative WER via ASR and SIM via speaker verification, normalize within the group to get relative advantages, and update with the GRPO objective (group-relative advantage, KL regularization to the reference flow model). Combine the two rewards into the scalar reward. Detailed group size/KL/learning rate are in the repo/paper.
- **Key results:** On zero-shot voice cloning vs conventional (deterministic) flow-matching TTS: ~29.5% relative WER reduction and ~4.6% relative SIM increase.
- **Notes:** Main novelty is making flow-matching probabilistic so policy-gradient RL (GRPO) is applicable; transfers the LLM GRPO recipe to non-autoregressive acoustic models. Official code released by FrontierLabs.

### 40. Fine-grained Preference Optimization Improves Zero-shot Text-to-Speech

_Jixun Yao, Yuguang Yang, Yu Pan, Yuan Feng, Ziqian Ning, Jianhao Ye, Hongbin Zhou, Lei Xie · 2025 · arXiv preprint (Northwestern Polytechnical University / Ximalaya Everest Team)_

- **Categories:** C3, C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2502.02950) · arXiv:2502.02950 · [code](https://yaoxunji.github.io/fpo)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Preference data is fully self-generated by the base TTS model: multiple inferences per transcript are produced by varying sampling hyperparameters, then scored by an automatic composite reward (intelligibility, quality, speaker similarity, duration) to form winner/loser pairs (margin threshold tau=0.3). Each generated sample is further auto-annotated at the token level into fine-grained issue types (using Whisper-timestamped, VAD, LLM prosody analysis, ASR, forced alignment), so synthetic samples carry localized error labels used by a selective DPO loss.
- **Method:** FPO (Fine-grained Preference Optimization): instead of optimizing the whole utterance, it localizes the problematic tokens in self-generated samples, categorizes errors into two types, and applies a token-selective DPO loss that only penalizes the problematic tokens, improving robustness and data efficiency for zero-shot TTS.
- **Architecture:** CosyVoice backbone: neural-codec-based decoder-only language model predicting discrete acoustic tokens via next-token prediction, conditioned on phoneme input and prompt speech, plus codec decoder/vocoder. Sizes not explicitly reported.
- **Base models:** CosyVoice, pretrained on ~170k hours multilingual speech, used as both policy and reference model. Auxiliary tools: Whisper-timestamped, a VAD, forced aligner, ASR, and an LLM for prosody analysis (annotation only, not trained).
- **Datasets:** Base CosyVoice training: LibriTTS and AISHELL-3 (already used by base model). Preference set: 1,000 self-generated utterance pairs for main experiments (data-efficiency swept 200-5,000). Evaluation in English and Mandarin Chinese.
- **Code:** https://yaoxunji.github.io/fpo (demo page); code repository not explicitly stated
- **Recipe:** 1) Start from pretrained CosyVoice. 2) Generate multiple candidates per transcript by varying sampling hyperparameters. 3) Score each with composite reward s(y)=lambda_w*w(y)^p + lambda_m*m(y)^p + lambda_c*c(y)^p + lambda_d*Dur(y)^p; keep pairs with score gap > tau=0.3 as (y_w, y_l). 4) Auto-annotate token-level issues into two categories: (a) temporal-modeling errors (mispronunciation, abnormal silence, unnatural prosody) via Whisper-timestamped + VAD + LLM prosody analysis; (b) semantic-phonetic alignment errors (repetitions, truncations) via ASR + forced alignment, marking all post-error tokens as problematic. 5) Train selective token-level DPO loss with indicator I(y_i) selecting only problematic tokens, KL coefficient beta. 6) Use ~1,000 pairs; evaluate WER/CER, bad-case ratio.
- **Key results:** CosyVoice -> FPO: CER (CN) 8.26 -> 3.92 (-52.5%), WER (EN) 6.97 -> 3.15 (-54.8%); bad-case ratio CN 31% -> 8% (~73% reduction), EN 24% -> 5% (~79% reduction). Outperforms Speech-DPO, UNO, and RIO on intelligibility/robustness; matches baselines with ~4x fewer training samples (better data efficiency).
- **Notes:** Core novelty is token-level selective DPO targeting only error spans rather than whole-utterance preference. Demo at yaoxunji.github.io/fpo; preference data is synthetic (self-sampled) with automatic fine-grained labeling.

### 41. Fine-Tuning Text-to-Speech Diffusion Models Using Reinforcement Learning with Human Feedback (DLPO)

_Jingyi Chen, Ju Seung Byun, Micha Elsner, Pichao Wang, Andrew Perrault (Ohio State University) · 2025 · Interspeech 2025_

- **Categories:** C2, C3
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2508.03123) · arXiv:2508.03123
- **Synthetic-data role:** Self-generated rollout data + automatic reward signals. During RL fine-tuning the diffusion TTS model generates its own audio samples (synthetic rollouts); these are scored by automatic naturalness/quality reward models (UTMOS, NISQA) that serve as a proxy for human feedback. No external paired preference dataset of human-labeled pairs is required; the optimization data is the model's own synthetic generations plus model-derived rewards. Human listeners are used only for final A/B evaluation.
- **Method:** Diffusion Loss-Guided Policy Optimization (DLPO): an RLHF framework that fine-tunes a diffusion-based TTS model to maximize a naturalness reward while incorporating the model's original diffusion training loss directly into the reward function, regularizing the policy to preserve generative quality and avoid the degradation/inefficiency seen in prior diffusion-RL methods (DDPO, DPOK, KLinR, RWR).
- **Architecture:** Diffusion/score-based non-autoregressive TTS (WaveGrad 2 / WaveGrad 2R) as the policy. RL policy-gradient optimization treats the iterative denoising chain as a sequential decision process; reward = automatic naturalness score (UTMOS/NISQA) combined with the diffusion reconstruction loss term as a regularizer. No separate critic/codec; operates end-to-end on the diffusion sampler.
- **Base models:** WaveGrad 2 (and a reduced variant WaveGrad 2R) as the base diffusion TTS model to be fine-tuned.
- **Datasets:** LJSpeech (single-speaker English) as the underlying TTS dataset for WaveGrad 2 training/fine-tuning; reward signals from UTMOS and NISQA MOS predictors. Synthetic rollouts generated by the model itself during RL.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Start from a pretrained WaveGrad 2 / WaveGrad 2R diffusion TTS on LJSpeech. 2) Define reward = naturalness score from automatic MOS predictors (UTMOS, NISQA). 3) Add the original diffusion training loss into the reward/objective so the policy stays close to its pretrained denoising behavior (this is the DLPO core, distinguishing it from DDPO/DPOK/KLinR which use KL or gradient regularization). 4) Treat the reverse diffusion denoising trajectory as an RL episode; sample synthetic audio rollouts from the current policy. 5) Apply policy-gradient updates maximizing reward minus the diffusion-loss-guided regularization. 6) Iterate; evaluate with automatic UTMOS/NISQA and human A/B preference. Compare against RWR, DDPO, DPOK, KLinR baselines.
- **Key results:** DLPO-tuned WaveGrad 2R reaches UTMOS 3.65 and NISQA 4.02, outperforming RWR, DDPO, DPOK, and KLinR. In human evaluation, DLPO audio is preferred 67% of the time over the base WaveGrad 2R, improving naturalness while preserving generative capability.
- **Notes:** Distinct from the 2024 preprint (arXiv:2405.14632, 'DLPO: Diffusion Model Loss-Guided RL...') by overlapping authors; this 2025 version is the Interspeech-published RLHF formulation. Reward is automatic-MOS-based, so 'human feedback' is approximated by learned MOS predictors except for final evaluation.

### 42. FireRedTTS-2: Towards Long Conversational Speech Generation for Podcast and Chatbot

_Kun Xie, Feiyu Shen, Junjie Li, Fenglong Xie, Xu Tang, Yao Hu (Xiaohongshu / FireRed Team) · 2025 · arXiv preprint_

- **Categories:** C2, C4, C6, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2509.02020) · arXiv:2509.02020 · [code](https://fireredteam.github.io/demos/firered_tts_2)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Synthetic data is used in two places. (1) Emotion fine-tuning: a 15-hour single-speaker (distinctive female voice) corpus covering six emotions is augmented with synthetic dialogue pairs whose TEXT is produced by a text LLM and then SYNTHESIZED INTO SPEECH (TTS) to build emotional conversational context, enabling controllable emotional dialogue. (2) The large-scale dialogue training corpora (300k hours multi-speaker dialogue post-training, 50h podcast SFT) are built from in-the-wild speech with automatic pipelines; the paper's headline novelty is the synthetic emotion-dialogue augmentation. Amount of synthetic emotion data is on the order of the 15h base corpus expanded with LLM-text + TTS pairs (exact synthetic hours not reported).
- **Method:** Streaming, fully-discrete conversational TTS that emits separate speaker-specific audio streams and supports synthesis without the full text upfront. Uses a text-speech interleaved sequence ([S1]<text><audio>[S2]<text><audio>...) modeled by a dual-transformer over a 12.5Hz speech tokenizer, giving long-dialogue support, accurate speaker turns, and context-aware prosody for podcast and chatbot use.
- **Architecture:** Dual decoder-only transformer: a large backbone predicts first-layer (semantic/coarse) speech tokens, a smaller decoder transformer completes the remaining RVQ layers. Speech tokenizer at 12.5Hz = pretrained Whisper encoder + trainable acoustic encoder + 16-layer RVQ (2048 codes/layer); Vocos-based streaming decoder reconstructs 24kHz audio. Loss weights lambda_text=0.01, lambda_decoder=0.6; decoder optimized on 1/8 of speech segments.
- **Base models:** Whisper encoder (pretrained) inside the speech tokenizer; LM backbone trained for this work (no external pretrained LM explicitly stated). Builds on the FireRedTTS lineage.
- **Datasets:** Tokenizer: ~500k h (stage 1) + 60k h high-fidelity (stage 2). TTS LM: pretraining 1.1M h monologue (2 epochs); post-training 300k h multi-speaker dialogue (5 epochs); SFT 50 h podcast dialogue (15 epochs). Emotion FT: 15 h six-emotion single-speaker corpus + LLM-text/TTS synthetic dialogue pairs.
- **Code:** Demo: https://fireredteam.github.io/demos/firered_tts_2 ; code released at https://github.com/FireRedTeam/FireRedTTS2
- **Recipe:** 1) Train 12.5Hz tokenizer in 2 stages (320k steps stage1, 80k steps stage2 on 32 H800 GPUs). 2) Build text-speech interleaved sequences with speaker tags. 3) Three-stage LM curriculum: pretrain on 1.1M h monologue (2 ep) -> post-train on 300k h dialogue (5 ep) -> SFT on 50 h podcast dialogue (15 ep). 4) Optional emotion FT: curate 15h six-emotion speech, generate dialogue text with an LLM, synthesize to speech, fine-tune for controllable emotion. Dual-transformer with first-layer prediction in big model, residual RVQ in small model; losses lambda_text=0.01, lambda_decoder=0.6.
- **Key results:** English dialogue WER 3.16% (vs ZipVoice 11.71%); Mandarin dialogue CER 2.08% (vs ZipVoice 2.93%); speaker similarity 0.703 EN / 0.753 ZH; zero-shot voice-clone WER 1.95% EN (F5-TTS 1.83%); podcast CMOS 0.0 baseline vs MoonCast -0.21; emotion accuracy 83-93%. Outperforms MoonCast, ZipVoice-Dialog, MOSS-TTSD on intelligibility, speaker-turn reliability and naturalness.
- **Notes:** Streaming + separate per-speaker output streams are the practical differentiators. Synthetic emotion data is the clearest synthetic-data contribution. Some dataset/pipeline details are summarized from the HTML; exact synthetic-hour counts not reported.

### 43. From Tens of Hours to Tens of Thousands: Scaling Back-Translation for Speech Recognition

_Tianduo Wang, Lu Xu, Wei Lu, Shanbo Cheng · 2025 · arXiv preprint_

- **Categories:** C4, C5, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2505.16972) · arXiv:2505.16972
- **Synthetic-data role:** The synthetic data is TTS-generated speech ('Speech Back-Translation'). Large-scale text corpora are converted into synthetic audio by off-the-shelf TTS models that are themselves trained on only tens of hours of real transcribed speech per language. More than 500,000 hours of synthetic speech across ten languages are generated (roughly 500x-1000x the original real audio) and used as continued-pretraining data for the ASR model. Synthetic speech is the dominant training signal; real speech is used only to seed the TTS models and as anchor data.
- **Method:** Analogous to back-translation in NMT but for ASR: train cheap TTS on minimal real transcribed speech, then synthesize huge volumes of speech from abundant text and continue-pretrain a multilingual ASR model on it. An intelligibility-based assessment framework filters/evaluates synthetic speech quality so only intelligible synthetic audio contributes.
- **Architecture:** ASR backbone is Whisper-large-v3 (encoder-decoder transformer), continued-pretrained on synthetic speech. The data-generation side uses off-the-shelf / lightweight TTS models trained per language on tens of hours of real speech. An intelligibility scoring framework (ASR-based) gates synthetic quality.
- **Base models:** Whisper-large-v3 as the ASR base; off-the-shelf TTS models for synthesis (trained on tens of hours of real speech per language).
- **Datasets:** Real: tens of hours of transcribed speech per language to train the TTS models (ten languages). Synthetic: >500,000 hours of generated speech across ten languages, sourced from large-scale text corpora. Standard multilingual ASR benchmarks for evaluation.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) For each of ten languages, train an off-the-shelf TTS model on only tens of hours of real transcribed speech. 2) Take large-scale text corpora and synthesize speech with these TTS models, scaling total synthetic audio to >500k hours (~500x-1000x the real seed data). 3) Apply an intelligibility-based assessment framework (an ASR model scores synthetic clips; low-intelligibility samples are filtered or down-weighted) to control data quality. 4) Continue-pretrain Whisper-large-v3 on the large synthetic corpus (optionally mixed with the small real set). 5) Evaluate transcription error on multilingual benchmarks. Key idea: synthetic quality must clear an intelligibility threshold rather than naturalness; scale compensates for per-sample imperfection.
- **Key results:** Average transcription error reductions of over 30% across the ten tested languages relative to the Whisper-large-v3 baseline, achieved by continued pretraining on the >500k hours of synthetic back-translated speech.
- **Notes:** Strongest demonstration in the set of synthetic-speech scaling for ASR (not TTS output quality). Headline contribution is the intelligibility-gating framework that makes massive imperfect TTS data useful. Code not found at time of review.

### 44. GLM-TTS Technical Report

_Jiayan Cui, Zhihan Yang, Naihan Li, Jiankun Tian, et al. (zai-org / Zhipu AI) · 2025 · arXiv (technical report, Zhipu AI / Z.ai)_

- **Categories:** C1, C3, C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2512.14291) · arXiv:2512.14291 · [code](https://github.com/zai-org/GLM-TTS)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Reinforcement learning relies on self-generated synthetic outputs: under GRPO the model samples groups of its own speech generations, which are scored by multiple reward models (CER/pronunciation, speaker similarity, emotion, laughter) and used as the optimization signal. This is on-policy synthetic data (model-generated rollouts) for preference/multi-reward optimization rather than added synthetic training corpus. LoRA voice customization also enables synthetic new speakers.
- **Method:** A production-grade two-stage zero-shot TTS: an LLM (Llama-architecture) converts text to discrete speech tokens autoregressively, then a flow-matching / diffusion model converts tokens to mel-spectrogram (then waveform via vocoder). Quality and controllability are boosted by an F0-constrained speech tokenizer, a GRPO multi-reward RL stage, LoRA-based voice customization, and a hybrid phoneme-text input scheme for pronunciation control.
- **Architecture:** Stage 1: Llama-based autoregressive LM producing speech tokens from text. Stage 2: token-to-mel Flow-Matching / Diffusion Transformer (DiT), then Vocos or HiFT vocoder. Optimized neural speech tokenizer with fundamental-frequency (F0) constraints. CosyVoice-based frontend for text/speech preprocessing and speaker-embedding extraction. LoRA adapters for voice customization. Hybrid phoneme+text input.
- **Base models:** Llama-architecture LLM backbone for the AR token model; CosyVoice-based frontend (preprocessing + speaker embedding); Vocos / HiFT vocoders; flow-matching DiT. Builds conceptually on the CosyVoice / Seed-TTS family of token-based zero-shot TTS.
- **Datasets:** ~100k hours of training data (composition not fully detailed). Evaluation on open-source benchmarks including seed-tts-eval (zh/en) and standard sets; RL uses model-generated rollouts scored by reward models.
- **Code:** https://github.com/zai-org/GLM-TTS (Apache 2.0; also weights on HuggingFace/ModelScope: huggingface.co/zai-org/GLM-TTS)
- **Recipe:** 1) Train an F0-constrained neural speech tokenizer. 2) Pretrain the Llama-based AR text-to-speech-token LM on ~100k hours. 3) Train the token-to-mel flow-matching/DiT model; attach Vocos/HiFT vocoder. 4) Supervised fine-tuning (SFT). 5) GRPO multi-reward RL: sample groups of generations per prompt, score each with multiple reward models (similarity reward, CER/pronunciation reward, emotion reward, laughter reward), compute group-relative advantages, and update the policy to jointly optimize pronunciation, speaker similarity, and expressive prosody. 6) Deployment features: LoRA-based parameter-efficient voice cloning (3-10s prompt audio for zero-shot) and hybrid phoneme-text input for precise pronunciation control. Open-sourced inference code, weights, configs, and RL training modules.
- **Key results:** On seed-tts-eval zh: GLM-TTS CER 1.03 / SIM 76.1; GLM-TTS_RL CER 0.89 / SIM 76.4, beating Seed-TTS (CER 1.12 / SIM 79.6) and CosyVoice3 (CER 1.12 / SIM 78.1) on CER, with the RL stage notably lowering CER. Claims SOTA on multiple open benchmarks with only 100k hours. Supports zero-shot cloning from 3-10s audio.
- **Notes:** Apache 2.0, fully open (code + weights + RL modules). RL is GRPO with a multi-reward design; the synthetic-data angle is on-policy self-generated rollouts rather than an added synthetic corpus. Seed-TTS still leads on SIM; GLM-TTS_RL leads on CER.

### 45. Group Relative Policy Optimization for Text-to-Speech with Large Language Models

_Chang Liu, Ya-Jun Hu, Ying-Ying Gao, Shi-Lei Zhang, Zhen-Hua Ling · 2025 · arXiv preprint (submitted to ICASSP 2026), 5 pages_

- **Categories:** C2, C3
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2509.18798) · arXiv:2509.18798 · [code](https://ryuclc.github.io/LLM-TTS-GRPO)
- **Synthetic-data role:** The TTS policy generates a group of G=8 candidate speech samples per text prompt during GRPO rollouts; these self-generated (synthetic) samples are scored by an off-the-shelf ASR (Whisper-large-v3) to compute rewards. No external preference labels or human annotation; rewards are derived automatically from ASR (CER + NLL). This is online self-generated data used for RL fine-tuning rather than a fixed synthetic corpus.
- **Method:** Apply GRPO to fine-tune pretrained LLM-based TTS models, deriving rewards from an off-the-shelf ASR model rather than a trained reward model. Reward combines ASR character error rate (intelligibility) and ASR negative log-likelihood (naturalness/fluency) via a weighted harmonic mean, giving more informative signals than prior RL-for-TTS approaches.
- **Architecture:** Operates on LLM-based TTS systems: CosyVoice2 (semantic tokens + flow-matching decoder) and Llasa-1B (acoustic speech tokens, ~1B). Reward derived from Whisper-large-v3 ASR. No new model components introduced; GRPO is the optimization layer.
- **Base models:** CosyVoice2 and Llasa-1B (pretrained LLM-based TTS); Whisper-large-v3 as the off-the-shelf ASR reward provider.
- **Datasets:** Fine-tuning on 4,000 sentences from the Emilia dataset (~90% Chinese/English). Evaluation: seed-tts-eval (2,020 Chinese + 1,088 English), plus 1,000 each Japanese/Korean from Common Voice. No explicit hour count.
- **Code:** https://ryuclc.github.io/LLM-TTS-GRPO
- **Recipe:** Single-stage GRPO fine-tuning of pretrained TTS LLM. Hyperparameters: LR 1e-5, KL penalty beta 0.1, group size G=8, reward weights lambda_c=0.6 (CER) and lambda_n=0.4 (NLL), sensitivity params alpha_c=3, alpha_n=3. Reward = weighted harmonic mean of CER-based and NLL-based components from Whisper-large-v3. For each text prompt, sample 8 outputs, transcribe with ASR, compute group-relative advantages, update policy.
- **Key results:** CosyVoice2 baseline: Chinese CER 1.41->1.07, English CER 2.46->2.30, speaker similarity ~0.753 maintained. Subjective MOS (CosyVoice2): Chinese 4.42->4.58, English 4.22->4.43, all languages significant (p<0.05). Ablation confirms both CER and NLL reward components contribute.
- **Notes:** Lightweight (no separate reward model), uses generic ASR. Submitted to ICASSP 2026.

### 46. InstructTTSEval: Benchmarking Complex Natural-Language Instruction Following in Text-to-Speech Systems

_Kexin Huang (CaasiHUANG) et al. · 2025 · arXiv preprint (Jun 2025)_

- **Categories:** C4
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.16381) · arXiv:2506.16381 · [code](https://github.com/KexinHUANG19/InstructTTSEval)
- **Synthetic-data role:** The benchmark's natural-language instructions are LLM-generated: GPT-4o (gpt-4o-2024-08-06) writes the instructions for all three tasks. For the Descriptive-Style Directive task, some acoustic features are randomly omitted to create unstructured descriptions; for Role-Play, chain-of-thought prompting makes GPT-4o infer vocal traits from a scenario. Reference audio is REAL (not synthetic), sourced from movies/TV dramas/variety shows. So synthetic data = the LLM-authored instruction text paired with real reference speech; the benchmark itself does not train any TTS model.
- **Method:** An automatic benchmark to evaluate how well instruct-TTS systems follow complex natural-language style instructions. Three hierarchical tasks of increasing abstraction: Acoustic-Parameter Specification (APS, explicit control over 12 acoustic features), Descriptive-Style Directive (DSD, free-form style descriptions with some attributes omitted), and Role-Play (RP, abstract scenario/role prompts requiring inference). Uses Gemini as an LLM-as-a-judge for scalable automatic scoring, validated against human judgments.
- **Architecture:** Not a model paper; it is a benchmark + evaluation harness. Evaluation backbone: Gemini 2.5 Pro Preview (and Gemini Flash) used as an automatic speech-understanding judge to score instruction-following consistency.
- **Base models:** No model trained. Systems evaluated include closed-source Gemini Flash, Gemini Pro, GPT-4o-mini-tts, Hume; open-source VoxInstruct, Parler-TTS (mini/large), PromptTTS, PromptStyle.
- **Datasets:** InstructTTSEval: 3 tasks x (1,000 English + 1,000 Chinese) = 6,000 instructions total, each paired with a real reference audio (~5.6 hours). Reference audio from NCSSD plus supplementary film/TV/variety-show content. Instructions authored by GPT-4o.
- **Code:** https://github.com/KexinHUANG19/InstructTTSEval ; dataset https://huggingface.co/datasets/CaasiHUANG/InstructTTSEval
- **Recipe:** To reproduce: 1) Collect real reference clips (NCSSD + film/TV) and annotate 12 acoustic features. 2) Generate APS instructions enumerating all 12 features; generate DSD instructions with random feature omission; generate RP scenario prompts via GPT-4o chain-of-thought that infers vocal traits. 3) Run candidate instruct-TTS systems on each instruction to synthesize speech. 4) Score with Gemini 2.5 Pro as judge for instruction-following consistency; validate judge against human ratings. Languages: EN + ZH.
- **Key results:** Gemini Flash is the top system (~88.7% average EN), with DSD easiest (~93.8% best), RP ~80.1% best, APS ~76.4% best. Open-source systems lag substantially (~47% average). Results highlight large headroom in complex instruction following.
- **Notes:** Benchmark/dataset paper; no TTS training. Gemini-as-judge is central, with human-correlation validation. Real audio + synthetic instructions.

### 47. Interpolating Speaker Identities in Embedding Space for Data Expansion

_Tianchi Liu, Ruijie Tao, Qiongqiong Wang, Yidi Jiang, Hardik B. Sailor, Ke Zhang, Jingru Lin, Haizhou Li · 2025 · APSIPA ASC 2025 (Best Paper)_

- **Categories:** C4, C6, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2508.19210) · arXiv:2508.19210
- **Synthetic-data role:** Fully synthetic speakers are generated to expand training data for speaker verification (and gender classification). Nearby real speaker embeddings are selected and combined via spherical linear interpolation (slerp) to produce NEW intermediate speaker embeddings that correspond to no real person; a TTS system then synthesizes speech waveforms conditioned on these interpolated embeddings, creating synthetic-identity audio that augments the real training set.
- **Method:** INSIDE expands speaker data by interpolating between existing speaker embeddings rather than recording new speakers. Pairs of close embeddings from a pretrained embedding space are selected, spherically interpolated to create intermediate identities, and fed to a TTS system to synthesize speech for those novel identities, yielding additional diverse training data.
- **Architecture:** Pipeline of (1) a pretrained speaker-embedding/encoder model defining the embedding space, (2) spherical linear interpolation (slerp) in embedding space, and (3) a speaker-conditioned multi-speaker TTS synthesizer to render waveforms. Downstream task models: speaker-verification network and a gender classifier.
- **Base models:** Pretrained speaker verification/embedding extractor (to obtain and select embeddings) and a pretrained speaker-conditioned TTS system used as the synthesizer. Specific checkpoints not detailed in abstract.
- **Datasets:** Real speaker-verification training corpus (VoxCeleb-style) augmented with INSIDE-generated synthetic-identity speech; evaluated on standard SV benchmarks plus a gender-classification task. Exact dataset names/scale not in abstract.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Extract speaker embeddings for the real training corpus with a pretrained speaker encoder. 2) Select pairs of nearby embeddings in the embedding space (close identities give plausible interpolants). 3) Generate intermediate embeddings via spherical linear interpolation (slerp) between each selected pair. 4) Feed each interpolated embedding into a speaker-conditioned TTS system to synthesize speech, creating new pseudo-speakers. 5) Add the synthesized utterances as extra training data and train the speaker-verification (or gender) model on the union of real + synthetic data; combine with conventional augmentation. 6) Evaluate EER / classification accuracy.
- **Key results:** Relative improvements of 3.06%-5.24% on speaker verification and 13.44% relative improvement on gender classification when adding INSIDE-expanded data; method composes with existing augmentation. Best Paper at APSIPA ASC 2025.
- **Notes:** Target downstream task is speaker verification, not TTS quality, but TTS is the generator of the synthetic corpus, so it qualifies as synthetic-speaker generation (6), an LLM/synthetic-speech-built dataset (4), and a partially synthetic corpus (7). Interpolating embeddings risks identity collapse if pairs are too far apart, hence nearby-pair selection.

### 48. Koel-TTS: Enhancing LLM based Speech Generation with Preference Alignment and Classifier Free Guidance

_Shehzeen Hussain, Paarth Neekhara, Xuesong Yang, Edresson Casanova, Subhankar Ghosh, Mikyas T. Desta, Roy Fejgin, Rafael Valle, Jason Li (NVIDIA) · 2025 · EMNLP 2025 (Main); also ICML 2025 Workshop on ML for Audio_

- **Categories:** C2, C3, C5, C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2502.05236) · arXiv:2502.05236 · [code](https://github.com/NVIDIA/NeMo)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Preference-alignment data is fully synthetic and self-generated: for each input the model samples 6 candidate generations (multinomial top-k sampling, k=80, temperature=0.7). These synthesized candidates are pseudo-labeled by automatic reward models, a CER score from ASR and an SSIM/speaker-similarity score from speaker verification, and ranked via Pareto optimization. DPO uses the highest-ranked as 'chosen' and lowest as 'rejected'; RPO uses top-two vs bottom-two. Thus the preference dataset (no human labels) is built entirely from model-generated speech scored by ASR/SV models.
- **Method:** Improve an LLM-style (encoder-decoder transformer) zero-shot/multilingual TTS by (1) preference alignment (DPO and Reward-aware Preference Optimization, RPO) using ASR- and speaker-verification-derived rewards over self-generated samples, and (2) classifier-free guidance over the text/speaker conditioning to boost transcript and speaker adherence.
- **Architecture:** Encoder-decoder Transformer mapping text (+ speaker context audio) directly to discrete acoustic codec tokens; codec is NVIDIA Low Frame-rate Speech Codec (1.89 kbps, 21.5 fps, N=8 codebooks via Finite Scalar Quantization). Model sizes: ~380M params (English-only) and ~1.1B params (multilingual).
- **Base models:** Trained from scratch as the base TTS transformer (not initialized from an external LM); uses the LFSC neural audio codec; frozen ASR and speaker-verification models supply rewards for preference optimization.
- **Datasets:** English: ~18k hours = LibriTTS (train-clean), HiFiTTS, MLS/LibriVox (~17k h), plus ~63 h proprietary (2 speakers). Multilingual: + CML-TTS, ~21k h total across 6 languages (English, Spanish, German, French, Italian, Dutch). Preference data is generated synthetically from these checkpoints.
- **Code:** https://github.com/NVIDIA/NeMo (Koel-TTS implementation in NeMo; project samples page exists). Repo link was omitted in the blind-review PDF but code is in NeMo.
- **Recipe:** Step 1: Train base encoder-decoder transformer to predict LFSC codec tokens from text + context audio; randomly drop conditioning with prob 0.10 during training to enable CFG. Step 2 (preference data gen): for each input sample 6 generations (top-k=80, temp=0.7), decode to audio, score each with ASR (CER) and SV (SSIM), rank by Pareto front. Step 3 (alignment): DPO with beta=0.01 (chosen=top, rejected=bottom) OR RPO with reward-gap scaling eta=1.0 (top-2 vs bottom-2). Step 4 (inference): classifier-free guidance combining conditional and unconditional logits, l_cfg = gamma*l_c + (1-gamma)*l_u, with optimal gamma=2.5.
- **Key results:** State-of-the-art zero-shot TTS, outperforming prior LLM-based TTS on intelligibility (CER/WER), speaker similarity, and naturalness despite a significantly smaller training set; CFG and preference alignment each add measurable gains, with RPO generally beating DPO. Exact CMOS/CER numbers in the paper tables.
- **Notes:** Foundational paper for the same group's Align2Speak. Demonstrates that automatic-metric (ASR+SV) reward models can construct preference data with no human raters. Code available within NVIDIA NeMo.

### 49. MoonCast: High-Quality Zero-Shot Podcast Generation

_Zeqian Ju, Dongchao Yang, Jianwei Yu, Kai Shen, Yichong Leng, Zhengtao Wang, Xu Tan, Xinyu Zhou, Tao Qin, Xiangyang Li · 2025 · arXiv (OpenReview MVlKSYR7HX)_

- **Categories:** C1, C4, C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2503.14345) · arXiv:2503.14345 · [code](https://github.com/jzq2000/MoonCast)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Two roles. (1) The podcast SCRIPT (text content) is fully LLM-generated: an external LLM (Gemini 2.0 Pro Experimental 02-05) turns an arbitrary knowledge source (TXT/PDF/web URL) into a spontaneous two-speaker conversational script via a two-stage INPUT2BRIEF then BRIEF2SCRIPT prompt chain, producing JSON dialogue with spontaneous markers. (2) The output podcast audio is fully synthetic, generated zero-shot in unseen voices. The authors note the script/text-content generation module is empirically as important as the TTS acoustic modeling. The large-scale TTS training corpus itself is real recorded speech, not synthetic.
- **Method:** End-to-end any-text-to-podcast system: an LLM writes a natural, spontaneous multi-speaker script from a knowledge source, then a long-context LM-based speech model synthesizes minutes-long, multi-speaker, spontaneous conversational audio in unseen (zero-shot) voices.
- **Architecture:** Long-context autoregressive language-model-based speech generator (~2.5B parameters, 40K-token context length) operating over discrete speech tokens. A speech semantic codec whose encoder and decoder each use 12 ConvNeXt blocks (kernel size 7, hidden size 384) produces the discrete tokens; separate semantic and acoustic modeling for long, multi-speaker dialogue. Trained on ~500k hours of long-context speech.
- **Base models:** External LLM Gemini 2.0 Pro Experimental 02-05 for script generation (prompt-only, no fine-tuning). Speech LM and semantic codec trained for this work; specific pretrained-LM initialization not reported.
- **Datasets:** Real training audio ~500k hours total: 300,000h Chinese audiobooks + 15,000h Chinese conversational + 200,000h English conversational. Evaluation: a curated set of two PDF knowledge sources and two web-URL sources spanning CS papers, economics papers, tech blogs, and news.
- **Code:** https://github.com/jzq2000/MoonCast (inference code; model weights on HuggingFace; demo https://mooncastdemo.github.io/)
- **Recipe:** 1) Train a speech semantic codec (12 ConvNeXt encoder/decoder blocks, kernel 7, hidden 384) to discretize speech into semantic tokens. 2) Train a ~2.5B-parameter long-context autoregressive speech LM with 40K context on ~500k hours (300k Chinese audiobook + 15k Chinese conversational + 200k English conversational) to model long, multi-speaker, spontaneous dialogue. 3) For inference: feed knowledge source (TXT/PDF/URL) + INPUT2BRIEF prompt to Gemini 2.0 Pro to produce a brief summary, then BRIEF2SCRIPT prompt to produce a JSON two-speaker spontaneous script; 4) condition the speech LM on speaker prompts (zero-shot unseen voices) and the script to autoregressively generate the full multi-minute podcast audio. Prompts released in the paper; Gradio inference UI provided.
- **Key results:** Outperforms baseline podcast/long-form TTS systems on objective and subjective metrics, with particularly notable gains in spontaneity and coherence and in multilingual podcast quality; specific numeric WER/MOS values not surfaced in abstract-level sources.
- **Notes:** Two-speaker podcast focus; bilingual (Chinese/English). Script-generation prompts are released, enabling replication of the text-content pipeline. Verified via arXiv, OpenReview, and the official GitHub repo and demo page.

### 50. MPO: Multidimensional Preference Optimization for Language Model-based Text-to-Speech

_Kangxiang Xia, Xinfa Zhu, Jixun Yao, Lei Xie · 2025 · arXiv preprint_

- **Categories:** C2, C3, C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2509.00685) · arXiv:2509.00685
- **Synthetic-data role:** Preference data is fully synthetic/self-generated: for each text input the fine-tuned TTS LM generates 10 candidate speech samples. These candidates are automatically scored along three dimensions using off-the-shelf models (Paraformer ASR for CER/intelligibility, WavLM-large speaker verification cosine similarity, log-F0 RMSE for prosody), then organized into a 'preference set' of multiple preferred and dispreferred samples. No human preference annotation; the preference corpus is derived from a 100-hour high-quality Mandarin TTS corpus by generating and auto-ranking model outputs.
- **Method:** Multidimensional preference optimization for LM-based TTS. Replaces single paired DPO comparisons with a 'preference set' containing multiple preferred and dispreferred samples spanning intelligibility, speaker similarity, and prosody, plus a cross-entropy regularization term to mitigate the over-optimization/degradation seen in vanilla DPO from overconfidence in reward signals.
- **Architecture:** Decoder-only LLaMA-architecture LM predicting acoustic tokens autoregressively from text. 24 transformer layers, 16 attention heads, 1024-dim embeddings. Speech tokenized via neural codec (8192 codebook); text via BPE.
- **Base models:** Custom LLaMA-style autoregressive acoustic-token TTS LM pretrained by the authors (not a public base model).
- **Datasets:** Base pretraining: WenetSpeech4TTS + LibriHeavy + internal data (160,000 hours total). Fine-tuning: 2,000-hour TTS corpus. Preference optimization: 100-hour high-quality Mandarin TTS corpus (used to generate candidate samples).
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** Stage 1 base LM: 2M steps, peak LR 3e-4 on 160k hours. Stage 2 fine-tune: 130k steps, peak LR 5e-5 on 2k-hour corpus. Stage 3 MPO: generate 10 candidates per text from the 100-hour Mandarin corpus; score each with Paraformer (CER), WavLM-large (SIM cosine), log-F0 RMSE (prosody); build preference sets of preferred/dispreferred samples per dimension; optimize on a single GPU at LR 1e-6 with combined loss = DPO + lambda*cross-entropy, lambda=10 balancing the two.
- **Key results:** CER 4.72->3.90; speaker similarity 0.548->0.577; prosody (log-F0 RMSE) 0.337->0.279; ABX preference test: MPO preferred in 52.3% vs baseline. Reports improvements in intelligibility, speaker similarity, and prosody over baseline DPO-style systems.
- **Notes:** Regularization (CE term) is the key fix against DPO degradation. Code not released as of the version reviewed.

### 51. Multi-Reward GRPO for Stable and Prosodic Single-Codebook TTS LLMs at Scale

_Yicheng Zhong, Peiji Yang, Zhisheng Wang · 2025 · arXiv preprint (4 pages, submitted Nov 2025)_

- **Categories:** C3, C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2511.21270) · arXiv:2511.21270
- **Synthetic-data role:** Synthetic supervision rather than synthetic audio corpora: the policy generates candidate speech token sequences (rollouts) under GRPO, which are scored by automatic/AI-derived reward signals. A reasoning LLM produces synthetic prosody/pause-structure annotations via in-context learning that act as a prosody-alignment reward (LLM-annotated, no human labels). ASR-derived intelligibility and speaker-similarity scores serve as self-generated pseudo-reward labels over the model's own outputs.
- **Method:** Stabilizes single-codebook autoregressive TTS LLMs by augmenting next-token training with multi-reward Group Relative Policy Optimization (GRPO) that directly optimizes the token-generation policy. Combines intelligibility and speaker-similarity rewards with a duration/length consistency penalty, entropy regularization for decoding stability, and an LLM-annotated prosody-alignment reward to improve rhythm and prosody at scale.
- **Architecture:** Single-codebook autoregressive TTS language model backbone (one discrete acoustic/semantic codebook per step), with an optional flow-matching decoder for higher-fidelity reconstruction. GRPO as the RL optimizer (group-relative advantages, no separate value/critic network).
- **Base models:** Pretrained single-codebook autoregressive TTS LLM (specific checkpoint not reported); a reasoning LLM used in-context to predict pause/prosody structure for the prosody reward (specific LLM not reported).
- **Datasets:** Not reported (specific real or synthetic corpora and hours not stated in the abstract).
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Start from a pretrained single-codebook AR TTS LLM. 2) For each prompt, sample a group of G candidate token sequences (rollouts). 3) Score each rollout with multiple rewards: (a) intelligibility via ASR, (b) speaker similarity vs reference, (c) duration/length-consistency penalty against runaway/truncated generations, (d) entropy regularization on the decoding distribution for stability, (e) prosody-alignment reward from an LLM that predicts pause/rhythm structure in-context compared to generated prosody. 4) Combine rewards (weighted sum), compute group-relative advantages, update with the GRPO objective (KL-regularized to reference policy). 5) Optionally decode through a flow-matching decoder. Exact reward weights, group size, KL coefficient, learning rate not reported.
- **Key results:** Reports improved stability (fewer catastrophic/unstable generations) and improved prosody/rhythm for single-codebook TTS LLMs; specific WER/MOS/SIM numbers and baselines not given in the available abstract.
- **Notes:** 4-page short paper, CC BY-NC-ND 4.0. Reward and dataset specifics sparse in abstract; treat quantitative claims as not reported. Related in spirit to RLAIF/GRPO TTS work.

### 52. No Verifiable Reward for Prosody: Toward Preference-Guided Prosody Learning in TTS

_Seungyoun Shin, Dongha Ahn, Jiwoo Kim, Sungwook Jeon · 2025 · arXiv preprint_

- **Categories:** C3, C2
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2509.18531) · arXiv:2509.18531 · [code](https://tts.ch.dev)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Synthetic/generated data here is the model's own TTS outputs used to build preference pairs. GRPO uses model-generated speech scored by automatic rewards (CER/NLL, optional speaker similarity) over 1.6M text prompts. The DPO path uses model-generated speech sampled into pairs that humans label for prosodic naturalness (~200 human preference pairs per round, 3 rounds). No external synthetic corpus; the 'synthetic data' is self-generated rollouts for preference optimization.
- **Method:** Argues prosody has no verifiable automatic reward, so RL with verifiable rewards (GRPO on CER/NLL) lowers error rates but collapses prosody to monotone speech. Proposes iterative DPO with small human-in-the-loop preference batches to directly optimize prosodic naturalness while regularizing to the current model (moving reference).
- **Architecture:** Autoregressive LM-based codec TTS: Llasa, a transformer initialized from LLaMA that generates discrete speech tokens decoded to waveform by the XCodec2 neural audio codec. Base size Llasa-1B.
- **Base models:** Llasa-1B (LLaMA-initialized transformer) + XCodec2 codec; continued-pretrained on 36k hours of Korean, then fine-tuned on 18 hours of proprietary single-speaker data before RL/DPO.
- **Datasets:** KoCC-TTS, curated authentic Korean call-center task-oriented dialogue speech (test set released on HuggingFace: channelcorp/KoCC-TTS-testset). 36k hours Korean for continued pretraining; 18 hours proprietary single-speaker for fine-tuning. GRPO uses 1.6M text prompts. DPO uses ~200 human-labeled preference pairs per round across 3 rounds.
