- **Architecture:** WaveGrad2: non-autoregressive diffusion TTS generating waveform directly from text (no separate mel stage). Reward model UTMOS (MOS predictor). WER measured with Whisper.
- **Base models:** WaveGrad2 (MINDs Lab PyTorch implementation) as base TTS; UTMOS (trained on VoiceMOS Challenge 2022) as reward model.
- **Datasets:** LJSpeech (~24h, 13,100 clips, single female speaker; 12,388 train / 512 val / 200 test). UTMOS trained on VoiceMOS Challenge 2022 (~14h).
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** Fine-tune WaveGrad2 with objective J = -alpha*r(x0,c) - beta*||eps_tilde(xt,t) - eps_theta(xt,c,t)||_2, alpha=1, beta=1; reward r from UTMOS. Batch size 64, 10 denoising steps (1-step also tested), 5.5h on 8x A100-80GB. Key contrast: vs DDPO/DPOK/KLinR/RWR, DLPO integrates the native diffusion loss as penalty instead of relying solely on KL regularization or policy gradients.
- **Key results:** DLPO UTMOS 3.65 / NISQA 4.02 / WER 1.2, beating Base (2.90/3.74/1.5), DPOK (3.18/3.76/1.1), KLinR (3.02/3.73/1.3), DDPO (2.69/2.96/2.1), RWR (2.18/3.00/8.9); GT 4.20/4.37. Human eval: 67% prefer DLPO vs 14% base, 19% tie (20 pairs, 11 listeners).
- **Notes:** Single-speaker English (LJSpeech) only. Reward and eval use different MOS predictors (UTMOS reward, NISQA eval) to limit reward hacking. No code released.

### 76. DMOSpeech: Direct Metric Optimization via Distilled Diffusion Model in Zero-Shot Speech Synthesis

_Yinghao Aaron Li (Columbia University), Rithesh Kumar, Zeyu Jin (Adobe Research) · 2024 · ICML 2025 (poster); arXiv 2410.11097 (also circulated as DMDSpeech)_

- **Categories:** C3, C2
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2410.11097) · arXiv:2410.11097 · [code](https://dmospeech.github.io/)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Synthetic data is the student's own generated samples plus the teacher's distribution: distribution-matching distillation transfers knowledge from a 128-step teacher diffusion model to a 4-step student. The student generates speech that is directly optimized against differentiable perceptual metrics (CTC/ASR and speaker-verification losses), so generated speech is the optimization substrate rather than added training corpus. Distillation/DMD uses teacher and student score networks over the teacher's data distribution.
- **Method:** Combines improved distribution matching distillation (DMD2) with direct metric optimization: enables gradient pathways to all components so the model can be end-to-end optimized for differentiable perceptual metrics (CTC intelligibility loss + speaker-verification similarity loss), yielding a 4-step student that surpasses its 128-step teacher in WER and speaker similarity while being far faster.
- **Architecture:** Latent speech diffusion with velocity-prediction objective; DAC variational autoencoder codec for latent speech; DMD2 distillation with adversarial training; teacher and student score estimators; conditional multimodal conformer discriminator. ~450M params (teacher and student generators). Sampling reduced 128 -> 4 steps.
- **Base models:** Teacher latent diffusion TTS in the SimpleTTS/DiTTo-TTS family, trained on LibriLight for 400k steps (128-step inference). DAC autoencoder codec; pre-trained latent CTC-based ASR model (CTC loss); pre-trained latent speaker-verification model (SV loss).
- **Datasets:** LibriLight (57,706.4 h, 7,439 speakers, 48 kHz), segmented to 30 s chunks via WhisperX, phonemized with Phonemizer. Evaluation against teacher and DiTTo-TTS on standard zero-shot TTS test sets.
- **Code:** Project/demo page: https://dmospeech.github.io/ (no source repo cited in paper)
- **Recipe:** Initialize student G_theta and fake-score network g_psi from teacher params. Student training 40,000 steps: lr 1e-5, batch size 96. Alternating updates: 5x g_psi per G_theta update, 1x discriminator D per G_theta update. Multi-step sampling schedule at noise levels {1.0, 0.75, 0.50, 0.25} with re-noising between steps. Loss (Eq. 15): DMD distribution-matching loss + adversarial (lambda_adv=1e-3) + CTC (lambda_CTC=0 for first 5,000 iters then 1.0) + SV (lambda_SV=0 for first 10,000 iters then 1.0). CTC loss from pre-trained latent CTC ASR on character-level alignment; SV loss is cosine similarity between latent speaker-verification embeddings.
- **Key results:** WER 1.94 (teacher 9.51; GT 2.19); SIM 0.69 (teacher 0.55; GT 0.67); RTF 0.07, ~13.7x faster than teacher (0.96). Subjective vs DiTTo-TTS: MOS-N 4.27+/-0.03 (~teacher 4.28); SMOS-V 4.35+/-0.03 (>4.16); SMOS-S 4.16+/-0.03 (>4.07). First successful end-to-end differentiable-metric optimization in TTS; student surpasses teacher.
- **Notes:** Also referenced as 'DMDSpeech'. The CTC and SV losses are reward-like differentiable metrics optimized directly (metric/preference-style optimization), hence category 3; distillation fine-tunes from a teacher, hence category 2.

### 77. Emilia: An Extensive, Multilingual, and Diverse Speech Dataset for Large-Scale Speech Generation

_Haorui He, Zengqiang Shang, Chaoren Wang, Xuyuan Li, Yicheng Gu, Hua Hua, Liwei Liu, Chen Yang, Jiaqi Li, Peiyang Shi, Yuancheng Wang, Kai Chen, Pengyuan Zhang, Zhizheng Wu · 2024 · IEEE SLT 2024_

- **Categories:** C4, C5, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2407.05361) · arXiv:2407.05361 · [code](https://huggingface.co/datasets/amphion/Emilia-Dataset)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Not synthetic speech generation. The synthetic contribution is pseudo-labeling/automatic annotation: raw in-the-wild speech (no human transcripts) is automatically processed and machine-transcribed (Whisper ASR), diarized, segmented and quality-filtered to create pseudo-labeled training data. The labels/transcripts and segmentation are machine-generated while the audio is real in-the-wild speech.
- **Method:** Introduces Emilia-Pipe, the first open-source preprocessing pipeline to turn raw in-the-wild audio (podcasts, video, talk shows) into high-quality annotated TTS/speech-generation training data, and releases the Emilia dataset built with it to capture spontaneous, human-like speech absent from audiobook corpora.
- **Architecture:** Data pipeline (not a generative model). Components: audio standardization; source separation (vocal/background); pyannote speaker diarization; Silero-VAD fine-grained segmentation; Whisper-medium ASR (via WhisperX / faster-whisper CTranslate2) for transcription + language ID; DNSMOS P.835 quality filtering.
- **Base models:** Off-the-shelf models used inside the pipeline: source-separation model, pyannote diarization, Silero-VAD, Whisper-medium (WhisperX/faster-whisper), DNSMOS P.835 quality predictor. Not a trained model itself.
- **Datasets:** Emilia: 101k+ hours of in-the-wild speech across six languages (English, Chinese, German, French, Japanese, Korean), built from raw web/in-the-wild audio.
- **Code:** https://huggingface.co/datasets/amphion/Emilia-Dataset ; pipeline code in Amphion repo (https://github.com/open-mmlab/Amphion , preprocessors/Emilia)
- **Recipe:** Six pipeline steps: 1) Standardization: convert to mono WAV, resample to 24 kHz, 16-bit, normalize loudness to -20 dBFS (volume adjust clamped -3..+3 dB). 2) Source separation: separate vocals from background/music/noise. 3) Speaker diarization: pyannote pipeline so each segment is single-speaker. 4) Fine-grained VAD segmentation: Silero-VAD splits into 3-30 s clips. 5) ASR: Whisper-medium (WhisperX + CTranslate2/faster-whisper) produces transcript and language tag. 6) Filtering: drop segments with language-ID confidence below 80%, DNSMOS P.835 OVRL below 3.0, or anomalous character/phone durations. Output JSON metadata + MP3 audio. To replicate: collect raw in-the-wild audio per target language, run these six steps, then train any speech-gen model on the (audio, pseudo-transcript) pairs.
- **Key results:** Yields 101k+ hours over 6 languages. Models trained on Emilia produce markedly more spontaneous, human-like speech than audiobook-trained models while maintaining comparable intelligibility; supports multilingual and crosslingual generation with diverse timbres and styles (specific WER/MOS in paper).
- **Notes:** SLT 2024 version. Open dataset and open-source pipeline (Amphion). Real audio with machine-generated labels; research-use licensing, sourced from in-the-wild data.

### 78. Emo-DPO: Controllable Emotional Speech Synthesis through Direct Preference Optimization

_Xiaoxue Gao, Chen Zhang, Yiming Chen, Huayun Zhang, Nancy F. Chen · 2024 · ICASSP 2025 (IEEE)_

- **Categories:** C3, C2, C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2409.10157) · arXiv:2409.10157 · [code](https://xiaoxue1117.github.io/Emo-tts-dpo/)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Preference pairs are constructed from existing real data rather than newly synthesized audio: for a given text, the target-emotion utterance is the preferred (positive) sample and a different-emotion utterance with the SAME text is mined from the training set as the dispreferred (negative) sample. The 'synthetic' element is this automatic preference-pairing/labeling that turns a standard emotional TTS corpus into chosen/rejected pairs to teach the model the contrast between emotions via DPO.
- **Method:** Reframes emotional TTS as preference optimization: instead of supervised single-emotion targets, an emotion-aware LLM-TTS is trained with Direct Preference Optimization to prefer the correct emotion over alternative emotions sharing the same text, so the model learns nuanced contrasts between emotions and leverages LLM in-context / instruction-following ability.
- **Architecture:** Emotion-aware LLM-TTS: autoregressive LLM-style TTS that predicts speech tokens, initialized from CosyVoice-300M-Instruct; inference reconstructs audio via a pretrained flow-matching model + HiFi-GAN vocoder over the speech tokenizer's tokens.
- **Base models:** CosyVoice-300M-Instruct (LLM-TTS backbone); CosyVoice flow-matching decoder + HiFi-GAN vocoder for waveform synthesis.
- **Datasets:** English portion of ESD (Emotional Speech Dataset): 10 speakers x 5 emotions (angry, happy, sad, surprise, neutral), ~1.2h per speaker (~1,750 utterances), ~1,000 validation and 1,500 test utterances.
- **Code:** https://xiaoxue1117.github.io/Emo-tts-dpo/ (demo/project page; no public training-code repo found)
- **Recipe:** Stage 1 (instruction tuning / SFT): fine-tune CosyVoice-300M-Instruct on ESD-English for 2 epochs with dynamic batching using a label-smoothing KL loss. Preference-pair construction: for each text x with target emotion (positive), sample negative instances that share the same text x but carry a different emotion. Stage 2 (Emo-DPO): 3 epochs, batch size 8, 4 GPUs, with a combined objective = DPO loss + KL regularization + SFT loss and a JS-divergence regularization; weighting coefficients alpha=1, theta=1, gamma=1 (DPO beta sharpness term unspecified). Inference: LLM-TTS generates tokens, decoded by flow matching + HiFi-GAN.
- **Key results:** Objective: emotion similarity 98.87 (vs CosyVoice 98.73, EmoSpeech 98.26); prosody similarity 3.89 (vs 3.69 / 3.35); speech-emotion-recognition accuracy 0.72 (vs 0.65 / 0.56). AB preference: Emo-DPO preferred 88.7% over CosyVoice and 85.6% over EmoSpeech. MOS and Emotion-MOS highest for Emo-DPO (exact values not tabulated). Baselines: EmoSpeech (FastSpeech2-based) and CosyVoice. (Intelligibility metric was slightly worse than EmoSpeech.)
- **Notes:** Verified via arXiv HTML, IEEE Xplore, and project page. 5-page ICASSP paper. Negative samples are real same-text different-emotion recordings, so this is preference-labeling of an existing corpus (categories 3/5) rather than new audio synthesis. No public training-code repo located, only the demo page.

### 79. EmoKnob: Enhance Voice Cloning with Fine-Grained Emotion Control

_Haozhe (Tony) Chen, Run Chen, Julia Hirschberg · 2024 · EMNLP 2024 (Main); ACL Anthology 2024.emnlp-main.466_

- **Categories:** C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2410.00316) · arXiv:2410.00316 · [code](https://github.com/tonychenxyz/emoknob)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Largely inference-time control rather than synthetic-data training. Uses paired neutral/emotional reference samples to derive an emotion direction vector; for the text-to-emotion methods it leverages emotions described by open-ended text. The few-shot pairs are real reference recordings, not generated; the system produces emotionally controlled synthetic speech as output. No large synthetic training corpus is generated.
- **Method:** EmoKnob extracts an 'emotion direction vector' in the speaker-embedding space of a foundation voice-cloning model from a pair of neutral and emotional samples. It then manipulates the reference speaker's embedding by adding the emotion direction scaled by a user-specified strength ('knob'), embedding fine-grained, intensity-controllable emotion into cloned speech with few-shot examples of arbitrary emotions. Two additional methods enable controlling emotions described by open-ended natural-language text.
- **Architecture:** Built on the MetaVoice voice-cloning backbone (foundation TTS with an expressive speaker representation space). Emotion control is a vector-arithmetic manipulation in speaker-embedding space (no retraining of the backbone). Includes new evaluation metrics for faithfulness and recognizability of emotion control.
- **Base models:** MetaVoice (MetaVoice-1B) foundation voice-cloning model as the backbone; CLAP/text encoders used for the open-ended text-to-emotion mapping.
- **Datasets:** Few-shot neutral/emotional reference pairs (real recordings); emotional speech samples for evaluation. Specific dataset names/hours not detailed in fetched content. Compared against commercial TTS services.
- **Code:** https://github.com/tonychenxyz/emoknob (project page: https://emoknob.cs.columbia.edu/)
- **Recipe:** 1) Choose a foundation voice-cloning model with a meaningful speaker-embedding space (MetaVoice). 2) Collect a small pair (few-shot) of neutral and emotional speech samples for a target emotion. 3) Compute speaker embeddings of both; the emotion direction = (emotional embedding - neutral embedding), optionally averaged over multiple pairs. 4) At synthesis time, take the target speaker's reference embedding and add strength * emotion_direction to inject the emotion at the desired intensity. 5) For open-ended text emotion control, map a text emotion description to a direction (two proposed methods, e.g., via retrieval/aggregation of demonstrative samples or text-embedding alignment). 6) Synthesize with the modified embedding. No backbone fine-tuning required; primary hyperparameter is emotion strength.
- **Key results:** Subjective and objective evaluations show EmoKnob effectively embeds emotions into cloned speech and surpasses the emotion expressiveness of commercial TTS services; introduces and reports faithfulness/recognizability metrics for emotion control. Exact MOS/numbers not captured in fetched excerpt.
- **Notes:** Real, peer-reviewed (EMNLP 2024 Main). Code and data publicly released. This is a training-free, inference-time emotion-control method built on a frozen cloning backbone.

### 80. Enhancing Low-Resource ASR through Versatile TTS: Bridging the Data Gap

_Guanrou Yang, Fan Yu, Ziyang Ma, Zhihao Du, Zhifu Gao, Shiliang Zhang, Xie Chen · 2024 · arXiv preprint (Shanghai Jiao Tong University X-LANCE / Alibaba)_

- **Categories:** C4, C5, C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2410.16726) · arXiv:2410.16726
- **Synthetic-data role:** A powerful zero-shot multilingual TTS (CosyVoice-base-300M) generates synthetic speech to augment low-resource ASR training. Synthetic speech is produced with diverse text prompts and diverse speaker embeddings, then mixed roughly 1:1 with real data. The paper studies which synthetic-data factors matter (text diversity, speaker diversity, data volume), finding text diversity more important than speaker diversity, and that generating a moderate amount (~equal to real data) is most cost-efficient.
- **Method:** Leverage a versatile zero-shot TTS to synthesize diverse, high-quality speech for low-resource ASR scenarios (accents, minority languages, dialects, long-tail hotwords), and ablate the contributing factors, showing text diversity drives most of the ASR gains.
- **Architecture:** TTS: CosyVoice-base-300M, a zero-shot multilingual codec/LM-based TTS (autoregressive text-to-speech-token LM + flow-matching acoustic model + vocoder), ~300M params. ASR: standard Conformer, 12-block Conformer encoder + 6-block Transformer decoder, hybrid CTC/attention loss, ~120M params.
- **Base models:** CosyVoice-base-300M (pretrained on 130k h Mandarin, 30k h English, 5k h Cantonese, 4.6k h Japanese, 2.2k h Korean) as the synthetic-speech generator; Conformer ASR trained per scenario.
- **Datasets:** Per scenario, real + TTS-synthesized: Accented English 300 h real + 300 h TTS; Korean (minority language) 3,700 h real + 4,000 h TTS; Min Nan dialect 200 h real + 200 h TTS; Wu dialect 200 h real + 200 h TTS; Chinese automotive hotwords 300 h real + 300 h TTS.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Use CosyVoice-base-300M (optionally adapt its components) as a versatile TTS. 2) For each low-resource scenario, collect diverse text prompts and a set of speaker vectors; synthesize speech to a volume comparable to the real data (most cost-efficient regime). 3) Mix synthetic with real data and train a standard Conformer ASR (12-layer Conformer encoder, 6-layer Transformer decoder, hybrid CTC/attention, ~120M params). 4) Ablate text diversity vs speaker diversity vs data volume to attribute gains. Key finding: text diversity > speaker diversity; ~1x real-data volume of TTS is optimal cost-efficiency.
- **Key results:** Relative WER/CER reductions: Accented English 12.61% to 10.69% (15.2% rel.); Korean 8.48% to 6.31% (25.6% rel.); Min Nan 55.42% to 30.00% (45.9% rel.); Wu 27.47% to 19.93% (27.5% rel.); Chinese hotwords 21.32% to 13.15% (38.3% rel.). Consistent, substantial gains over real-data-only Conformer baselines.
- **Notes:** ASR-centric study where TTS-generated speech is the augmentation; strong concrete metrics and clear factor ablation (text diversity most critical). Verified via arXiv abstract and HTML fetch.

### 81. Enhancing Zero-shot Text-to-Speech Synthesis with Human Feedback

_Chen Chen, Yuchen Hu, Wen Wu, Helin Wang, Eng Siong Chng, Chao Zhang · 2024 · arXiv preprint (also OpenReview submission)_

- **Categories:** C3, C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2406.00654) · arXiv:2406.00654
- **Synthetic-data role:** The model itself generates the candidate speech used for optimization: for each transcript a batch of b outputs is sampled from VoiceCraft using different unseen-speaker prompts. These generated (synthetic) samples are then human-annotated as desirable/undesirable with an associated uncertainty score, forming unpaired preference data. No external preference dataset or reward model is needed; the synthetic self-generated samples plus human binary labels drive the update.
- **Method:** UNO (Uncertainty-aware Optimization): a sampling-annotating-learning framework that aligns a zero-shot TTS LM to human feedback. It samples diverse generations from the model, collects binary human desirability labels with uncertainty, and optimizes a KTO-style (unpaired) objective whose update magnitude is scaled by inverse annotation uncertainty, so confident-good samples update aggressively and uncertain ones conservatively.
- **Architecture:** VoiceCraft: neural-codec autoregressive language model. Speech tokenizer = EnCodec with 4 RVQ codebooks, vocabulary size 2048; decoder-only token LM. Two sizes: 330M and 830M params.
- **Base models:** VoiceCraft (330M and 830M) pretrained on GigaSpeech as the policy/reference model. Uncertainty estimators (EDL and I-CNF) trained on the SOMOS MOS dataset.
- **Datasets:** Pre-training: GigaSpeech (~9k hours, audiobooks/podcasts/YouTube). Optimization prompts: LibriTTS (no GigaSpeech overlap). Uncertainty models trained on SOMOS. Evaluation: LibriSpeech test-clean.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Start from pretrained VoiceCraft (330M/830M). 2) For each optimization transcript, sample a batch of b generations using b different unseen-speaker prompts to maximize diversity. 3) Human annotators label each generation desirable/undesirable and provide an uncertainty u in [0,1) reflecting evaluation variance; estimate u via EDL or I-CNF trained on SOMOS. 4) Optimize UNO value function V_TTS = sigmoid(u^-1 * R(t,p,s) - Z_ref) for positive samples (KTO-inspired, unpaired), minimizing (1 - V_TTS); inverse uncertainty u^-1 scales update magnitude. 5) Evaluate WER, MOS, speaker similarity vs DPO baselines.
- **Key results:** 330M model: WER 8.4% -> 2.6% (vs 7.2% for SpeechAlign-DPO); MOSNet MOS 3.65 -> 4.31; speaker similarity 0.84 -> 0.91. Human naturalness MOS 3.38 -> 4.06, rated comparable to ground-truth speech. Substantially reduces failure/bad cases and improves robustness; also adapts to desired style for emotional TTS.
- **Notes:** Key distinction from DPO: works on unpaired preference data with explicit annotation-uncertainty weighting (KTO-flavored), eliminating the need for a reward model or paired preferences. Self-generated samples are the synthetic optimization data.

### 82. Exploring synthetic data for cross-speaker style transfer in style representation based TTS

_Lucas H. Ueda, Leonardo B. de M. M. Marques, Flavio O. Simoes, Mario U. Neto, Fernando Runstein, Bianca Dal Bo, Paula D. P. Costa · 2024 · Interspeech 2024 workshop SynData4GenAI 2024_

- **Categories:** C2, C6, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2409.17364) · arXiv:2409.17364
- **Synthetic-data role:** A voice conversion (VC) model generates expressive synthetic speech for target speakers lacking expressive recordings (low-resource expressive scenario). Donor expressive speech is converted to target timbre, producing synthetic expressive-target pairs that augment training so the TTS performs cross-speaker style transfer. Extended cross-lingually for accent transfer.
- **Method:** To enable expressive cross-speaker style transfer when target speakers have only neutral/limited data, use voice conversion to synthesize expressive speech in the target voice and train a style-representation TTS on this augmented data. The style encoder is pre-trained with timbre perturbation and a prototypical angular loss to disentangle style from speaker timbre and prevent identity leakage.
- **Architecture:** Style-representation-based TTS (style encoder producing a style embedding conditioning the acoustic model) plus a separate VC model as synthetic-data generator. Style encoder pre-trained with timbre perturbation augmentation and prototypical angular loss.
- **Base models:** Voice conversion model as synthetic-data generator (backbone not detailed); style-representation TTS as target system. Specific pretrained checkpoints not reported.
- **Datasets:** Expressive donor-speaker data plus target-speaker (low-resource expressive) data; synthetic VC-generated expressive speech for targets; cross-language data for accent transfer. Exact corpus names/hours not reported in the abstract.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Pre-train a style encoder with timbre perturbation augmentation and prototypical angular loss to disentangle style from speaker identity. 2) Use a VC model to convert expressive donor speech into the target speaker's voice, generating synthetic expressive target recordings. 3) Train/fine-tune the style-representation TTS on real plus VC-synthesized expressive data for cross-speaker transfer. 4) Extend the VC-augmentation pipeline cross-lingually for accent transfer. 5) Evaluate naturalness and speaker similarity. Exact hyperparameters/hours not reported.
- **Key results:** Synthetic VC data improves naturalness and speaker similarity in cross-speaker style-transfer scenarios; extends successfully to cross-language accent transfer. Reported qualitatively; precise MOS/SIM numbers not in available sources.
- **Notes:** License CC BY 4.0. Workshop paper (SynData4GenAI 2024). Numeric metrics and exact dataset names require the full PDF.

### 83. Extending Multilingual Speech Synthesis to 100+ Languages without Transcribed Data

_Takaaki Saeki, Gary Wang, Nobuyuki Morioka, Isaac Elias, Kyle Kastner, Fadi Biadsy, Andrew Rosenberg, Bhuvana Ramabhadran, Heiga Zen, Francoise Beaufays, Hadar Shemtov · 2024 · ICASSP 2024 (Google)_

- **Categories:** C6, C5, C1
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2402.18932) · arXiv:2402.18932 · [code](https://google.github.io/tacotron/publications/extending_tts/)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Uses untranscribed (unpaired) found speech and unspoken (text-only) data as a substitute for paired transcribed supervision. Pseudo-supervision: a joint speech-text encoder learns shared representations so that for a new language only untranscribed audio and/or raw text are needed (no human-aligned transcripts). Optionally just 15 minutes of transcribed found data per language is added. The synthetic element is the self/semi-supervised representation learning and aligned pseudo-targets that stand in for paired transcribed data, enabling synthesis in 100+ languages.
- **Method:** Scales a multilingual TTS model to 100+ languages using found, mostly untranscribed data. Combines a massively multilingual joint speech-text encoder (pretrained semi-supervised) with unsupervised training on untranscribed speech and unspoken text, so the model can synthesize intelligible speech in languages with no transcribed data.
- **Architecture:** Built on the Virtuoso / Maestro framework: speech encoder + text encoder + shared encoder + RNN-T decoder (alignment/ASR-style objective) + speech decoder for generation. Maestro provides matched speech-text representations via modality matching; Virtuoso extends it with a speech decoder for TTS. Acoustic generation is non-autoregressive TTS producing spectrogram/speech features.
- **Base models:** Virtuoso (massive multilingual speech-text joint semi-supervised TTS), which extends MAESTRO (matched speech-text representations through modality matching). Initialized/pretrained from these joint speech-text representation frameworks.
- **Datasets:** Massively multilingual found data: untranscribed speech and unspoken (text-only) corpora covering 100+ languages, with as little as 15 minutes of transcribed found data per new language for the supervised variant. Evaluated on 30+ unseen languages.
- **Code:** https://google.github.io/tacotron/publications/extending_tts/ (audio demos only; no open code)
- **Recipe:** 1) Pretrain a joint speech-text encoder (Maestro-style) with modality matching on massively multilingual data to align speech and text representations. 2) Add a speech decoder (Virtuoso) for generation. 3) For a new/unseen language with no transcribed data, train using only untranscribed speech and unspoken text via unsupervised objectives leveraging the shared representation space. 4) Optionally fine-tune with ~15 minutes of transcribed found data per language to sharpen intelligibility. Evaluate CER vs ground truth and naturalness MOS. Replication needs the Virtuoso/Maestro joint-encoder setup plus large multilingual untranscribed audio and text-only corpora.
- **Key results:** Without any transcribed speech in a new language, generates intelligible speech in >30 unseen languages with CER difference <10% vs ground truth. With just 15 minutes of transcribed found data, reduces the intelligibility gap to <=1% and matches ground-truth naturalness MOS in several languages.
- **Notes:** Google research; ICASSP 2024. No public code or weights, only a demo page. Strong example of using untranscribed/unspoken data as a substitute for paired transcribed data to reach 100+ languages.

### 84. Generating Data with Text-to-Speech and Large-Language Models for Conversational Speech Recognition

_Samuele Cornell, Jordan Darefsky, Zhiyao Duan, Shinji Watanabe · 2024 · SynData4GenAI 2024 workshop (ISCA)_

- **Categories:** C4, C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2408.09215) · arXiv:2408.09215 · [code](https://github.com/popcornell/ASRteacher TTSFT)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Both the conversational text and the speech are synthetic. Llama 3 8B Instruct (prompted with 8 few-shot examples from the Parakeet training subset) generates multi-speaker conversational transcripts; the Parakeet conversational multi-speaker diffusion TTS then synthesizes the corresponding speech. 80-160h of synthetic conversational audio is generated for Fisher experiments and 80h for Mixer 6, used to fine-tune Whisper for downstream conversational ASR. Also compares against using real Fisher transcripts (instead of LLM-generated) fed to the same TTS.
- **Method:** A pipeline that generates synthetic multi-speaker conversational speech for ASR adaptation: an LLM writes conversational dialogues, a conversational multi-speaker TTS renders them as audio, and Whisper is fine-tuned on the result; shown to beat classical multi-speaker simulation for telephone and distant-speech conversational ASR.
- **Architecture:** Data-generation components: Llama 3 8B Instruct (LLM, few-shot prompted) for dialogue text; Parakeet, a diffusion-based conversational multi-speaker TTS trained on 60,000h of Spotify podcasts, for audio. ASR model fine-tuned: Whisper medium with LoRA adapters (rank 64, alpha 128, dropout 0.1) on a frozen backbone. Baselines: Coqui xTTS-v2 TTS and NeMo multi-speaker simulation over LibriSpeech.
- **Base models:** Llama 3 8B Instruct (LLM), Parakeet diffusion conversational TTS (pretrained on 60k h Spotify podcasts), Whisper medium (ASR backbone fine-tuned with LoRA). Baseline TTS: Coqui xTTS-v2.
- **Datasets:** Real: Fisher (11,699 telephone conversations; train/val/test 1960h/7h/7h), Mixer 6 Speech (~60h dev/eval, CHiME-7 re-annotated). Synthetic: 80-160h generated for Fisher, 80h for Mixer 6. NeMo multi-speaker-simulation baseline uses LibriSpeech.
- **Code:** https://github.com/popcornell/ASRteacher TTSFT
- **Recipe:** 1) Prompt Llama 3 8B Instruct with 8 few-shot examples drawn from the Parakeet training subset to generate multi-speaker conversational transcripts (or alternatively use real Fisher transcripts). 2) Synthesize audio with Parakeet (diffusion conversational multi-speaker TTS) to produce 80-160h (Fisher) / 80h (Mixer 6) of synthetic conversational speech. 3) Fine-tune Whisper medium using LoRA adapters (rank=64, alpha=128, dropout=0.1) on the frozen backbone; up to 20 epochs, linear warmup+decay, gradient L2 clipping=5, early stopping after 2 epochs without val improvement. 4) Evaluate cpWER on Fisher and Mixer 6 against no-adaptation, xTTS, NeMo MSS, and real in-domain adaptation baselines.
- **Key results:** Fisher test (80h adaptation, cpWER): no adaptation 44.94%; Parakeet+LLM-generated text 20.41%; Parakeet+real Fisher transcripts 21.44%; xTTS+LLM 34.65%; NeMo MSS 34.37%; real in-domain Fisher 80h 15.43%. Mixer 6 (80h): Parakeet+LLM 21.25% vs NeMo MSS 36.71% vs in-domain 20.36%. The Parakeet+LLM synthetic pipeline far outperforms classical simulation and standard multi-speaker TTS, approaching real in-domain data, with LLM-generated text matching or slightly beating real transcripts.
- **Notes:** Workshop paper (SynData4GenAI 2024). Fine-tuning code public; Parakeet is the Darefsky conversational TTS. Verified via arXiv HTML, ISCA archive, and the public fine-tuning repo.

### 85. Hard-Synth: Synthesizing Diverse Hard Samples for ASR using Zero-Shot TTS and LLM

_Not reported (extracted from arXiv listing) · 2024 · arXiv preprint (Nov 2024)_

- **Categories:** C4, C5, C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2411.13159) · arXiv:2411.13159
- **Synthetic-data role:** Fully synthetic ASR training data is generated to augment a low-resource real corpus. LLaMA3.1-8B rewrites in-domain text (no extra text data needed) to produce diverse new transcripts (~13% new vocabulary). A zero-shot TTS model (VoiceCraft) then synthesizes speech for these transcripts, but crucially clones speech styles selected as HARD for the current ASR model (hard prompt selection). Total synthetic data: 16.15 hours / 9,196 utterances, derived from 20 hours of hard prompts, added on top of LibriSpeech-clean-100.
- **Method:** ASR data augmentation that (1) uses an LLM to rewrite in-domain text into diverse new transcripts, and (2) uses zero-shot TTS to synthesize that text while cloning speaker/prosody styles the ASR model finds hardest to recognize. Hardness is measured by running a weak ASR model and selecting high-CER audio clips as voice-cloning prompts, so synthetic audio targets the model's weaknesses rather than using predefined styles.
- **Architecture:** Pipeline of three model families: LLaMA3.1-8B (text rewriting LLM); zero-shot TTS for voice cloning, primarily VoiceCraft (autoregressive neural-codec LM TTS), compared against F5-TTS (flow-matching DiT TTS); and the downstream ASR model, a Conformer (~34.23M params) trained with joint CTC + attention loss.
- **Base models:** LLaMA3.1-8B (frozen, for text rewriting); VoiceCraft and F5-TTS as pretrained zero-shot TTS systems; a weak/seed Conformer ASR (trained 15 epochs) used as the hardness scorer; the target Conformer is trained from scratch.
- **Datasets:** Real: LibriSpeech-clean-100 (100 hours, low-resource setting), with dev-other/test-other for evaluation. Synthetic: 16.15 hours / 9,196 utterances generated by Hard-Synth from 20 hours of hard prompts (~13% new vocabulary).
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Train a weak seed Conformer on LibriSpeech-clean-100 for 15 epochs. 2) Run it on candidate audio, compute CER between hypotheses and references; higher CER = harder. Retain clips >3s as voice-cloning prompts (hard prompt selection). 3) Use LLaMA3.1-8B to rewrite in-domain transcripts into diverse new text. 4) Synthesize new audio with zero-shot TTS (VoiceCraft) using the hard-selected speaker prompts, producing 16.15h / 9,196 utterances. 5) Train the target Conformer (34.23M params) from scratch on real + synthetic data: CTC + attention loss, 70 epochs, lr 2e-3, 15,000 warmup steps, Fbank features (400-sample window, 160-sample hop), SpecAugment, average 10 best checkpoints.
- **Key results:** On LibriSpeech with the Conformer: dev-other 17.47% -> 16.34% WER (6.5% relative reduction) and test-other 17.43% -> 16.67% WER (4.4% relative reduction) versus the baseline without Hard-Synth augmentation. Ablations compare VoiceCraft vs F5-TTS and hard vs random prompt selection.
- **Notes:** Verified on arXiv (2411.13159) and Papers with Code. Combines LLM text generation (cat 4), self-training/data-augmentation targeting model weaknesses via pseudo-difficulty scoring (cat 5), and synthetic-speaker/style cloning (cat 6). No public code repo found. Demonstrates that ASR-hardness-aware synthetic speech outperforms naive TTS augmentation.

### 86. Improving Accented Speech Recognition using Data Augmentation based on Unsupervised Text-to-Speech Synthesis

_Cong-Thanh Do, Shuhei Imai, Rama Doddipatla, Thomas Hain · 2024 · arXiv preprint (Toshiba Cambridge Research Lab / University of Sheffield)_

- **Categories:** C4, C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2407.04047) · arXiv:2407.04047
- **Synthetic-data role:** Synthetic accented speech is generated by UNSUPERVISED TTS systems and used to augment ASR training data. The TTS systems are trained on small amounts of accented speech WITHOUT manual transcriptions, using pseudo-labels (unsupervised units) instead of human annotation. The TTS then generates synthetic accented speech from text prompts, combined with non-accented real speech to train/fine-tune the ASR model. This is both an LLM-free synthetic-speech corpus (cat 4) and a pseudo-label/self-training augmentation (cat 5).
- **Method:** Use unsupervised TTS (trained on limited untranscribed accented speech via pseudo-labels) to synthesize accented speech, then mix that synthetic accented audio with non-accented data to augment ASR training, improving recognition of accented English.
- **Architecture:** ASR: wav2vec2.0 self-supervised models pre-trained on large unsupervised accented speech, then fine-tuned for ASR (CTC). TTS: an unsupervised TTS system trained from limited accented speech using predicted/pseudo labels (no transcripts) to synthesize accented speech from text prompts.
- **Base models:** wav2vec2.0 (pretrained, then fine-tuned) as the ASR backbone; an unsupervised TTS model trained on small accented corpora with pseudo-labels.
- **Datasets:** TTS training: L2-ARCTIC and British Isles corpora (read accented speech). Non-accented ASR data: LibriSpeech. Evaluation: Edinburgh International Accents of English Corpus (EdAcc, spontaneous conversational). Synthetic data = unsupervised-TTS-generated accented speech.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Train an unsupervised TTS on small accented corpora (L2-ARCTIC, British Isles) using pseudo-labels rather than transcripts. 2) Synthesize accented speech from text prompts. 3) Combine synthetic accented speech with non-accented real data (LibriSpeech) and fine-tune a pretrained wav2vec2.0 ASR model. 4) Evaluate on EdAcc spontaneous accented speech, comparing WER against an ASR baseline trained only on non-accented data. The wav2vec2.0 SSL pretraining can use unsupervised accented audio.
- **Key results:** Up to 6.1% relative WER reduction from wav2vec2.0 fine-tuned with synthetic accented speech vs the baseline trained on non-accented data, on the Edinburgh accented-English evaluation.
- **Notes:** ASR-centric study where TTS-generated speech is the augmentation source; relevant as a synthetic-speech-for-ASR data-augmentation study. Verified via arXiv abstract fetch.

### 87. Improving Data Augmentation-based Cross-Speaker Style Transfer for TTS with Singing Voice, Style Filtering, and F0 Matching

_Leonardo B. de M. M. Marques, Lucas H. Ueda, Mario U. Neto, Flavio O. Simoes, Fernando Runstein, Bianca Dal Bo, Paula D. P. Costa · 2024 · INTERSPEECH 2024 (arXiv Oct 2024)_

- **Categories:** C2, C5, C6, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2410.05620) · arXiv:2410.05620
- **Synthetic-data role:** Synthetic expressive training data is created via a pretrained singing voice conversion (SVC) model: expressive source-speaker recordings (including singing voice) are voice-converted into the target speaker's timbre, manufacturing expressive target-speaker data that does not exist (target only has neutral data). A style classifier then filters these synthetic utterances to keep the most expressive ones, and F0 matching corrects pitch range mismatch between source and target. This augmented synthetic set lets the target speaker learn expressive styles from only minutes of real neutral audio.
- **Method:** Cross-speaker style transfer for TTS via data augmentation: convert a source speaker's expressive (and singing) data into a target speaker's voice with SVC, filter the conversions by a style classifier, and apply F0 matching to handle timbral/pitch differences, so a target with only neutral data gains expressive styles.
- **Architecture:** TTS acoustic model trained on augmented data (multi-speaker/multi-style TTS, VITS/Tacotron-style; exact backbone not detailed in abstract) + a pretrained singing-voice-conversion model for augmentation + a style classifier for filtering + an F0-matching/normalization module to align fundamental frequency between speakers.
- **Base models:** A pretrained singing voice conversion (SVC) model used for the augmentation step; a style classifier; underlying TTS model. Specific checkpoints not reported.
- **Datasets:** Expressive multi-style source-speaker data plus singing voice as augmentation sources; target speaker with only a few minutes of neutral data. Real corpus names and hours not specified in the abstract.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Take expressive (and singing) data from source speakers and a target speaker who has only neutral recordings (minutes). 2) Use a pretrained SVC model to convert source expressive/singing utterances into the target speaker's voice, generating synthetic expressive target data. 3) Apply a style classifier to filter the converted utterances, keeping only the most expressive/high-quality samples. 4) Apply F0 matching to mitigate tonal/pitch differences between source and target (align fundamental frequency distributions). 5) Mix the filtered, F0-matched synthetic expressive data with real neutral target data and train/fine-tune the TTS model for cross-speaker style transfer. 6) Evaluate naturalness, style intensity, and speaker similarity. Exact model backbone, training steps, and hyperparameters not in abstract.
- **Key results:** Competitive with state-of-the-art cross-speaker style transfer using only minutes of neutral target data; perceptual improvements in naturalness and style intensity for high-effort vocal styles; F0 matching improves speaker similarity. Specific MOS/CMOS/SIM numbers not given in abstract.
- **Notes:** INTERSPEECH 2024. SVC-as-augmentation plus style filtering plus F0 matching is the novel combination. No public code found; exact metrics need the full paper. Verified via arXiv abstract.

### 88. Improving Pronunciation and Accent Conversion through Knowledge Distillation And Synthetic Ground-Truth from Native TTS

_Tuan Nam Nguyen, Seymanur Akti, Ngoc Quan Pham, Alexander Waibel · 2024 · ICASSP 2025 (arXiv preprint 2024)_

- **Categories:** C2, C5, C6, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2410.14997) · arXiv:2410.14997
- **Synthetic-data role:** A native-pronunciation TTS system generates 'ideal' synthetic ground-truth target audio for each non-native utterance: given the non-native audio plus its transcript, the pipeline produces native-like-pronunciation reference audio that preserves the original speaker's duration and prosody. These synthetic native targets form parallel (accented input -> native target) training pairs that supervise the accent-conversion / pronunciation-correction model, replacing unavailable real native-by-same-speaker recordings. Knowledge distillation transfers the native TTS teacher's pronunciation knowledge into the AC model.
- **Method:** Accent conversion that simultaneously corrects pronunciation and converts accent while preserving speaker identity. Instead of needing parallel native/non-native recordings, it synthesizes the native-pronunciation ground truth with a native TTS system (keeping source duration/prosody) and distills that knowledge, then learns a direct accented->native mapping.
- **Architecture:** End-to-end VITS framework (variational inference + normalizing flows + adversarial training + HiFiGAN-style decoder) for high-quality waveform reconstruction; a native TTS teacher generates synthetic targets; knowledge distillation couples teacher and AC student.
- **Base models:** VITS as the end-to-end backbone; a pretrained native (English) TTS system used as the synthetic-ground-truth generator / teacher. Exact checkpoints not reported.
- **Datasets:** Non-native / accented speech with transcripts as input (specific corpus names/hours not reported in abstract); synthetic native-pronunciation targets generated by the native TTS for each utterance.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Collect non-native audio + transcripts. 2) For each utterance, run a native-pronunciation TTS to synthesize a 'ground-truth' native-accent rendering, constrained to the original utterance's duration and prosody (so only pronunciation/accent changes). 3) Build parallel pairs (accented source -> synthetic native target). 4) Train a VITS-based end-to-end model to map accented input to native-sounding output while preserving speaker identity, using knowledge distillation from the native TTS teacher. 5) Evaluate accent nativeness, pronunciation improvement, and speaker-identity retention. Specific hyperparameters, training steps, and dataset scale are not reported in the abstract.
- **Key results:** Reported qualitatively: produces audio that closely resembles native accents, improves pronunciation, and retains the original speaker's identity. Specific WER/MOS/SIM numbers not given in the available abstract.
- **Notes:** Accepted at ICASSP 2025. Concrete metrics, dataset names/hours, and hyperparameters are not in the abstract; full PDF would be needed to replicate exactly. Verified via arXiv abstract page.

### 89. MacST: Multi-Accent Speech Synthesis via Text Transliteration for Accent Conversion

_Sho Inoue, Shuai Wang, Wanxing Wang, Pengcheng Zhu, Mengxiao Bi, Haizhou Li · 2024 · IEEE ICASSP 2025_

- **Categories:** C4, C5, C6, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2409.09352) · arXiv:2409.09352 · [code](https://github.com/shinshoji01/MacST-project-page)
- **Synthetic-data role:** The entire parallel accent-conversion training corpus is synthetic. An LLM transliterates English text to mimic how a non-native speaker would pronounce it; this transliterated text is then fed to a multilingual TTS system to synthesize accented English speech, producing paired (native, accented) samples from a single speaker. The synthetic parallel corpus is used to train the accent-conversion model.
- **Method:** Create paired multi-accented speech for accent-conversion training without recording real accented speakers: use an LLM to transliterate text (so it sounds accented when spoken), synthesize it with multilingual TTS to get accented speech, then train a sequence-to-sequence accent-conversion reference model on this synthetic parallel corpus.
- **Architecture:** Pipeline: LLM for text transliteration + multilingual (multi-speaker) TTS for accented speech synthesis; a sequence-to-sequence accent-conversion model trained on the resulting synthetic parallel corpus. Specific model sizes not reported.
- **Base models:** Large language model (for transliteration) and a pretrained multilingual TTS system; specific model identities not reported.
- **Datasets:** A synthetically generated parallel accented-English speech corpus produced by the LLM-transliteration + multilingual-TTS pipeline; evaluated on both native and non-native English speakers. Specific real-corpus names/hours not reported.
- **Code:** https://github.com/shinshoji01/MacST-project-page
- **Recipe:** 1) Take English source text. 2) Prompt an LLM to transliterate the text into a form that, when read aloud, produces a target foreign accent. 3) Feed the transliterated text to a multilingual/multi-speaker TTS model to synthesize accented English speech, paired with the native rendering from the same speaker -> synthetic parallel corpus. 4) Train a sequence-to-sequence accent-conversion model on this synthetic parallel data. 5) Evaluate with subjective (accentedness/quality) and objective metrics on native and non-native speakers.
- **Key results:** Subjective and objective evaluations reported showing effective generation of multi-accented speech and accent conversion; specific numeric metric values not surfaced in abstract-level sources.
- **Notes:** Accepted to ICASSP 2025. Project page/code available. Verified via arXiv abstract and project GitHub.

### 90. Maximizing Data Efficiency for Cross-Lingual TTS Adaptation by Self-Supervised Representation Mixing and Embedding Initialization

_Wei-Ping Huang, Sung-Feng Huang, Hung-yi Lee · 2024 · IEEE ICASSP 2024 (paper accepted; abstract page also references the group's ASRU line)_

- **Categories:** C2, C5, C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2402.01692) · arXiv:2402.01692
- **Synthetic-data role:** Two synthetic/pseudo-label mechanisms: (1) pseudo-labels are generated for unlabeled target-language speech, and the NOISY portion of these pseudo labels is REPLACED with self-supervised representations (representation mixing) during fine-tuning, mitigating pseudo-label noise; (2) self-supervised features are injected during pretraining. Synthetic supervision is thus the pseudo-labels / SSL features used to adapt a TTS model to a new language with almost no real labeled data (as little as 4 labeled utterances + 15 min unlabeled).
- **Method:** Cross-lingual TTS language adaptation that maximizes data efficiency by (a) using self-supervised features in pretraining, (b) replacing the noisy part of pseudo labels with self-supervised representations during fine-tuning (representation mixing), and (c) an embedding initialization trick that better leverages unlabeled data when adapting to an unseen target language.
- **Architecture:** Sequence-to-sequence multi-speaker/multilingual neural TTS (Tacotron/transformer-style acoustic model with a neural vocoder), augmented with a self-supervised speech representation extractor; phoneme/character embedding tables initialized via the proposed embedding-initialization scheme.
- **Base models:** Pretrained multilingual TTS backbone and a pretrained self-supervised speech model used to extract SSL features for representation mixing; adapts/fine-tunes from these. Specific SSL checkpoint not stated in abstract.
- **Datasets:** Multilingual TTS corpora for pretraining; extremely low-resource target-language adaptation set of only 4 labeled utterances plus 15 minutes of unlabeled speech. Exact corpus names/hours not given in abstract.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Pretrain a multilingual TTS model, incorporating self-supervised features. 2) For a new (unseen) language, collect minimal data: ~4 labeled utterances and ~15 min unlabeled audio. 3) Generate pseudo labels for the unlabeled speech using the pretrained model. 4) During fine-tuning, identify the noisy/unreliable portion of the pseudo labels and replace it with self-supervised representations (representation mixing). 5) Apply the embedding-initialization trick to seed the new language's token embeddings so unlabeled data is used effectively. 6) Fine-tune and evaluate intelligibility/naturalness in the target language. Repeat with more data to show the method still beats conventional adaptation.
- **Key results:** Produces intelligible speech in an unseen language from only 4 labeled utterances + 15 minutes of unlabeled data, and continues to surpass conventional adaptation techniques even as more data becomes available. Specific WER/MOS numbers not in abstract.
- **Notes:** Hung-yi Lee group (NTU). Sits at the intersection of fine-tuning with synthetic/pseudo-labels (2), self-training/pseudo-labeling (5), and multilingual TTS (6). Abstract page is thin on quantitative detail; metrics in the full ICASSP/ASRU paper.

### 91. Multi-Scale Accent Modeling and Disentangling for Multi-Speaker Multi-Accent Text-to-Speech Synthesis

_Xuehao Zhou, Mingyang Zhang, Yi Zhou, Zhizheng Wu, Haizhou Li · 2024 · arXiv preprint (also submitted to a speech venue)_

- **Categories:** C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2406.10844) · arXiv:2406.10844
- **Synthetic-data role:** No synthetic/generated training corpus is used. The model generates multi-speaker multi-accent speech (synthetic speech as output) and disentangles speaker from accent so a speaker can be rendered in unseen accents (speaker-independent accent control), but it does not train on machine-generated/pseudo-labeled audio. Included as a multi-accent/speaker-disentanglement TTS reference; not a synthetic-data-for-training paper.
- **Method:** Multi-scale accent modeling for multi-speaker multi-accent TTS: models accent variation at both utterance (global) level and phoneme (local) level, and disentangles speaker identity from accent via speaker embeddings, enabling speaker-independent accent control (render any speaker in a target accent while preserving identity). A local accent predictor allows generation directly from phoneme inputs.
- **Architecture:** Acoustic-model-based TTS (FastSpeech2-style non-autoregressive sequence-to-sequence with phoneme inputs and explicit duration/variance modeling), augmented with utterance-level and phoneme-level accent representations, speaker embeddings, and accent disentanglement modules; neural vocoder for waveform generation. Specific component sizes not stated in fetched content.
- **Base models:** not reported (standard TTS acoustic model + neural vocoder; no pretrained LM/teacher TTS explicitly named in the abstract).
- **Datasets:** An English accented speech corpus (multi-speaker, multi-accent); specific dataset names/hours not stated in the fetched abstract (accent-corpus benchmarks such as L2-ARCTIC/VCTK-type accented data are typical for this task but were not confirmed from the fetched content).
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Prepare a multi-speaker multi-accent English corpus with accent and speaker labels. 2) Train a FastSpeech2-style TTS with two accent modeling branches: a global utterance-level accent embedding and a local phoneme-level accent representation, plus a speaker embedding. 3) Apply disentanglement so accent representations are independent of speaker identity (speaker-independent accent control). 4) Train a local accent predictor that predicts phoneme-level accent from phoneme input, enabling direct phoneme-to-speech generation in a chosen accent. 5) Vocode to waveform. Exact losses/hyperparameters not in fetched content.
- **Key results:** Outperforms baseline systems in speech quality and accent rendering for multi-speaker multi-accent synthesis; ablations validate the contributions of global and local accent modeling and disentanglement. Specific MOS/objective numbers not captured in fetched excerpt.
- **Notes:** Title, authors, and arXiv id confirmed. Focus is accent modeling/disentanglement and multilingual/multi-accent rendering (category 6), not synthetic data generation.

### 92. Natural Language Guidance of High-Fidelity Text-to-Speech with Synthetic Annotations

_Dan Lyth, Simon King · 2024 · arXiv preprint (Stability AI / University of Edinburgh). Basis for HuggingFace Parler-TTS and Data-Speech._

- **Categories:** C4, C5, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2402.01912) · arXiv:2402.01912 · [code](https://text-description-to-speech.com/)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Core contribution is SYNTHETIC TEXT ANNOTATIONS, not synthetic audio. The audio is real (45k+ hours), but every natural-language style/condition description used for conditioning is machine-generated: classifiers/extractors automatically label gender, accent (86%-accurate accent classifier over 53 accents trained on EdAcc/VCTK/VoxPopuli), SNR and C50 reverberation (Brouhaha), pitch (PENN), and speaking rate (phoneme-count/duration via g2p). Continuous attributes are quantized into 7 bins, then a large language model (Stable Beluga 2.5) is prompted to convert the tags into full natural-language description sentences. This fully-automatic pipeline replaces human labels and enables scaling text descriptions to 45k+ hours for the first time.
- **Method:** Enable natural-language (text-prompt) control of TTS without reference speech by automatically generating descriptive annotations for a very large speech corpus and training a speech language model conditioned on those descriptions. Bridges reference-speech conditioning and free-text prompting via scalable synthetic annotation.
- **Architecture:** Autoregressive transformer language model over neural-audio-codec tokens. Codec = Descript Audio Codec (DAC) at 44.1 kHz, 86 Hz frame rate, 9 codebooks. Built on Meta AudioCraft's LM (MusicGen/AudioGen-style delay-pattern multi-codebook modeling). Transcript is provided as prefix; the natural-language description conditions generation via cross-attention. (HF reproduction Parler-TTS: ~880M mini, ~2.2B large.)
- **Base models:** Initializes from / adapts Meta AudioCraft (MusicGen-style) LM codebase; DAC neural audio codec; Stable Beluga 2.5 LLM used to write descriptions; a language-identification embedding model + trained accent classifier; Brouhaha (SNR/C50), PENN (pitch) for label extraction.
- **Datasets:** Real audio: Multilingual LibriSpeech (MLS) English ~45,000 hours + LibriTTS-R ~585 hours (~45.5k h total). Each utterance receives a machine-generated natural-language description (synthetic annotation). Auxiliary classifier training data: EdAcc, VCTK, VoxPopuli (53 accents).
- **Code:** Project/samples: https://text-description-to-speech.com/ ; official reproduction: https://github.com/huggingface/parler-tts and Data-Speech annotation pipeline https://github.com/huggingface/dataspeech ; models at https://huggingface.co/parler-tts
- **Recipe:** Annotation pipeline (synthetic): 1) Run extractors per utterance: gender, accent classifier (embeddings from a language-ID model; 86% test acc; trained on EdAcc/VCTK/VoxPopuli, 53 accents), SNR + C50 reverberation via Brouhaha, pitch via PENN, speaking rate = phoneme_count/duration using g2p. 2) Quantize continuous attributes into 7 discrete bins (e.g. very low/low/.../very high). 3) Prompt an LLM (Stable Beluga 2.5) with the tag set to write a fluent natural-language description sentence. Training: 4) Tokenize audio with DAC (44.1kHz, 9 codebooks, 86Hz). 5) Train an AudioCraft-style autoregressive transformer LM with multi-codebook delay-pattern decoding; condition on the transcript (prefix) and the synthetic description (cross-attention). 6) Train on ~45.5k h (MLS + LibriTTS-R). Inference: provide transcript + free-text style/condition description; sample codec tokens; decode with DAC.
- **Key results:** Naturalness MOS 3.92 vs Audiobox 2.79; description-relevance score 3.88 vs Audiobox 3.19. Attribute controllability via classifiers on generated speech: gender 94% accuracy, accent 68% accuracy. Generates high-fidelity speech across diverse accents, prosodic styles, channel and acoustic conditions from a single model; reported to significantly outperform recent work. No WER reported in the paper.
- **Notes:** Foundational synthetic-annotation paper; spawned the open Parler-TTS + Data-Speech ecosystem (Apache-2.0). Synthetic = the descriptions/labels, audio is real, so this is a partially-synthetically-built corpus (categories 4 LLM-generated text descriptions, 5 automatic/pseudo-labeling, 7 corpus partially synthetically generated).

### 93. Preference Alignment Improves Language Model-Based TTS

_Jinchuan Tian, Chunlei Zhang (corresponding), Jiatong Shi, Hao Zhang, Jianwei Yu, Shinji Watanabe, Dong Yu · 2024 · arXiv preprint / IEEE (interns at Tencent AI Lab)_

- **Categories:** C3, C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2409.12403) · arXiv:2409.12403 · [code](https://github.com/espnet/espnet)
- **Synthetic-data role:** On-policy synthetic generations form the preference data. For each (text, reference-speech) condition the model samples 10 utterances; all generated samples are ranked by automatic preference metrics, and the top 20% (best) and bottom 20% (worst) are selected as chosen/rejected pairs for DPO-style alignment. All preference-training audio is model-generated (self-sampled), making this a self-training / synthetic-preference pipeline.
- **Method:** A systematic empirical study showing that preference alignment algorithms (chiefly DPO) consistently improve language-model-based zero-shot TTS across intelligibility, speaker similarity, and proxy subjective quality, including in low-resource and out-of-domain settings.
- **Architecture:** 1.15B-parameter Multi-Scale Transformer language-model TTS over a neural audio codec; audio tokenized at 50 frames/second with 8 codes per frame (RVQ-style). Alignment applied as post-training on top of this LM.
- **Base models:** Pre-trained 1.15B Multi-Scale Transformer codec-LM TTS (trained on ~55k h). Reward/metric models: Whisper-large (WER), RawNet speaker embeddings (SPK_SIM), UTMOS (proxy MOS).
- **Datasets:** Real training: ~55,000 hours English from LibriSpeech, GigaSpeech, and Multilingual LibriSpeech. Preference data: model self-generated samples (10 per condition) ranked and filtered into chosen/rejected pairs. Evaluation includes in-domain and out-of-domain/low-resource conditions.
- **Code:** https://github.com/espnet/espnet (stated: 'Code will be released in ESPnet')
- **Recipe:** 1) Pre-train a 1.15B codec-LM TTS on ~55k h (LibriSpeech + GigaSpeech + MLS), 50 fps codec with 8 codes/frame. 2) Generate preference data: for each condition (same text + same reference speech) sample 10 utterances from the base model. 3) Score each sample with WER (Whisper-large), SPK_SIM (RawNet embeddings), Proxy MOS (UTMOS). 4) Rank samples; select top 20% as chosen and bottom 20% as rejected to build preference pairs. 5) Run preference alignment, primarily DPO (length normalization explored but ultimately not used); also benchmark KTO, SimPO, IPO, ORPO. 6) Configuration D3 combines all three metrics into a composite ranking for balanced gains. 7) Evaluate; repeat in low-resource and out-of-domain regimes.
- **Key results:** With the 1.15B model, alignment improves all axes: WER 4.5 -> 3.0, speaker similarity 0.635 -> 0.667, Proxy MOS 3.80 -> 4.23, with SIM and proxy-MOS surpassing human ground truth in some evaluations. Gains hold in low-resource and out-of-domain settings. DPO is the strongest among the compared alignment algorithms.
- **Notes:** Authors interns at Tencent AI Lab; code release planned in ESPnet (verify availability). Demonstrates self-generated synthetic data + automatic-metric ranking is sufficient to build effective DPO preference pairs without human labels.

### 94. Robust Zero-Shot Text-to-Speech Synthesis with Reverse Inference Optimization

_Yuchen Hu, Chen Chen, Siyin Wang, Eng Siong Chng, Chao Zhang · 2024 · arXiv preprint (work in progress, submitted Jul 2024); demo page yuchen005.github.io/RIO-TTS-demos_

- **Categories:** C3, C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2407.02243) · arXiv:2407.02243 · [code](https://yuchen005.github.io/RIO-TTS-demos/)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Self-generated training data with automatic (model-derived) preference labels: the TTS system samples speech from its own outputs, then automatically annotates quality via reverse inference (does the generated speech work well as a prompt for regenerating the same content?). Good/bad exemplars selected this way form the preference data for RLHF/DPO-style optimization, with no human annotation and no trained reward model. Both 'chosen' and 'rejected' samples are synthetic model outputs.
- **Method:** RIO (Reverse Inference Optimization) improves robustness of autoregressive zero-shot TTS via a Bayesian-inspired self-selection criterion: a high-quality generated sample should itself serve as an effective prompt for regenerating the same speech. Using reverse-inference scoring to pick exemplars, RIO runs a sampling -> automatic annotating -> learning (preference optimization) loop that steers the model toward robustness and drastically reduces bad cases.
- **Architecture:** Autoregressive neural-codec zero-shot TTS LM (VoiceCraft backbone: a transformer LM over EnCodec-style discrete acoustic tokens with causal token-infilling). Optimized with an RLHF/DPO-style preference objective using reverse-inference-selected pairs (no separate reward model or critic).
- **Base models:** Backbone = VoiceCraft, pretrained on GigaSpeech (~9k hours of audiobooks, podcasts, YouTube at 16 kHz). EnCodec-style neural audio codec for tokenization.
- **Datasets:** Pretraining backbone: GigaSpeech ~9k hours. RIO optimization data: LibriTTS (no overlap with GigaSpeech), with speech samples self-generated from LibriTTS prompts/texts and auto-annotated by reverse inference. Evaluation on standard zero-shot TTS benchmarks (LibriTTS/LibriSpeech-derived test sets).
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Take a pretrained AR codec TTS backbone (VoiceCraft, GigaSpeech-pretrained). 2) Sampling: generate multiple speech samples per LibriTTS prompt/text. 3) Automatic annotating via reverse inference: feed each generated sample back as the prompt to regenerate the target content; high-quality regeneration (high consistency/intelligibility/similarity) labels it chosen, else rejected, applying a Bayesian posterior view that a good output is a good conditioning prompt. 4) Learning: optimize the policy with RLHF/DPO-style preference loss on chosen/rejected pairs, KL-regularized to the reference; iterate. No reward model or human preference data needed. 5) Evaluate MOS, WER, SIM, and bad-case ratio vs ground-truth-prompt upper bound.
- **Key results:** Without human annotation, RIO improves MOS, WER, and SIM over the base model and over other optimization baselines (e.g., standard DPO/preference baselines), and reduces the ratio of bad cases to near-zero, approaching the robustness of using ground-truth prompts.
- **Notes:** Distinctive contribution is reward-model-free, human-annotation-free preference data construction via reverse inference (self-distilled preference learning). Demo page exists; no released training code found. VoiceCraft backbone is open-source, aiding partial replication.

### 95. Seed-TTS: A Family of High-Quality Versatile Speech Generation Models

_Philip Anastassiou et al. (ByteDance Seed team, 46 authors) · 2024 · arXiv preprint (technical report)_

- **Categories:** C2, C3, C5, C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2406.02430) · arXiv:2406.02430 · [code](https://bytedancespeech.github.io/seedtts_tech_report/)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Generated/synthetic data appears in three roles: (1) a self-distillation method for speech factorization, where the model generates factorized representations used to train the disentangled (timbre/content) system enabling controllable voice conversion; (2) a reinforcement-learning stage that uses the model's own generations scored by reward signals to improve robustness, speaker similarity, and controllability; (3) outputs that match ground-truth human speech. Specific generated-data volumes are not disclosed.
- **Method:** A family of large-scale versatile speech-generation foundation models for zero-shot in-context generation (voice cloning), with an autoregressive codec-LM variant and a non-autoregressive fully diffusion variant (Seed-TTS-DiT), plus self-distillation for speech factorization and an RL post-training stage.
- **Architecture:** Two variants. (1) Seed-TTS: large-scale autoregressive language model over a neural speech/audio codec (speech tokenizer -> AR LM -> token decoder/vocoder). (2) Seed-TTS-DiT: fully diffusion-based non-autoregressive model that directly predicts output speech latent representations end-to-end, with no separate phoneme-duration prediction module. Parameter counts not disclosed.
- **Base models:** Proprietary in-house neural audio codec and tokenizer; trained at large scale from scratch (no public pretrained init reported). RL reward models/verifiers not specified publicly.
- **Datasets:** Large-scale internal training data (names, hours, scale undisclosed). Evaluation on standard zero-shot TTS benchmarks (objective WER/SIM and subjective CMOS/MOS).
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** High-level (details proprietary): 1) Tokenize speech with a neural codec; train a large AR LM for prompt-conditioned zero-shot generation. 2) Apply self-distillation to factorize speech attributes (timbre vs content) enabling controllable voice conversion. 3) Train Seed-TTS-DiT diffusion model to directly predict speech latents end-to-end without explicit duration estimation. 4) Run an RL post-training stage to improve robustness, speaker similarity, and controllability using reward signals over the model's own generations. 5) Optionally fine-tune per application to raise subjective quality above the base in-context model. Exact hyperparameters, data scale, and reward definitions are not released.
- **Key results:** Achieves speaker similarity and naturalness matching ground-truth human speech on objective and subjective evaluations for zero-shot generation; per-application fine-tuning further raises subjective scores. Precise WER/SIM/CMOS numbers in the full report but not in the abstract; widely cited SOTA foundation TTS model.
- **Notes:** Industry technical report (ByteDance); weights/code not open-sourced and training data undisclosed, so full replication is impossible from the paper alone. Strong influence on later codec-LM and DiT TTS work.

### 96. SpeechAlign: Aligning Speech Generation to Human Preferences

_Dong Zhang, Zhaowei Li, Shimin Li, Xin Zhang, Pengyu Wang, Yaqian Zhou, Xipeng Qiu · 2024 · NeurIPS 2024_

- **Categories:** C2, C3
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2404.05600) · arXiv:2404.05600 · [code](https://github.com/0nutation/SpeechGPT)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Preference pairs are built by contrasting 'golden' (ground-truth-derived) codec tokens against the model's own synthetic codec tokens for the same utterances, addressing the train-inference distribution gap. Synthetic (model-generated) tokens are the 'rejected' side and golden tokens the 'chosen' side for DPO/RLHF; the loop iterates, regenerating synthetic tokens from the improved model each round.
- **Method:** SpeechAlign closes the train-inference distribution gap in codec language models via iterative preference optimization. It builds a preference codec dataset (golden codec tokens as chosen vs synthetic/model-generated tokens as rejected), then applies preference optimization (DPO, plus comparisons to CoH, RLHF-PPO, Best-of-N) to align the codec LM toward ground-truth-like generations, repeating for continual self-improvement.
- **Architecture:** Neural codec language model: an autoregressive codec LM (built on SpeechGPT) over discrete audio codec tokens, plus a preference-optimization layer using DPO (and CoH, RLHF-PPO, Best-of-N variants).
- **Base models:** Pretrained SpeechGPT as the AR codec LM, further fine-tuned on LibriSpeech; a neural audio codec for token discretization.
- **Datasets:** LibriSpeech for continue-finetuning the AR model; preference codec dataset built from 50k speech-text pairs randomly sampled from LibriSpeech train (golden vs synthetic codec tokens).
- **Code:** https://github.com/0nutation/SpeechGPT
- **Recipe:** 1) Fine-tune pretrained SpeechGPT (AR codec LM) on LibriSpeech. 2) Sample 50k speech-text pairs from LibriSpeech train; for each obtain golden codec tokens (encode ground-truth audio) and synthetic codec tokens (model-generated), forming chosen vs rejected pairs targeting the distribution gap. 3) Apply preference optimization, primarily DPO (also CoH, RLHF-PPO, Best-of-N). 4) Iterate: regenerate synthetic tokens with the improved model, rebuild preference pairs, re-optimize (Iter1, Iter2, Iter3...). 5) Evaluate win rate, WER, speaker similarity each iteration.
- **Key results:** SpeechAlign-DPO improves progressively: by Iteration 3, WER reduced ~0.8 vs baseline and speaker similarity raised to ~0.9. SpeechAlign-BoN, SpeechAlign-RLHF-PPO, and SpeechAlign-DPO-Iter1 all significantly beat baseline in win rates. Generalizes to smaller models; enables continuous self-improvement.
- **Notes:** NeurIPS 2024. Code under SpeechGPT repo (github.com/0nutation/SpeechGPT). Among the first to apply DPO/RLHF-style preference optimization to codec speech LMs; it is the 'utterance-level optimization' baseline that W3AR (paper 1) compares against.

### 97. Towards Controllable Speech Synthesis in the Era of Large Language Models: A Systematic Survey

_Tianxin Xie, Yan Rong, Pengfei Zhang, Wenwu Wang, Li Liu · 2024 · EMNLP 2025 (Main Conference); arXiv Dec 2024_

- **Categories:** C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2412.06602) · arXiv:2412.06602 · [code](https://github.com/imxtx/awesome-controllable-speech-synthesis)
- **Synthetic-data role:** As a survey it does not generate data itself; it reviews methods that use natural-language prompts / LLM-based control and catalogs controllable-TTS datasets and evaluation. Synthetic-data techniques (e.g., LLM-generated prompts, synthetic speaker/style control) appear within the surveyed methods rather than as the survey's own contribution.
- **Method:** First comprehensive systematic survey of controllable TTS, tracing the field from traditional control techniques to LLM/diffusion-era natural-language prompt control. Categorizes model architectures, control strategies, and feature representations, and summarizes challenges, datasets, and evaluation methodologies for fine-grained control over emotion, timbre, and style.
- **Architecture:** Survey (no model). Taxonomy spans autoregressive LM + neural codec systems, diffusion/flow-matching acoustic models, VITS-style end-to-end models, GAN/HiFiGAN vocoders, and prompt/LLM-based control front-ends as covered categories.
- **Base models:** not reported (survey)
- **Datasets:** Catalogs controllable/expressive TTS datasets used across the field (review-level summary); no new dataset introduced.
- **Code:** https://github.com/imxtx/awesome-controllable-speech-synthesis ; ACL Anthology https://aclanthology.org/2025.emnlp-main.40/
- **Recipe:** Not applicable (literature survey). Reproduction = follow the surveyed taxonomy: pick a control paradigm (label/reference/natural-language prompt), choose a backbone (codec-LM, diffusion, or VITS-style), and select control-feature representations; the curated GitHub repo tracks papers, datasets, and tools.
- **Key results:** No empirical metrics; provides taxonomy, dataset/evaluation summary, and open-challenge discussion. Positioned as the first systematic survey in controllable speech synthesis.
- **Notes:** Living survey with an actively maintained GitHub paper list. Useful as an index into categories 1-7 of synthetic-data-for-TTS work, though it is not itself a synthetic-data method.

### 98. VoxInstruct: Expressive Human Instruction-to-Speech Generation with Unified Multilingual Codec Language Modelling

_Yixuan Zhou, Xiaoyu Qin, Zeyu Jin, Shuoyi Zhou, Shun Lei, Songtao Zhou, Zhiyong Wu, Jia Jia · 2024 · ACM Multimedia 2024_

- **Categories:** C4, C6, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2408.15676) · arXiv:2408.15676 · [code](https://github.com/thuhcsi/VoxInstruct)
- **Synthetic-data role:** LLM-generated training text: instruction data (combined spoken content + descriptive style info written as free natural language) is synthesized by sampling speech attributes randomly and then using an LLM to rewrite them into natural human instructions (explicitly done for Chinese instructions, multilingual). These synthetic instructions are paired with real speech to train the unified instruction-to-speech model.
- **Method:** Reframes TTS as a general human-instruction-to-speech task: a single free-form natural-language instruction conveys both what to say and how to say it, instead of separate content and style prompts. A unified multilingual codec language model uses speech semantic tokens as intermediate instruction-to-content guidance and multiple Classifier-Free Guidance (CFG) strategies to strengthen instruction following.
- **Architecture:** Autoregressive codec language model built on a LLaMA-based LLM backbone; a pretrained mT5 text encoder for multilingual instruction understanding; HuBERT + k-means semantic tokens as intermediate (content-bearing, prosody-free) representation; neural audio codec (EnCodec) for acoustic tokens with Vocos as the acoustic decoder/vocoder (replacing the EnCodec decoder for better reconstruction); multiple CFG strategies at inference.
- **Base models:** LLaMA (LM backbone), mT5 (text encoder), HuBERT + k-means (semantic tokenizer), EnCodec (acoustic codec), Vocos (vocoder). LLM used to generate/rewrite the instruction dataset.
- **Datasets:** Multilingual speech (English + Chinese) paired with synthesized natural-language instructions; Chinese instructions generated by random attribute sampling + LLM rewriting. Specific hour counts not stated in the abstract.
- **Code:** https://github.com/thuhcsi/VoxInstruct (demo: voxinstruct.github.io/VoxInstruct/)
- **Recipe:** 1) Curate multilingual speech with attribute labels. 2) Construct instruction dataset: randomly sample speech attributes, then prompt an LLM to rewrite them into free-form natural-language human instructions (combining content + style), notably for Chinese. 3) Extract HuBERT+k-means semantic tokens (content guidance) and EnCodec acoustic tokens (targets). 4) Train a LLaMA-based codec LM, conditioned via mT5-encoded instructions, to first predict semantic tokens then acoustic tokens. 5) Apply multiple Classifier-Free Guidance strategies during training/inference to boost instruction adherence. 6) Decode acoustic tokens with Vocos vocoder.
- **Key results:** Demonstrates first-of-its-kind unified instruction-to-speech with expressive, multilingual, controllable generation and the ability to combine speech prompts with descriptive instructions; abstract reports qualitative superiority but no specific numeric MOS/WER in the fetched text.
- **Notes:** Accepted ACM Multimedia 2024. Synthetic-data role is LLM-rewritten instruction text (category 4/7); the speech audio is real.

### 99. XTTS: a Massively Multilingual Zero-Shot Text-to-Speech Model

_Edresson Casanova, Kelly Davis, Eren Golge, Gorkem Goknar, Iulian Gulea, Logan Hart, Aya Aljafari, Joshua Meyer, Reuben Morais, Samuel Olayemi, Julian Weber (Coqui) · 2024 · Interspeech 2024 (arXiv 2024)_

- **Categories:** C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2406.04904) · arXiv:2406.04904 · [code](https://github.com/coqui-ai/TTS)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Not a primary contribution. XTTS is trained on real recorded multilingual corpora (LibriTTS-R, LibriLight, Common Voice, internal data); the abstract/paper do not report training on synthetic speech. The model itself is a generator of synthetic speech and is widely used downstream to produce synthetic data, but within this paper synthetic data is not used to train XTTS.
- **Method:** A massively multilingual (16 languages) zero-shot TTS that supports cross-language voice cloning from short reference audio. Built on the Tortoise architecture with novel modifications for multilingual training and improved voice cloning, reaching SOTA in most languages while remaining streaming-capable. Combines a discrete audio codec, an autoregressive language-model conditioning encoder, and a GAN vocoder.
- **Architecture:** Three components: (1) VQ-VAE codec (~13M params) encoding mel-spectrograms at 21.53 Hz, 1 codebook of 8192 codes filtered to the 1024 most frequent. (2) GPT-2 style decoder-only transformer (~443M params) with a custom 6681-token BPE text tokenizer, conditioned by a Perceiver Resampler producing 32 x 1024-dim embeddings from reference audio; six 16-head scaled-dot-product attention layers. (3) HiFi-GAN decoder/vocoder (~26M params) taking GPT-2 latents, conditioned with H/ASP speaker embeddings via linear projection at upsampling layers, trained with a Speaker Consistency Loss.
- **Base models:** Tortoise TTS architecture as the starting point (modified). H/ASP speaker encoder for speaker conditioning. Trained from data rather than from another pretrained LM.
- **Datasets:** 27,281.6 hours across 16 languages. English 14,513.1 h; German 3,584.4; Portuguese 2,386.8; French 2,215.5; Spanish 1,514.3; Italian 1,296.6; Korean 539.1; Arabic 240.9; Chinese 233.9; Polish 198.8; Turkish 165.3; Russian 147.1; Dutch 74.1; Hungarian 62.0; Japanese 57.3; Czech 52.4. Sources: LibriTTS-R, LibriLight, Common Voice, plus internal datasets.
- **Code:** https://github.com/coqui-ai/TTS ; weights https://huggingface.co/coqui/XTTS-v2 ; demo https://edresson.github.io/XTTS/ ; eval code https://github.com/Edresson/ZS-TTS-Evaluation
