At inference you sample a fresh embedding from this learned prior to produce a brand-new speaker, then run standard TTS conditioned on it. TTS and the embedding prior are trained jointly end to end.
- **Architecture:** Recurrent attention-based (Tacotron-style) autoregressive TTS acoustic model predicting mel spectrograms, conditioned on a speaker embedding; a learned probabilistic speaker-embedding prior (mixture distribution, optionally conditioned on speaker metadata) over the embedding table; separate neural vocoder for waveform. No transfer from a pretrained speaker-ID/ASV network is required (a deliberate contrast to d-vector/x-vector transfer).
- **Base models:** Builds on Tacotron-style attention TTS; trained from scratch jointly with the speaker prior. No pretrained speaker-verification model used for embeddings (by design).
- **Datasets:** Multi-speaker English speech corpora (proprietary Google internal multi-speaker data plus public multi-speaker sets); exact hours not reported in abstract. Evaluation uses held-out and newly sampled (synthetic) speakers.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Train a multi-speaker Tacotron-style TTS consuming a continuous speaker embedding. 2) Replace the fixed per-speaker embedding lookup with a learned prior p(embedding | metadata) parameterized as a mixture distribution; optimize TTS reconstruction loss plus embedding prior likelihood jointly. 3) Optionally condition the prior on categorical metadata (region, gender) for controllable sampling. 4) At inference, sample a novel embedding from the prior, feed to TTS + vocoder to synthesize a new speaker. 5) Evaluate with proposed objective speaker-similarity/novelty metrics (shown to correlate with human similarity judgments) plus subjective MOS/similarity listening tests. Layer sizes and training steps not reported in abstract.
- **Key results:** Demonstrates sampling of diverse, novel speakers; proposes objective metrics for novelty and speaker similarity shown to correlate with human perception; subjective listening tests assess naturalness and that sampled speakers are perceived as distinct/novel. Exact MOS numbers not reported in fetched abstract.
- **Notes:** Foundational reference for synthetic speaker generation (category 6). Google/DeepMind authors; proprietary data limits exact replication.

### 124. SynthASR: Unlocking Synthetic Data for Speech Recognition

_Amin Fazel, Wei Yang, Yulan Liu, Roberto Barra-Chicote, Yixiong Meng, Roland Maas, Jasha Droppo (Amazon Alexa) · 2021 · Interspeech 2021_

- **Categories:** C2, C5, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2106.07803) · arXiv:2106.07803
- **Synthetic-data role:** TTS-synthesized speech is the primary training data for a new ASR domain (recognizing medication names) where real production audio is sparse or unavailable. Synthetic audio is generated from text by state-of-the-art near-human-naturalness TTS engines and used to teach the RNN-T to recognize the new vocabulary, then mixed with existing real data to avoid catastrophic forgetting on general domains. Synthetic data substitutes for hard-to-collect real data.
- **Method:** Treat synthetic speech as a way to bootstrap ASR for low-resource / new application domains, and use a continual-learning multi-stage training recipe to add the new (synthetic) domain without degrading recognition on pre-existing real-data domains. The recipe explicitly counters the train/test mismatch and catastrophic forgetting that arise when training partly on synthetic audio.
- **Architecture:** End-to-end RNN-Transducer (RNN-T) ASR model (encoder/prediction-network/joint-network). Synthetic audio produced by an external multi-style TTS pipeline; exact TTS/vocoder sizes not reported in the abstract.
- **Base models:** Builds on a pre-trained baseline RNN-T ASR model (general-purpose, trained on real data) which is then continually adapted; synthetic audio comes from a separate production TTS engine. Specific TTS model identity not reported.
- **Datasets:** In-house Amazon datasets: a new medication-name recognition application (data sparse, augmented with TTS-synthesized utterances of medication-name text) plus existing general ASR application data (real). Hours not reported.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Start from a pre-trained RNN-T baseline. 2) Generate synthetic speech for the new domain by feeding target text (e.g., medication names) to a high-naturalness TTS engine. 3) Apply a multi-stage continual-learning strategy combining: (a) weighted multi-style training (up-weight new-domain/synthetic data while retaining real general data), (b) data augmentation on the synthetic audio to reduce synthetic-real mismatch, (c) encoder freezing (freeze lower/encoder layers to preserve acoustic knowledge learned from real data), and (d) parameter regularization to penalize drift from the base model. 4) Evaluate on both the new medication application and the original general applications to confirm no regression. Exact hyperparameters/hours not reported.
- **Key results:** More than 65% relative WER improvement on the new medication-name recognition application versus the baseline, with no degradation on existing general ASR applications. Exact absolute WER values not reported in the abstract.
- **Notes:** Industrial/in-house data, not publicly released. Core contribution is the catastrophic-forgetting mitigation recipe for training ASR on synthetic data, not a new TTS model. Accepted Interspeech 2021.

### 125. Can Speaker Augmentation Improve Multi-Speaker End-to-End TTS?

_Erica Cooper, Cheng-I Lai, Yusuke Yasuda, Junichi Yamagishi · 2020 · Interspeech 2020_

- **Categories:** C6, C5, C2
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2005.01245) · arXiv:2005.01245
- **Synthetic-data role:** Two forms of augmentation. (1) Speaker augmentation: ARTIFICIAL speakers are created (e.g. perturbation of existing utterances treated as new speaker identities) to enrich the speaker-embedding space of a multi-speaker TTS. (2) Data augmentation with low-quality / found data: extra non-studio corpora are added purely as augmentation while assuming the target high-quality speaker has limited data; channel and dialect factors are modeled as extra conditioning so low-quality augmentation does not corrupt output quality.
- **Method:** Build a multi-speaker Tacotron2 TTS conditioned on speaker embeddings transferred from a separately trained ASV (speaker verification) network, then test whether augmenting with artificial speakers and low-quality found data improves speaker similarity and dialect coverage. Adds channel and dialect conditioning so the model absorbs noisy augmentation data without degrading studio-quality output.
- **Architecture:** Tacotron2 seq2seq acoustic model (encoder + location-sensitive attention + autoregressive mel decoder) modified with external d-vector/x-vector speaker embeddings from a pretrained ASV model, plus learned channel and dialect embedding/code conditioning; neural vocoder for waveform synthesis. Warm-start training from a base multi-speaker model.
- **Base models:** Modified Tacotron2; speaker embeddings transferred from a separately trained Automatic Speaker Verification (ASV) network; warm-started from a pretrained multi-speaker TTS checkpoint.
- **Datasets:** VCTK corpus (multi-speaker English, ~109 speakers, studio quality) as the high-quality base; additional low-quality / found multi-accent corpora used only for speaker augmentation; artificial speakers created from these. Exact hours not all reported.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Train Tacotron2 multi-speaker on VCTK conditioned on ASV-derived speaker embeddings (transfer-learned, not jointly learned). 2) Create artificial speakers by perturbing existing speakers (treated as distinct embeddings) and/or adding low-quality external speakers, expanding the augmentation-only speaker set. 3) Add channel and dialect conditioning codes so the decoder factors out recording-channel and dialect variation from augmentation data; at inference request clean-channel output. 4) Warm-start from the base model, then continue training with the augmented speaker set. 5) Evaluate with large-scale subjective listening tests (naturalness MOS, speaker similarity) and an objective distance metric for dialect-synthesis fidelity. Specific learning rates/steps not reported in abstract.
- **Key results:** Large-scale listening tests assess naturalness, speaker similarity, and dialect similarity; a distance metric quantifies dialect synthesis. Speaker augmentation plus channel/dialect modeling analyzed for whether they improve similarity vs a plain multi-speaker Tacotron2 baseline; conditional/mixed gains reported. Exact MOS figures not in fetched abstract.
- **Notes:** MIT/NII collaboration. Core idea: artificial-speaker augmentation + found-data augmentation with channel/dialect disentangling. Relevant to categories 6 (multilingual/accent), 5 (augmentation), 2 (fine-tune/warm-start).

### 126. Improving Low Resource Code-switched ASR using Augmented Code-switched TTS

_Yash Sharma, Basil Abraham, Karan Taneja, Preethi Jyothi · 2020 · Interspeech 2020 (arXiv preprint)_

- **Categories:** C2, C4, C5, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2010.05549) · arXiv:2010.05549
- **Synthetic-data role:** Code-switched (Hindi-English) speech is synthesized by a code-switched TTS system from code-switched text and used as augmentation data to train/improve a low-resource code-switched ASR model. Because naively adding synthetic audio gives limited gains, two techniques are introduced to make the synthetic speech more useful: Mixup (linear interpolation between synthetic-TTS and real samples) and a new loss that better weights the synthetic/code-switched data.
- **Method:** Augment a low-resource code-switched ASR system with TTS-generated code-switched speech, and crucially propose how to leverage it: apply Mixup between TTS and real samples and a new loss function so the noisy synthetic data improves rather than harms ASR, with focus on the code-switching points themselves.
- **Architecture:** ASR: transformer/sequence-to-sequence multilingual acoustic model (reported as transformer-based encoder). Code-switched TTS used to generate the synthetic speech (Tacotron-2-style acoustic model + WaveGlow/neural vocoder per fetched detail). Training augmentations: Mixup + custom weighted loss.
- **Base models:** Code-switched TTS (Tacotron-2 + WaveGlow-style vocoder) used to generate augmentation audio; ASR built on a transformer-based multilingual backbone. Specific pretrained checkpoints not reported.
- **Datasets:** Hindi-English code-switched ASR task; small real code-switched corpus (low-resource, on the order of tens of hours) augmented with TTS-synthesized code-switched utterances drawn from code-switched text. Exact hours not authoritatively reported (fetched estimate ~20h real).
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Build/obtain a code-switched (Hindi-English) TTS system and synthesize code-switched utterances from code-switched text to create augmentation audio. 2) Train the transformer-based code-switched ASR on real + synthetic data. 3) Apply Mixup: create new training samples via linear interpolation of TTS and real speech samples (and their targets) to bridge the synthetic-real gap. 4) Apply a new loss function that emphasizes code-switched / rare utterances to better exploit the synthetic data. 5) Evaluate WER and a code-switching-specific metric on in-domain and out-of-domain code-switched test sets. Exact hyperparameters not reported in abstract.
- **Key results:** Up to ~5% absolute WER reduction on the Hindi-English code-switched task and measurable improvement in code-switching ability using the proposed Mixup + new-loss techniques over baselines that use synthetic data naively. (Fetched-PDF approximate figures: baseline ~25-30% WER down to ~18-22%; treat as indicative, not exact.)
- **Notes:** Focus is methods to USE synthetic code-switched TTS audio effectively, not building the TTS. No official code repo found. The 5% absolute WER figure is the abstract's headline; finer numbers in the fetched PDF summary are approximate.

### 127. LRSpeech: Extremely Low-Resource Speech Synthesis and Recognition

_Jin Xu, Xu Tan, Yi Ren, Tao Qin, Jian Li, Sheng Zhao, Tie-Yan Liu · 2020 · KDD 2020_

- **Categories:** C2, C5, C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2008.03687) · arXiv:2008.03687
- **Synthetic-data role:** Synthetic data is central via Dual Transformation (DT): the TTS model synthesizes speech from unpaired text to create pseudo-paired data that trains ASR, and the ASR model transcribes unpaired speech to create pseudo-paired data that trains TTS. These two models bootstrap each other iteratively. Additionally, knowledge distillation generates large synthetic (text, speech) corpora: a target-speaker TTS teacher generates audio to customize TTS, and a multi-speaker setting distills ASR over many synthesized voices.
- **Method:** A three-stage pipeline to build TTS and ASR for extremely low-resource languages: (1) pre-train both on rich-resource languages, (2) fine-tune with very little paired data plus large unpaired speech and text via Dual Transformation (ASR<->TTS mutual data generation), and (3) knowledge distillation to refine the customized TTS for a target speaker and to make ASR robust across speakers, using synthetic data.
- **Architecture:** Transformer-based TTS (Transformer TTS / FastSpeech-lineage acoustic model) plus Transformer-based ASR; mel-spectrogram acoustic features with a neural vocoder for waveform; multi-speaker conditioning for the distillation stage.
- **Base models:** Initialized by pre-training on rich-resource language data (e.g. English) before transferring to the low-resource target; builds on the dual-learning / Transformer TTS and Transformer ASR families from the same group.
- **Datasets:** Rich-resource: English (for pretraining/validation). Target low-resource: Lithuanian. Uses only a few hundred paired sentences from a single speaker plus unpaired speech and unpaired text in the target language; synthetic pseudo-paired data generated through DT and distillation.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** Stage 1 Pre-training: train TTS and ASR on a rich-resource language to learn general speech-text alignment. Stage 2 low-resource fine-tuning with Dual Transformation: starting from very limited paired data (single speaker), alternately (a) synthesize speech from unpaired target text with current TTS to train ASR and (b) transcribe unpaired target speech with current ASR to train TTS, iterating so accuracy compounds. Stage 3 Knowledge Distillation: use the customized TTS as a teacher to generate a large synthetic speech corpus to further train TTS toward the target speaker, and generate multi-speaker synthetic data to make ASR robust to many voices. Targets: >98% TTS intelligibility, >3.5 MOS, with only a few hours / few hundred paired sentences.
- **Key results:** TTS reaches >98% intelligibility and MOS >3.5; ASR achieves promising recognition accuracy on Lithuanian using only a tiny paired set plus unpaired data; quality stated to meet industrial deployment, and the method was deployed in a commercialized cloud speech service.
- **Notes:** Industry (Microsoft) paper; data-cost framing for 6000+ languages. Heavy reliance on synthetic pseudo-pairs makes it a strong example of self-training plus distillation for low-resource TTS/ASR. No public code released.

### 128. Semi-supervised Learning for Multi-speaker Text-to-speech Synthesis Using Discrete Speech Representation

_Tao Tu, Yuan-Jui Chen, Alexander H. Liu, Hung-yi Lee · 2020 · Interspeech 2020_

- **Categories:** C5, C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2005.08024) · arXiv:2005.08024 · [code](https://github.com/ttaoREtw/semi-tts)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Leverages large amounts of UNPAIRED untranscribed REAL speech (semi-supervised), not generated audio. A discrete (quantized) speech representation acts as a pseudo-phoneme/pseudo-text bridge: the model self-supervises on unpaired speech by reconstructing it through its discrete code, and only ~1 hour of paired text-speech grounds the text-to-code link. The synthetic element is model-derived discrete pseudo-labels, not synthesized waveforms.
- **Method:** Build a multi-speaker TTS that learns mostly from untranscribed audio via a Sequential Representation Quantization AutoEncoder (SeqRQ-AE) mapping speech to a discrete token sequence aligned to the phoneme space; paired data ties text to these discrete tokens while abundant unpaired speech trains the speech-to-token and token-to-speech paths.
- **Architecture:** Encoder-decoder with discrete speech representation (SeqRQ-AE): speech encoder -> vector-quantization codebook bottleneck producing a discrete phoneme-like sequence -> decoder reconstructing speech, conditioned on a speaker embedding for multi-speaker control. Text encoder maps phonemes to the same discrete space. Tacotron-style attention seq2seq backbone with speaker conditioning.
- **Base models:** Trained essentially from scratch; relies on a learned VQ codebook (SeqRQ-AE) and speaker embedding rather than a pretrained TTS teacher or external codec.
- **Datasets:** Real: LibriSpeech (multi-speaker) with ~1 hour paired transcribed speech plus the remainder as unpaired speech; experiments with paired data from single vs multiple speakers. No synthetic corpora.
- **Code:** https://github.com/ttaoREtw/semi-tts
- **Recipe:** 1) Pretrain SeqRQ-AE on unpaired speech: speech encoder + quantization to a discrete codebook + decoder reconstruction (self-supervised), encouraging the discrete sequence to behave like a phoneme sequence. 2) Use ~1h paired text-speech to supervise the mapping between phoneme/text tokens and learned discrete codes (alignment to phoneme space). 3) Jointly train so unpaired speech improves the discrete representation and decoder while paired data grounds text->code. 4) Condition decoder on speaker embedding for multi-speaker synthesis. Key finding: only 1h paired data (single- or multi-speaker) yields intelligible speech in multiple voices, robust even when unpaired speech is noisy.
- **Key results:** With only ~1 hour paired data the model generates intelligible multi-speaker speech; intelligibility (ASR-based accuracy) and naturalness improve over low-resource supervised baselines, and quality holds when paired data is single-speaker or when unpaired data is noisy.
- **Notes:** Code available (ttaoREtw/semi-tts). Strong example of discrete-representation pseudo-labeling for low-resource multi-speaker TTS.

### 129. Synth2Aug: Cross-domain speaker recognition with TTS synthesized speech

_Yiling Huang, Yutian Chen, Jason Pelecanos, Quan Wang · 2020 · IEEE SLT 2021_

- **Categories:** C4, C5, C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2011.11818) · arXiv:2011.11818
- **Synthetic-data role:** Fully synthetic SPEECH is generated by a multi-speaker TTS and added as extra training data for a downstream speaker-recognition (verification) model. The TTS produces utterances for many speakers from chosen transcripts to augment a small real-speaker training set. The paper studies how much synthetic data to add and which transcripts to synthesize (target-domain-matched text best; otherwise large-vocabulary transcripts).
- **Method:** Use a multi-speaker TTS to synthesize additional training utterances to improve a speaker-recognition model when few real training speakers are available, showing the synthetic data helps cross-domain generalization, especially combined with multi-style (real acoustic) augmentation.
- **Architecture:** Two-system pipeline: (1) multi-speaker TTS (Tacotron-style multi-speaker acoustic model + vocoder) as speech generator; (2) text-independent speaker-recognition embedding network (Google-style d-vector LSTM speaker encoder) trained on the augmented data. Combined with multi-style training (noise/room augmentation).
- **Base models:** Builds on a pretrained multi-speaker TTS as generator and a standard text-independent speaker-verification embedding network as consumer; specific backbones beyond 'multi-speaker TTS' and d-vector not fully named in abstract.
- **Datasets:** Real speaker-recognition training/eval corpora in a low-resource setting (baseline ~50k real utterances) plus cross-domain eval sets; synthetic set = TTS-generated utterances across many speakers and transcripts (amount swept). Exact corpus names not specified in abstract.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Train/obtain a multi-speaker TTS. 2) Choose transcripts to synthesize: prefer text matching the target evaluation domain; else a transcript set with large/diverse vocabulary. 3) Generate synthetic utterances across many speakers; sweep the AMOUNT of synthetic data added relative to real (too much hurts). 4) Train the speaker-recognition embedding model on real + synthetic, combined with multi-style training (acoustic augmentation). 5) Evaluate cross-domain EER/AUC vs real-only baseline. Guidance: text-content match > vocabulary diversity; tune synthetic:real ratio.
- **Key results:** In a low-resource setting (~50k real utterances baseline), adding an optimal amount of TTS-synthesized speech improved EER by ~30.1% and AUC by ~46.7% relative; synthetic data is complementary to multi-style training and improves cross-domain speaker recognition.
- **Notes:** Downstream task is speaker recognition (not TTS itself), but a clear case of TTS-generated speech used as a synthetic training corpus. Relevant to synthetic-speech-dataset and synthetic-speaker-generation categories.

### 130. TTS-by-TTS: TTS-driven Data Augmentation for Fast and High-Quality Speech Synthesis

_Min-Jae Hwang, Ryuichi Yamamoto, Eunwoo Song, Jae-Min Kim · 2020 · ICASSP 2021_

- **Categories:** C1, C5, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2010.13421) · arXiv:2010.13421 · [code](https://r9y9.github.io/projects/tts-by-tts/)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Core method. A well-designed autoregressive (AR) teacher TTS generates a large-scale synthetic corpus of text-waveform pairs WITH phoneme durations; this synthetic data trains the target non-AR (FastSpeech 2) student. The 5h real training database is augmented to 179h synthetic data, directly supplying the durations and targets the non-AR model needs.
- **Method:** TTS-driven data augmentation: use a high-quality AR teacher TTS to synthesize large amounts of text-waveform-duration triples, then train a fast non-autoregressive student (FastSpeech 2) on this augmented corpus to overcome the quality degradation of non-AR models under limited real data.
- **Architecture:** AR teacher: Tacotron-style autoregressive TTS (provides spectrograms and phoneme durations). Student acoustic model: FastSpeech 2 (non-autoregressive transformer with duration predictor). Vocoder: Parallel WaveGAN (GAN-based neural vocoder).
- **Base models:** AR Tacotron-style teacher TTS used to generate the synthetic corpus and durations; FastSpeech 2 student trained from the augmented data; Parallel WaveGAN vocoder.
- **Datasets:** 5 hours of real training speech, augmented by the AR teacher to 179 hours of synthetic text-waveform-duration data. Specific corpus identity not detailed in abstract.
- **Code:** Project/demo pages: https://r9y9.github.io/projects/tts-by-tts/ and https://min-jae.github.io/icassp2021/ (audio samples; no official training-code repo stated)
- **Recipe:** 1) Train a high-quality AR teacher TTS on the limited (5h) real data. 2) Use the AR teacher to synthesize a large corpus (179h) of text-waveform pairs, extracting phoneme durations from the teacher's alignment. 3) Train the non-AR FastSpeech 2 acoustic model on this synthetic corpus (durations as supervision). 4) Train/apply a Parallel WaveGAN vocoder for waveform generation. Evaluation via perceptual listening test (MOS).
- **Key results:** FastSpeech 2 + Parallel WaveGAN trained with the augmentation reached MOS 3.74, about 40% higher than the conventional (non-augmented) method, significantly improving non-AR TTS quality under low-data conditions.
- **Notes:** Early (2020/ICASSP 2021) foundational work on teacher-to-student synthetic augmentation for non-AR TTS; predates LLM-codec TTS. Authors from LINE/NAVER (Yamamoto = Parallel WaveGAN/r9y9). Confirmed via arXiv abs, project pages, IEEE Xplore, Semantic Scholar.

### 131. Almost Unsupervised Text to Speech and Automatic Speech Recognition

_Yi Ren, Xu Tan, Tao Qin, Sheng Zhao, Zhou Zhao, Tie-Yan Liu · 2019 · ICML 2019_

- **Categories:** C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/1905.06791) · arXiv:1905.06791
- **Synthetic-data role:** Dual transformation generates synthetic paired data from unpaired data: TTS converts unpaired text to speech to make (synthetic speech, text) pairs that train ASR, and ASR converts unpaired speech to text to make (speech, pseudo-text) pairs that train TTS. This iterative back-translation-style pseudo-pairing is the core source of supervision beyond the ~200 real paired samples (~20 minutes). Denoising auto-encoding additionally reconstructs corrupted speech/text from the unpaired side.
- **Method:** Trains TTS and ASR jointly with very little paired data (a few hundred pairs) plus large unpaired speech and text. Four ingredients: (1) denoising auto-encoder to build language/feature modeling in each domain from unpaired data; (2) dual transformation (TTS<->ASR) to iteratively generate and consume pseudo-paired data; (3) bidirectional sequence modeling to combat error propagation in long sequences under low-resource conditions; (4) a single unified transformer that shares modules across both tasks.
- **Architecture:** Single shared Transformer encoder-decoder serving both TTS and ASR. Speech side uses mel-spectrogram features (vocoder for waveform); text/phoneme side uses standard token embeddings. Denoising auto-encoder and dual-transformation losses on top of the shared transformer; bidirectional (left-to-right and right-to-left) decoding to mitigate error propagation.
- **Base models:** Trained largely from scratch (no large pretrained LM/codec); relies only on the unified transformer plus a vocoder. Not reported as initializing from an external teacher.
- **Datasets:** LJSpeech (single-speaker English). Uses ~200 paired samples (~20 minutes of audio) as the labeled set, with the remaining LJSpeech speech and text treated as unpaired data.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Convert text to phonemes and speech to mel-spectrograms. 2) Pretrain with denoising auto-encoder on unpaired speech and unpaired text (corrupt then reconstruct) to learn in-domain sequence structure. 3) Apply dual transformation: TTS(text)->speech then ASR reconstructs text; ASR(speech)->text then TTS reconstructs speech, alternating so each model trains on the other's generated pairs. 4) Use bidirectional sequence modeling (both decoding directions) to reduce error accumulation in long mel/phoneme sequences. 5) Mix in the ~200 real paired samples for supervised anchoring. Single unified transformer shares parameters across tasks. Vocoder synthesizes waveforms from predicted mel-spectrograms.
- **Key results:** TTS: 99.84% intelligibility rate and 2.68 MOS. ASR: 11.7% phoneme error rate (PER). Achieved using only ~200 paired samples (~20 min) plus unpaired data on LJSpeech, substantially better than supervised low-resource baselines.
- **Notes:** Influential ICML 2019 work establishing denoising + dual-transformation as a recipe for near-unsupervised joint TTS/ASR; canonical reference for self-training/pseudo-labeling in TTS. No official code located.

### 132. Semi-supervised Sequence-to-sequence ASR using Unpaired Speech and Text

_Murali Karthick Baskar, Shinji Watanabe, Ramon Astudillo, Takaaki Hori, Lukas Burget, Jan Cernocky · 2019 · INTERSPEECH 2019_

- **Categories:** C5, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/1905.01152) · arXiv:1905.01152
- **Synthetic-data role:** Synthetic speech is generated on-the-fly by an end-to-end TTS from text, and pseudo-transcriptions are generated by the ASR from unpaired/unlabeled speech. These generated intermediates act as supervision inside two cycle-consistency losses (ASR->TTS and TTS->ASR), so neither modality needs paired labels. The synthetic data is not stored as a corpus; it is produced within each differentiable training cycle from unpaired WSJ/LibriSpeech speech and text.
- **Method:** A cycle-consistency / dual-loss framework that closes the loop between ASR and TTS to learn from unpaired speech and text. Unpaired speech is run speech->ASR(text)->TTS(speech) to reconstruct the speech (TTS->ASR loss path), and unpaired text is run text->TTS(speech)->ASR(text) to reconstruct the text, giving an end-to-end differentiable ASR<->TTS reconstruction objective that backpropagates through the generated intermediate.
- **Architecture:** Attention-based encoder-decoder (sequence-to-sequence) ASR; end-to-end attention TTS (Tacotron-style acoustic model) used as the reconstruction/generation module. The ASR->TTS path is made differentiable so gradients flow through generated text representations (expected/embedding rather than hard tokens).
- **Base models:** Built on encoder-decoder ASR (ESPnet-style hybrid CTC/attention lineage) and an end-to-end TTS module; initialized from a small amount of paired supervised data, then improved with unpaired data. No pretrained external LM emphasized (that is added in the follow-up EAT paper).
- **Datasets:** Wall Street Journal (WSJ) and LibriSpeech as the real benchmarks; paired subsets used for supervised init and the remaining speech/text treated as unpaired. No external synthetic corpus; synthetic audio/text generated during training.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Train baseline seq2seq ASR and end-to-end TTS on the limited paired subset. 2) Define two reconstruction losses: TTS->ASR (feed unpaired speech to ASR to get text, synthesize speech with TTS, reconstruct against the original speech) and ASR->TTS (feed unpaired text to TTS to get speech, recognize with ASR, reconstruct the text). 3) Make the ASR->TTS direction differentiable by passing expected/soft text embeddings to TTS so gradients flow end-to-end. 4) Jointly optimize supervised paired loss plus the unpaired cycle losses; sweep loss weights. 5) Add increasing amounts of unpaired speech and text and confirm monotonic WER gains. Evaluate WER on WSJ and LibriSpeech.
- **Key results:** Reduces WER versus prior semi-supervised seq2seq baselines on WSJ and LibriSpeech, with gains scaling as more unpaired speech and text are added; outperforms comparable cycle/back-translation style semi-supervised methods (exact WER figures reported in the paper tables).
- **Notes:** Direct precursor to EAT (arXiv:2104.07474) by overlapping authors. Key replication challenge is the differentiable ASR->TTS coupling (passing soft text distributions to TTS). Synthetic data is ephemeral/in-loop, not a released corpus.

### 133. SpecAugment: A Simple Data Augmentation Method for Automatic Speech Recognition

_Daniel S. Park, William Chan, Yu Zhang, Chung-Cheng Chiu, Barret Zoph, Ekin D. Cubuk, Quoc V. Le · 2019 · Interspeech 2019_

- **Categories:** C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/1904.08779) · arXiv:1904.08779
- **Synthetic-data role:** Augmentation, not synthetic speech generation. New training examples are produced on-the-fly by directly perturbing the input log-mel spectrogram of REAL utterances (no model generates audio/text). Three transforms create the variants: time warping, frequency masking (mask blocks of mel channels), and time masking (mask blocks of time steps). Applied to every training utterance each epoch.
- **Method:** Apply cheap label-preserving deformations directly to the filter-bank/spectrogram features fed to an ASR model, converting over-fitting into under-fitting so larger models can train longer. Feature-space augmentation requiring no extra data and no audio resynthesis.
- **Architecture:** Augmentation method, model-agnostic. Demonstrated on Listen-Attend-Spell (LAS) attention seq2seq ASR: bidirectional/pyramidal LSTM listener encoder + attention decoder, variants LAS-4-1024 to LAS-6-1280 (6 encoder layers, 1280 cell dim). Optional 2-layer RNN LM for shallow fusion.
- **Base models:** Not a TTS model; builds on standard LAS ASR encoder-decoder. No teacher/pretrained generator; augmentation only.
- **Datasets:** Real only: LibriSpeech 960h (test-clean/test-other), Switchboard 300h (Hub5'00 SWB/CallHome eval). No synthetic corpora.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Compute log-mel spectrogram (e.g. 80 mel channels). 2) Per utterance apply: time warping (warp a time-axis point by W via sparse_image_warp, W=80 for LibriSpeech), frequency masking (mF masks each width f~U(0,F); LibriSpeech F=27, mF up to 2), time masking (mT masks each width t~U(0,T), T optionally bounded by p*utterance-length with p=1.0; LibriSpeech mT up to 2 with T=100). Predefined policies LB/LD (LibriSpeech basic/double), SM/SS (Switchboard). 3) Train LAS with augmentation always on and a much longer LR schedule (train far past normal convergence since augmentation prevents overfitting). 4) Optional RNN-LM shallow fusion at decode.
- **Key results:** LibriSpeech: 2.8% WER test-clean / 6.8% test-other without LM; 2.5%/5.8% with LM (SOTA at time vs prior ~3.2%/7.5% hybrid). Switchboard: 7.2%/14.6% (SWB/CH) without LM; 6.8%/14.1% with LM.
- **Notes:** Foundational augmentation baseline. Relevant to a TTS-synthetic-data survey only as the canonical feature-space augmentation contrast point (no generated speech). Open reimplementations exist.

### 134. Speech Recognition with Augmented Synthesized Speech

_Andrew Rosenberg, Yu Zhang, Bhuvana Ramabhadran, Ye Jia, Pedro Moreno, Yonghui Wu, Zelin Wu · 2019 · ASRU 2019_

- **Categories:** C5, C4, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/1909.11699) · arXiv:1909.11699
- **Synthetic-data role:** Synthetic SPEECH (not text) is generated by a multi-speaker Tacotron TTS and added to the ASR training set to augment/replace human audio. The study manipulates TTS latent embeddings (prosody, speaker, style from acoustic references) to inject acoustic and lexical variety into the synthetic data, then measures how much synthetic augmentation helps ASR, especially for domain transfer. Quantifies the residual human-vs-synthetic gap.
- **Method:** Use a controllable multi-speaker Tacotron to synthesize large amounts of diverse training audio for ASR, deliberately increasing acoustic variety (sampling speaker/prosody/style latents) and lexical variety (varied transcripts), and study whether this synthetic augmentation improves recognition across two domains. Finds gains for domain transfer but a persistent human-vs-synthetic gap.
- **Architecture:** Tacotron multi-speaker TTS (encoder-attention-decoder mel model) with manipulable latent embeddings for prosody/speaker/style (GST-like reference encoding) + vocoder, used as the data generator; a separate end-to-end ASR model consumes the augmented data.
- **Base models:** Multi-speaker Tacotron TTS as synthesizer; end-to-end ASR system as the downstream consumer. Specific ASR backbone not detailed in abstract.
- **Datasets:** Two corpora from different domains (names not disclosed in abstract); human speech vs Tacotron-synthesized speech compared. Scale not reported in abstract.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Train/obtain a multi-speaker controllable Tacotron with latent prosody/speaker/style embeddings. 2) Generate synthetic training audio: sample/vary the latent embeddings to maximize ACOUSTIC variety and use varied transcripts to maximize LEXICAL variety, producing many speaker/style variants per utterance. 3) Augment the ASR training set with this synthetic speech (study synthetic-only vs mixed). 4) Train end-to-end ASR; evaluate WER on in-domain and out-of-domain (domain-transfer) test sets. 5) Compare against ASR trained only on human speech to measure the human-vs-synthetic gap. Specific hyperparameters not in abstract.
- **Key results:** Augmenting ASR training with synthesized speech improves recognition, with clearest benefit for domain transfer; however a substantial WER gap remains between recognizers trained on human vs synthesized speech. Exact WER numbers not in fetched abstract.
- **Notes:** Google authors. Important early study quantifying the human-vs-synthetic speech gap for ASR and the value of acoustic+lexical diversity in synthetic data. Relevant to categories 5 (augmentation), 4 (synthetic-speech datasets), 7 (synthetically generated corpora).

### 135. Teacher-Student Training for Robust Tacotron-based TTS

_Rui Liu, Berrak Sisman, Jingdong Li, Feilong Bao, Guanglai Gao, Haizhou Li · 2019 · ICASSP 2020_

- **Categories:** C2, C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/1911.02839) · arXiv:1911.02839
- **Synthetic-data role:** Self-generated/predicted frames as training signal: the student Tacotron2 is trained with its own predicted (synthetic) mel frames fed back as decoder input (free-running) instead of natural frames, to match inference-time conditions. The teacher (trained with natural frames) supplies a distillation target so the student's predicted-frame trajectory stays close to the teacher's, mitigating exposure bias. The 'synthetic' data here is the model's own autoregressive predictions, not an external corpus.
- **Method:** Reduces exposure bias in autoregressive Tacotron2 TTS via teacher-student training: a teacher decodes from ground-truth frames while a student decodes from its own predicted frames, with a distillation loss aligning the student's output probabilities to the teacher's on top of the standard feature (reconstruction) loss, improving robustness on out-of-domain text.
- **Architecture:** Two Tacotron2-based acoustic models (attention-based seq2seq: encoder + location-sensitive attention + autoregressive decoder predicting mel-spectrograms), plus a neural vocoder for waveform. Teacher and student share the Tacotron2 architecture; difference is the decoder input regime (natural vs. predicted frames).
- **Base models:** Tacotron2 (teacher and student both Tacotron2-based). Vocoder not specified in abstract.
- **Datasets:** Chinese and English TTS systems; specific corpus names and hours not reported in the abstract.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Train a teacher Tacotron2 conventionally with teacher forcing (natural mel frames as decoder input). 2) Train a student Tacotron2 in free-running mode where its own predicted frames are fed back as decoder input (matching inference). 3) Add a distillation loss that makes the student's output distribution match the teacher's output probabilities, combined with the standard feature/reconstruction (mel L1/L2) loss. 4) Optimize the student jointly under feature loss + distillation loss to reduce train/inference mismatch (exposure bias). 5) Evaluate on out-of-domain test text in both Chinese and English. Exact loss weights, learning rates, and corpora are in the full paper (not in abstract).
- **Key results:** Consistent voice-quality improvement on out-of-domain test data for both Chinese and English systems; specific WER/MOS numbers not given in the abstract.
- **Notes:** Accepted to ICASSP 2020 (Barcelona). Verified via arXiv. No official code located. Core relevance is self-training/exposure-bias mitigation via the model's own predicted (synthetic) frames plus knowledge distillation.

### 136. Cycle-consistency training for end-to-end speech recognition

_Takaaki Hori, Ramon Astudillo, Tomoki Hayashi, Yu Zhang, Shinji Watanabe, Jonathan Le Roux (MERL, INESC-ID, Nagoya Univ., Google, JHU) · 2018 · ICASSP 2019 (arXiv Nov 2018)_

- **Categories:** C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/1811.01690) · arXiv:1811.01690
- **Synthetic-data role:** Uses UNPAIRED AUDIO (no transcripts) for ASR training via a cycle: text is produced by ASR, then a Text-To-Encoder (TTS-like) model reconstructs the speech ENCODER STATE sequence, and the cycle-consistency loss is the encoder-state reconstruction error. Rather than synthesizing raw waveforms, the 'synthetic' target is the reconstructed encoder-state representation, which preserves information (e.g., speaker traits) lost through the text bottleneck. 360 h of untranscribed audio is exploited this way on top of 100 h paired.
- **Method:** Enables training end-to-end ASR with unpaired data by composing ASR with a reverse text-to-encoder model to form a cycle-consistency loss. Key idea: define the loss on the speech ENCODER STATE sequence (encoder reconstruction error) instead of on the raw speech signal, so the cycle does not require modeling speaker/style detail lost in the text bottleneck, making cycle-consistency usable for ASR improvement from unlabeled audio.
- **Architecture:** Attention-based encoder-decoder end-to-end ASR (ESPnet-style sequence-to-sequence). A 'Text-To-Encoder' (TTE) model maps text back to the ASR encoder-state sequence (a TTS-like reverse module operating in encoder-state space rather than waveform/spectrogram). Cycle-consistency loss = encoder-state reconstruction error. Exact layer sizes not reported in fetched material.
- **Base models:** Initial end-to-end ASR trained on 100 h paired LibriSpeech; a Text-To-Encoder model for the reverse direction. No external pretrained LM/codec required.
- **Datasets:** LibriSpeech: 100 h paired (speech+transcripts) as the initial model; additional 360 h of audio WITHOUT transcriptions for cycle-consistency training; text-only data also explored for language modeling.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Train attention-based seq2seq ASR on 100 h paired LibriSpeech. 2) Train a Text-To-Encoder (TTE) model that reconstructs the ASR encoder-state sequence from text. 3) Cycle training on 360 h untranscribed audio: pass audio through ASR encoder to get encoder states, decode text, feed text to TTE to reconstruct encoder states, minimize encoder-state reconstruction (cycle-consistency) error so ASR learns from unlabeled audio. Optionally use text-only data for the language model. Exact hyperparameters not reported in fetched material.
- **Key results:** Cycle-consistency training reduced WER by 14.7% relative from the initial 100 h-paired model by adding 360 h of untranscribed audio (LibriSpeech).
- **Notes:** Foundational cycle-consistency-for-ASR work that later TTS+ASR joint-training papers (e.g., Makishima 2022) build on. 'Synthetic' here is reconstructed encoder states, not waveforms. Specific architecture sizes/hyperparameters not in the fetched abstract.

### 137. Machine Speech Chain with One-shot Speaker Adaptation

_Andros Tjandra, Sakriani Sakti, Satoshi Nakamura · 2018 · Interspeech 2018_

- **Categories:** C5, C6
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/1803.10525) · arXiv:1803.10525
- **Synthetic-data role:** Within a closed-loop ASR<->TTS speech chain, the TTS module synthesizes speech from unlabeled text and the ASR module transcribes unlabeled speech; each component's generated output becomes pseudo-paired training data for the other. Crucially, the synthetic speech is conditioned on a one-shot speaker embedding so that ASR can learn to recognize arbitrary/unseen speakers from TTS-generated waveforms. Synthetic data here is the speech (and text) produced inside the loop from unpaired data; quantity is the unpaired portion of the corpus rather than a fixed external set.
- **Method:** Extends the machine speech chain (dual ASR/TTS feedback loop, dual learning) by inserting a speaker-recognition/embedding model into the loop and adding one-shot speaker adaptation to TTS. For unpaired text, TTS generates speech and ASR reconstructs text (and vice versa for unpaired speech), with reconstruction losses propagated so the two models teach each other. The speaker embedding lets TTS mimic a target voice from a single sample and lets ASR generalize to unseen speakers.
- **Architecture:** Sequence-to-sequence Tacotron-style attention-based TTS conditioned on a neural speaker embedding (Deep Speaker style speaker recognition model); attention-based encoder-decoder (seq2seq) ASR. Speaker recognition/embedding network produces a fixed-dim speaker vector used to condition TTS. Vocoding/feature reconstruction at the mel/spectral level.
- **Base models:** Builds on the original machine speech chain framework (Tjandra et al. 2017); uses a Tacotron-like seq2seq TTS, a seq2seq attention ASR, and a Deep Speaker-style speaker embedding model. No large pretrained LM or codec.
- **Datasets:** WSJ (Wall Street Journal) multi-speaker corpus is the primary evaluation set, split into a small labeled (paired) portion plus a larger unlabeled (unpaired) portion of speech and text for the chain. (Exact hours not stated in the abstract.)
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Pretrain seq2seq ASR and Tacotron-style TTS on the small labeled subset (supervised). 2) Train/obtain a Deep Speaker-style speaker embedding model; use it to condition TTS for one-shot adaptation (extract embedding from a single reference utterance of a target speaker). 3) Run the speech-chain loop on unpaired data: ASR->TTS path (unlabeled speech: ASR predicts text, TTS resynthesizes speech conditioned on the speaker embedding of the original utterance, minimize speech reconstruction loss) and TTS->ASR path (unlabeled text: TTS generates speech with a sampled/known speaker embedding, ASR transcribes, minimize text reconstruction loss). 4) Alternate supervised paired updates with unsupervised chain updates. Key design choices: speaker embedding conditioning is what enables unseen-speaker ASR gains and one-shot voice mimicking. Hyperparameters (LR, batch size, embedding dim) not detailed in the abstract.
- **Key results:** After enabling the speech-chain loop with speaker adaptation, ASR recognition rate improves significantly over supervised-only baseline and over other semi-supervised techniques; TTS can mimic an unseen speaker's voice from a single one-shot sample. Exact CER/WER and MOS numbers not given in the abstract.
- **Notes:** Foundational machine-speech-chain paper adding speaker identity to the loop; one of the earliest TTS<->ASR mutual-learning works directly relevant to synthetic-speech-for-ASR. Specific metric numbers were not surfaced from the abstract.

### 138. Semi-Supervised Training for Improving Data Efficiency in End-to-End Speech Synthesis

_Yu-An Chung, Yuxuan Wang, Wei-Ning Hsu, Yu Zhang, RJ Skerry-Ryan · 2018 · ICASSP 2019_

- **Categories:** C2, C5
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/1808.10128) · arXiv:1808.10128
- **Synthetic-data role:** No synthetic speech is generated for training. Instead unpaired REAL data is exploited: large unpaired TEXT corpora pretrain word embeddings that condition the encoder, and unpaired untranscribed SPEECH pretrains the decoder as an acoustic/autoregressive LM. Pairing is only needed for a tiny fine-tune set (<0.5h). Semi-supervised pretraining/self-supervision, not pseudo-labeling or synthesized audio.
- **Method:** Make Tacotron data-efficient by decoupling encoder and decoder learning: condition the text encoder on pretrained word vectors from large unpaired text, pretrain the autoregressive decoder on unpaired speech to model acoustics, then fine-tune the full model on a very small paired text-audio set.
- **Architecture:** Tacotron end-to-end attention seq2seq TTS: CBHG encoder over (word-conditioned) inputs + attention + autoregressive decoder predicting mel/linear spectrogram frames + Griffin-Lim/vocoder reconstruction. Encoder conditioned on pretrained word embeddings.
- **Base models:** Tacotron architecture; initialized from pretrained word embeddings (large external text) and a decoder pretrained on unpaired speech. No teacher TTS, no neural codec.
- **Datasets:** Real: single-speaker TTS corpus for paired fine-tuning (<30 min paired used). Unpaired text from large public corpora (word vectors); unpaired/untranscribed speech for decoder pretraining. Exact hours beyond '<30 min paired' not enumerated in abstract.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** Stage 1: train word embeddings on large unpaired text; condition the Tacotron encoder on them. Stage 2: pretrain the Tacotron decoder on unpaired speech as a conditional acoustic LM (generate spectrogram frames without text alignment). Stage 3: fine-tune the whole encoder-decoder with attention on the small paired set. Evaluate intelligibility as paired-data size shrinks. Key claim: intelligible speech with less than ~30 minutes paired data.
- **Key results:** Produces intelligible speech with <30 min paired data where a baseline Tacotron on the same small set fails; improvements via subjective/intelligibility evaluation. Exact MOS/WER not given in abstract.
- **Notes:** Early data-efficiency work predating neural-codec LM TTS. Relevant as a self-/semi-supervised pretraining baseline rather than synthetic-speech augmentation.

### 139. Training Neural Speech Recognition Systems with Synthetic Speech Augmentation

_Jason Li, Ravi Gadde, Boris Ginsburg, Vitaly Lavrukhin · 2018 · arXiv preprint (NVIDIA / OpenSeq2Seq)_

- **Categories:** C5, C4, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/1811.00707) · arXiv:1811.00707 · [code](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenSeq2Seq)
- **Synthetic-data role:** Synthetic SPEECH generated by a Tacotron-2-with-Global-Style-Tokens TTS (trained on MAILABS US-English, ~100h, 3 speakers) augments the natural LibriSpeech ASR training set. GST provide multiple speaker identities so the synthetic audio is not single-voice. Synthetic utterances are mixed with real LibriSpeech to train large end-to-end ASR models.
- **Method:** Address scarce labeled speech by synthesizing extra training audio with a multi-style (GST) Tacotron-2 and mixing it into LibriSpeech to train end-to-end CTC ASR models, achieving SOTA character-level WER without an external language model.
- **Architecture:** Generator: Tacotron-2-like model with Global Style Tokens (T2-GST) for multi-speaker/multi-style mel synthesis + vocoder, from the OpenSeq2Seq toolkit. Consumer ASR: end-to-end OpenSeq2Seq models, namely Wave2Letter+ (fully convolutional, CTC) and Deep Speech 2 (recurrent), character-level output.
- **Base models:** OpenSeq2Seq Tacotron-2 + GST as synthesizer; OpenSeq2Seq Wave2Letter+ and Deep Speech 2 as ASR models. Synthesizer trained on MAILABS; ASR trained on LibriSpeech (+ synthetic).
- **Datasets:** Real: LibriSpeech (~1000h) for ASR; MAILABS English-US (~100h, 3 speakers) to train the T2-GST synthesizer. Synthetic: Tacotron-2-GST-generated speech augmenting LibriSpeech.
- **Code:** https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenSeq2Seq
- **Recipe:** 1) Train T2-GST (Tacotron-2 with Global Style Tokens) on MAILABS US-English (~100h, 3 speakers) to get a multi-speaker/multi-style synthesizer. 2) Synthesize speech for LibriSpeech transcripts, using GST to vary speaker/style for acoustic diversity. 3) Mix synthetic audio with real LibriSpeech and train end-to-end character-level ASR (Wave2Letter+ fully-convolutional CTC and/or Deep Speech 2) in OpenSeq2Seq with mixed-precision training. 4) Decode greedily/CTC WITHOUT an external language model; report WER. 5) Compare LibriSpeech-only vs LibriSpeech+synthetic. Configs available in the OpenSeq2Seq repo.
- **Key results:** Augmenting LibriSpeech with synthetic speech improves WER over LibriSpeech-only training and achieves state-of-the-art WER for character-level models without an external language model. Exact WER values not in fetched abstract (5-page paper, 1 figure).
- **Notes:** NVIDIA; reproducible via open-source OpenSeq2Seq (Apache-2.0). Early demonstration that GST-driven multi-speaker TTS synthetic data benefits CTC ASR. Categories 5/4/7.

### 140. Listening while Speaking: Speech Chain by Deep Learning

_Andros Tjandra, Sakriani Sakti, Satoshi Nakamura · 2017 · IEEE ASRU 2017_

- **Categories:** C5, C7
- **Links:** [paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/1707.04879) · arXiv:1707.04879
- **Synthetic-data role:** Synthetic intermediates drive semi-supervised learning. For unlabeled speech, ASR produces a transcription, then TTS resynthesizes speech from that text and is trained to reconstruct the original speech (ASR supplies pseudo-text to TTS). For unlabeled text, TTS produces speech, then ASR transcribes it back and is trained to reconstruct the original text (TTS supplies synthetic speech to ASR). Both generated signals are used as training targets within the closed loop; no fixed synthetic corpus is released.
- **Method:** The original deep-learning 'machine speech chain': a closed-loop coupling of seq2seq ASR and seq2seq TTS that mimics human auditory feedback, letting the two models teach each other on the concatenation of labeled and unlabeled data so each improves beyond separate supervised training.
- **Architecture:** Sequence-to-sequence attention ASR (encoder-decoder) and a modified Tacotron TTS with speaker embedding; both connected in a closed feedback loop. Speaker embedding lets TTS reconstruct the correct voice during the speech->text->speech path.
- **Base models:** Not reported (trained from scratch); TTS is a modified Tacotron, ASR is a standard attention seq2seq of the era. No external pretrained LM or codec.
- **Datasets:** BTEC ATR-EDB corpus; the US Northeast (single-region) portion of about 22k utterances was used (drawn from ~180k utterances across six regions). Split into a small paired/labeled set plus unpaired speech and text for the chain training.
- **Code:** none found
- **Recipe:** 1) Pre-train ASR and TTS separately on the small labeled (paired) subset. 2) Speech-chain unrolling: (a) speech->ASR->text->TTS->speech, train TTS (and propagate) to reconstruct the original unlabeled speech using the ASR-produced text plus speaker embedding; (b) text->TTS->speech->ASR->text, train ASR to reconstruct the original unlabeled text from TTS-synthesized speech. 3) Alternate/jointly train on the concatenation of labeled and unlabeled data, looping the chain so generated outputs become inputs. 4) Use speaker embedding in TTS to preserve voice identity through the loop. Evaluate ASR (WER/CER) and TTS quality against separately-trained supervised baselines.
- **Key results:** The closed-loop speech chain significantly outperforms separately-trained ASR and TTS systems that use labeled data only (improved ASR error rate and TTS quality on the BTEC ATR-EDB subset); presented as the first deep-learning model unifying the two speech behaviors.
- **Notes:** Foundational paper establishing the machine speech chain that later works (LRSpeech dual transformation, Baskar et al. ASR-TTS cycle, EAT) build on. Single-speaker/single-region subset limits scale. Follow-up (arXiv:1803.10525) adds one-shot speaker adaptation. No public code found.

---

## 7. Methodology & caveats

This review was produced by a 63-agent automated literature-review pipeline run on 2026-06-23:

1. **Search (14 agents)** swept the web and arXiv from distinct angles: training-from-scratch on synthetic speech, fine-tuning/adaptation, DPO/RLHF/GRPO preference optimization, LLM-generated text corpora, self-training/pseudo-labeling/augmentation, synthetic-speaker/accent/style/multilingual, large data-engine TTS systems, surveys/datasets, and 2025-2026 preprints.
2. **Consolidation** deduplicated 392 raw hits by arXiv-id and normalized title into 186 unique papers, ranked by how many independent scouts surfaced each.
3. **Enrichment (35 batched agents)** verified each paper existed via search/fetch and extracted the structured fields shown in the catalog. Only papers confirmed real were kept; all 140 entries here are verified.
4. **Completeness critique (4 agents)** hunted for missing foundational, cutting-edge, subdomain, and method-specific works; their finds were enriched in a gap-fill round.
5. **Synthesis (11 agents)** wrote the per-category sections, introduction, replication guide, and trends section from the verified corpus only.

**Caveats.** (a) Extraction reflects what each source reported; recipe/metric fields can be incomplete where papers omit detail. (b) "Verified" means the paper was confirmed to exist with a working source URL, not that every extracted metric was independently reproduced. (c) Synthesis sections were instructed to reference only papers in the verified corpus, but LLM-written prose can still contain minor attribution slips; cross-check against the catalog and linked sources before citing. (d) Coverage is broad but not exhaustive; the 86 lowest-signal dedup candidates were not enriched.
